ماہیت کا تصور حاصل ہوتا ہے۔

فائدہ:۔ تعریف اسکی کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ تعریف اسمی دو چیزوں کا فائدہ دیتی ہے (۱) مسمی کی مشہور لفظ کے ساتھ وضاحت کر دیتی ہے جیسے الغضفر الاسد یہاں اسد نے غضنفر کی وضاحت کی ہے (۲) مجمل کی تفصیل کر دیتی ہے مثلاً الاصل میں معنی ہے لیکن مجمل ہے جب اس کی تعریف کی گئی یقنی علیہ غیرہ کیسا تھ اس کا اجمال دور ہو کر تفصیل ہو گئی

فتعريفات المعد ومات :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چھٹا حصہ ہے۔ ماقبل میں تعریف حقیقی اور تعریف اسمی میں فرق بیان کیا گیا ہے یہاں سے اس پر تفریع متفرع کی گئی ہے کہ تعریف معدومات کی ہوگی یا موجودات کی ہوگی معدومات کی تعریف ہمیشہ اسمی ہی ہو گی حقیقی نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ معدومات کے حقائق بالکل ہوتے ہی نہیں اور موجودات کی تعریف کبھی امی ہوتی ہے اور کبھی حقیقی۔ کیونکہ موجودات کے لیے حقائق بھی ہوتے ہیں اور مفہومات بھی ۔

فَإِنْ قُلْتَ ظَاهِرُ عِبَارَتِهِ مُشْعِرٌ بِأَنْ تَعْرِيفَ الْمَاهِيَّاتِ الْحَقِيقِيَّةِ حَقِيقِيُّ الْبَيَّةَ كَمَا أَنَّ تَعْرِيفَ الْمَاهِيَّاتِ الاعْتِبَارِيَّةِ اسْمِيٌّ أَلْبَتَّةَ قُلْتُ فِي الْعُدُولِ عَنْ ظَاهِرِ الْعِبَارَةِ سَعَةٌ إِلَّا أَنَّ التَّحْقِيقَ أَنَّ الْمَاهِيَّةَ الْحَقِيقِيَّةَ قَدْ تُؤْخَذُ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهَا حَقِيقَةُ مُسَمَّى الاسْمِ وَمَاهِيَّتِهِ الثَّابِتَةُ فِي نَفْسِ الْأَمْرِ وَتَعْرِيفُهَا بِهَذَا الْاعْتِبَارِ حَقِيقِيٌّ الْبَيَّةَ ؛ لأنَّهُ جَوَابٌ ل "مَا الَّتِي لِطَلَب الْحَقِيقَةِ وَهِيَ مُتَأَخَّرَةٌ عَنْ "هَلْ الْبَسِيطَةِ الطَّالِبَةِ لِوُجُودِ الشَّيْء الْمُتَأَخَّرَةِ عَنْ "مَا الَّتِي لِطَلَبِ تَفْسِيرِ الاسْمِ وَبَيَانِ مَفُهُومِهِ وَقَدْ تُؤْخَذُ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهَا مَفْهُومُ الاسْمِ وَمُتَعَقَّلُ الْوَاضِعِ عِنْدَ وَضْعِ الاسْمِ وَتَعْرِيفُهَا بِهَذَا الاعْتِبَارِ اسْمِيٌّ أَلْبَتَّةَ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ جَوَابٌ عَنْ مَا الَّتِي لِطَلَبِ مَفْهُومٍ الاسْمِ وَمُتَعَقَّلِ الْوَاضِعِ فَهَذَا التَّعْرِيفُ قَدْ يَكُونُ نَفْسَ حَقِيقَةِ ذَلِكَ الشَّيْء بِأَنُ يَكُونَ مُتَعَقَّلُ الْوَاضِعِ نَفْسَ الْحَقِيقَةِ وَقَدْ يَكُونُ غَيْرَهَا وَلِهَذَا صَرَّحُوا بِأَنَّهُ قَدْ يَتَّحِدُ التَّعْرِيفُ الاسْمِيُّ وَالْحَقِيقِيُّ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ قَبْلَ الْعِلْمِ بِوُجُودِ الشَّيْء يَكُونُ اسْمِيًّا وَبَعْدَ الْعِلْمِ بِوُجُودِهِ يَنْقَلِبُ حَقِيقِيًّا مَثَلًا تَعْرِيفُ الْمُتَلَّثِ فِي مَبَادِهِ الْهِنْدَسَةِ بِشَكْلٍ يُحِيطُ بِهِ ثَلاثَةُ أَضْلاعِ تَعْرِيفٌ اسْمِيٌّ وَبَعْدَ الدَّلَالَةِ عَلَى وُجُودِهِ يَصِيرُ هُوَ بِعَيْنِهِ تَعْرِيفًا حَقِيقِيًّا

ترجمہ: پس اگر تو اعتراض کرتا ہے کہ اس (ماتن) کی عبارت کا ظاہر مشعر ہے اس بات کی طرف کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف حقیقی ہوگی یقینی طور پر جیسا کہ ماہیات اعتباریہ کی تعریف تعریف اسمی ہوتی ہے یقینی طور پر تو میں کہتا ہوں کہ ظاہر العبارة سے عدول کرنے میں وسعت ہے مگر بیشک تحقیق یہ ہے کہ بیشک ما بیت حقیقیہ بھی لی جاتی ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ اسم کے مسمی کی حقیقت ہے اور وہ ایسی ماہیت ہے جو ثابت ہے نفس الامر میں اور اس ( ماہیت حقیقیہ ) کی تعریف اس اعتبار سے تعریف حقیقی ہوگی یقینی طور پر اس لئے کہ بیشک وہ جواب ہے اس ماہ کیلئے جو حقیقت کو طلب کرنے کیلئے ہے وہ مؤخر ہوتی ہے ھل بسیطہ سے جو طلب کرنے والا ہے شی متاخرہ کے وجود کیلئے اس ما سے جو اسم کی تفسیر کو طلب کرنے کے لیے اور اس کے مفہوم کو بیان کرنے کے لئے ہے۔ کبھی لیا جاتا ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ بیشک وہ اسم کا مفہوم ہے اور واضع کا تعقل ہے اسم کے وضع کرنے کے وقت اور اس کا تعریف کرنا اس اعتبار سے اسی ہے یقینا اس لیے کہ وہ جواب ہے اس ما کا جو اسم کے مفہوم کو طلب کرنے کیلئے ہے اور واضع کے تعقل کیلئے ہے اور یہ تعریف کبھی ہوتی ہے اس شی کی نفس حقیقت بایں طور کہ ہوگا واضع کا تعقل نفس حقیقت اور کبھی ہوتا ہے اس کے علاوہ سے اسی وجہ سے تصریح کی ہے انہوں نے بائیں طور کہ کبھی متحد ہوتی ہے تعریف اسمی اور تعریف حقیقی مگر بے شک وہ مٹی کے وجود کے علم سے پہلے ہمی ہوتی ہے اور وجود کے علم کے بعد تبدیل ہو جاتی ہے حقیقی سے مثال کے طور پر مثلث کی تعریف مبادی ہندسہ میں ایسی شکل کے ساتھ جس کا احاطہ کریں اضلاع ثلاث تعریف آسی ہے اور دلالت کرنے کے بعد اس کے وجود پر ہو جائے گی وہ ( تعریف آسی ) بعینہ تعریف حقیقی

ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف کبھی اسمی ہوتی ہے اور کبھی حقیقی ہوتی ہے

فان قلت :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض اس عبارت کی ایک اعتراض نقل کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض:- شارخ پر اعتراض یہ ہے کہ آپ کی کلام سے یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ماہیت حقیقیہ کی تعریف کبھی اسمی ہوگی اور کبھی حقیقی لیکن ماتن کی کلام سے یہ ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف ہمیشہ حقیقی ہوگی جیسا کہ ماہیات اعتباریہ کی تعریف ہمیشہ اسکی ہوتی ہے اور وجہ ظہور یہ ہے کہ ماتن نے تعریف حقیقی کو ماہیات حقیقیہ کے مقابلے میں ذکر کیا ہے اور تعریف اسمی کو ماہیات اعتباریہ کے مقابلے میں ذکر کیا ہے اور ماہیات اعتباریہ کی تعریف صرف امی ہی ہوتی ہے لھذا اس تقابل سے معلوم
If you say: The apparent meaning of his (the matn author's) expression suggests that the definition of real essences is definitely haqiqi, just as the definition of conceptual essences is definitely ismi. I say: There is scope in departing from the apparent meaning, but the verification is that the real essence can be taken from the perspective that it is the reality of the named thing and its essence established in the external world, and its definition from this perspective is definitely haqiqi because it is an answer to 'ma' which seeks the reality, and it is subsequent to the simple 'hal' which seeks the existence of the thing, which is subsequent to 'ma' that seeks the interpretation of the name and the clarification of its concept. And it can be taken from the perspective that it is the concept of the name and the conceptualization of the coiner at the time of naming, and its definition from this perspective is definitely ismi because it is an answer to 'ma' that seeks the concept of the name and the conceptualization of the coiner. So this definition may be the very reality of that thing if the conceptualization of the coiner is the reality itself, or it may be other than it. For this reason, they explicitly stated that the ismi and haqiqi definitions may coincide, except that before knowledge of the thing's existence it is ismi, and after knowledge of its existence it becomes haqiqi. For example, the definition of a triangle in the principles of geometry as a shape enclosed by three sides is an ismi definition, and after proof of its existence, that same definition becomes a haqiqi definition.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the classification of definitions (ta'rif) into haqiqi (real) and ismi (nominal), specifically applied to mahiyat (essences). The author first presents a benefit (fa'ida) of ismi definitions: they clarify a known name with a more famous synonym (e.g., 'al-asad' for 'al-ghadanfar') or detail a summary (e.g., defining an ambiguous term). Then he differentiates between definitions of non-existent things (ma'dumat) which are always ismi, and existent things (mawjudat) which can be ismi or haqiqi. The core of the passage addresses an objection: the matn's wording seems to assert that real essences always have haqiqi definitions and conceptual essences always ismi. The commentator refines this, showing that a real essence can be considered in two ways: as an extramental reality (then its definition is haqiqi) or as a mental concept (then its definition is ismi). These two definitions may coincide when the concept matches the reality. Before knowing the existence of the thing, the definition is ismi; after confirming existence, the same definition becomes haqiqi. The example of a triangle illustrates this. The passage ends with a new objection (fa-in qulta) questioning why the commentator departs from the matn's apparent meaning, but the text cuts off. This analysis follows the Hanafi usul tradition of precise conceptual distinction.

Key Terms
تعريف حقيقي (ta'rif haqiqi): A definition that reveals the extramental reality (haqiqah) of a thing, answering the question 'ma' (what is it) seeking the true essence.
تعريف اسمي (ta'rif ismi): A definition that clarifies the conceptual meaning (mafhum) and the understanding of the coiner (wadi') of the name, regardless of the thing's external existence.
ماهية حقيقية (mahiyah haqiqiyyah): A real essence that has an existence in the external world (fi nafs al-amr).
ماهية اعتبارية (mahiyah i'tibariyyah): A conceptual essence that exists only in the mind (i'tibar), not externally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition causes an ismi definition to become haqiqi?
A) When the definition matches the coiner's concept
B) When the existence of the thing is proven
C) When the definition is detailed
D) When the thing is conceptual

Key Takeaway
A definition's classification as haqiqi or ismi is not fixed; it depends on the perspective and epistemic context, with the existence of the defined thing being the key transformative factor.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
Two Answers on Definitions of Real Essences
Responds to objection that real essences only have real definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why real essences can have both real and nominal definitions, and identify the two answers given by the commentator.

Core Idea
Real essences have two aspects: essence itself (real definition) and concept of a name (nominal definition).

In usul al-fiqh, definitions play a crucial role in clarifying legal terms. A common claim is that real essences can only be defined by real definitions—definitions that state the quiddity itself. However, the commentator in this passage argues that this claim is incomplete. Through two answers, he shows that real essences can also be defined nominally when considered from the aspect of their conceptual meaning. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying definitions in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and the matn's claim
The matn states that definitions of real essences are only real. Understand why this appears problematic for the commentator—it seems to exclude nominal definitions entirely.
The objection is not from another school but from within the commentary tradition; the matn's literal wording is being challenged.
2
Analyze the first answer: ta'wil
The commentator offers three interpretations to reconcile the matn with the truth: (a) restricting the definition to the aspect of being a real essence, (b) stating that real definitions occur in most cases, or (c) treating the matn's statement as an example rather than a rule.
Ta'wil is a standard Hanafi tool to harmonize texts with established principles.
3
Analyze the second answer: direct correction
If the matn is taken literally, it contradicts the truth. The truth is that real essences have two aspects: as essence (leading to real definition) and as concept of a name (leading to nominal definition).
This answer acknowledges that the matn may be incomplete and corrects it based on rational analysis.
4
Distinguish the instruments of inquiry
The question 'ma haqiqiyyah' (what is its real essence?) demands a real definition; the question 'ma sharhiyyah' (what is its explanation?) demands a nominal definition. Different questions yield different definition types.
This distinction is key: the type of definition depends on the aspect asked about.
5
Apply to an example
For 'human,' the real definition is 'rational animal' (essence); the nominal definition is 'the being that laughs' (concept). This shows both types are valid for the same real essence.
This example illustrates the practical application of the two answers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہوا کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف بھی صرف حقیقی ہوگی اسمی نہیں ہوگی۔
قلت في العدول عن ظاہر العبارة سعة :- یہاں سے شارح نے دو جواب دیے ہیں۔
جواب:(۱)۔ اگر چہ مصنف کی عبارت کے ظاہر سے یہی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف حقیقی ہی ہوتی ہے لیکن تاویل کر کے ظاہر سے عدول کیا جاسکتا ہے وہ اسطرح کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ میں حیثیت کی قید معتبر ہے تقدیر عبارت یوں ہوگی تعريف الماهية الحقيقية من حيث انها الماهية الحقيقية لهذا اب تعارض ختم ہو گیا کیونکہ مصنف کی عبارت کا مطلب بھی یہی ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف حقیقی تب ہوگی جب انکی ماہیات حقیقیہ ہونے کے اعتبار سے کی جائے اگر تعریف مفہومات کے اعتبار سے کی جائے تو وہ تعریف اسمی ہوگی دوسری تاویل یوں کی جاسکتی ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف اکثر طور پر تعریف حقیقی ہوتی ہے تقدیری عبارت ہوگی كتعريف الماهية الحقيقية من حيث الاكثر تیسری تاویل یوں بھی ہو سکتی ہے کہ كتعريف الماهيات الحقيقية کہہ کر تعریف حقیقی کی مثال بیان کی ہے اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف تعریف حقیقی پر منحصر ہے۔
جواب (۲):- یہ ہے کہ اگر مصنف کی عبارت کو ظاہر سے نہ ہٹایا جائے تو یہ عبارت تحقیق کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ تحقیق یہ ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف حقیقی بھی ہوگی اور تعریف اسمی بھی ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ میں دو اعتبار ہیں۔ (1) ماہیت حقیقیہ کا اعتبار کیا جائے۔ اس حیثیت سے کہ یہ ماہیت حقیقیہ ہے اس اعتبار سے جو تعریف ہوگی وہ تعریف حقیقی ہوگی اور اس ماہیت حقیقیہ کے بارہ میں جو سوال ہوگا وہ ما حقیقیہ کے ذریعے ہوگا۔ (۲) ماہیت حقیقیہ میں یہ لحاظ کیا جائے یہ اسم مسمی کا مفہوم ہے واضع کا متعقل متصور ہونے کے اعتبار سے ۔اس اعتبار سے تعریف اسمی ہوگی اس لئے کہ جب ماہیت حقیقیہ کے بارہ میں سوال کیا ہے تو ما شارحہ کے ذریعہ سوال ہوگا جو ما حقیقیہ سے دو درجے مؤخر ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ آلات طلب مختلف ہیں لھذا ان کے جوابات بھی مختلف ہوں گے۔
It happened that the definition of real essences is only real, not nominal. I said: There is scope to deviate from the apparent meaning of the expression. Here the commentator gave two answers. Answer (1): Although from the apparent meaning of the author's expression it is understood that the definition of real essences is only real, but by interpretation, deviation from the apparent is possible. That is, the condition of aspect is considered in real essences; the implied expression would be 'the definition of the real essence insofar as it is the real essence'. Thus the contradiction is resolved because the author's expression also means that the definition of real essences is real only when made from the aspect of their being real essences; if the definition is made from the aspect of concepts, then that definition would be nominal. A second interpretation is that the definition of real essences is mostly real; the implied expression would be 'the definition of the real essence in most cases'. A third interpretation is that by saying 'the definition of real essences' he gave an example of a real definition, from which it does not follow that the definition of real essences is confined to real definition. Answer (2): That if the author's expression is not removed from its apparent meaning, then this expression is contrary to the truth because the truth is that the definition of real essences will be both real and nominal. This is because real essences have two aspects: (1) Consider the real essence from the aspect that it is a real essence; the definition from that aspect will be real, and the question about that real essence will be through 'ma haqiqiyyah'. (2) Consider the real essence from the aspect that it is the concept of a name, what the positor imagines and conceptualizes; the definition from that aspect will be nominal because when the question is about the real essence, it will be through 'ma sharhiyyah', which is two steps behind 'ma haqiqiyyah'. So it became known that the instruments of inquiry are different, hence their answers will also be different.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a statement from the matn that definitions of real essences are only real definitions. The commentator (Sharh) provides two answers to resolve an apparent contradiction. The first answer uses interpretation (ta'wil) to show that the matn's statement can be understood in multiple ways: either by restricting the definition to a specific aspect, or by saying it is mostly real, or by considering it as an example. The second answer directly states that real essences can be defined both really and nominally depending on the aspect considered. The key is that the instruments of inquiry (alat talab) differ: when asking about the essence itself (ma haqiqiyyah) the answer is a real definition; when asking about the conceptual meaning (ma sharhiyyah) the answer is a nominal definition. This distinction is crucial for understanding the methodology of definition in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
ماهية حقيقية (māhiyyah ḥaqīqiyyah): A real essence, the quiddity of a thing in itself.
تعريف اسمي (taʿrīf ismī): A nominal definition that explains the meaning of a name, not the essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The agreement of scholars

Key Takeaway
Real essences can be defined both really and nominally depending on the aspect of inquiry; the commentator's two answers harmonize the matn with this truth.

Distinction Between Definition of Name and Definition of Reality
Explains the difference between ismi and haqiqi definitions with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between nominal (ismi) and real (haqiqi) definitions and apply this distinction to identify whether a given definition is nominal or real based on the stage of knowledge.

Core Idea
The same definition shifts from nominal to real once existence is known — existence changes the nature of the question.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, definitions play a crucial role in clarifying terms. One key distinction is between a nominal definition (al-ta'rif al-ismi), which explains a term before its existence is known, and a real definition (al-ta'rif al-haqiqi), which captures the essence after existence is established. This lesson unpacks that distinction, explaining how the same phrase can serve both functions depending on context, and illustrates it with examples from geometry and linguistics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definition types
Recognize that nominal definitions answer 'what is it in explanation?' (ma sharha) and real definitions answer 'what is its reality?' (ma haqiqiyya). The key difference is whether the existence of the defined thing is known or not.
Nominal definitions are often given when first learning a concept; real definitions are given once the concept's existence is established.
2
Analyze the role of existence knowledge
The passage states that before existence is known, a definition is nominal; after existence is known, the same definition becomes real. For example, the definition of a triangle as 'a figure bounded by three sides' is nominal in early geometry but real once triangles are known to exist.
Existence here refers to mental or external existence known to the definer.
3
Examine the examples
Consider the definition of 'man' as 'rational animal' – this is a real definition capturing essence. The definition of 'man' as 'laughing' is nominal because laughter is an accident, not essence. Similarly, 'ghudanfar' (lion) can be defined nominally before its existence is known and really after.
The example of 'laughing' shows that nominal definitions may use accidental attributes.
4
Apply to a new case
Take a term from usul al-fiqh, e.g., 'amm' (general). Before knowing that the category 'general' exists in revelation, a definition like 'a term that covers multiple individuals' is nominal. After confirming that such a category is used in sharia, the same definition becomes real.
This illustrates how the distinction is practical in fiqh reasoning.
5
Evaluate the diagram's contribution
The passage includes a diagram that visually organizes the relationships: mahiyyah (essence), haqiqah (reality), i'tibariyyah (considerational), and the two types of definitions. The diagram helps solidify the conceptual framework.
Review the diagram in the source to see how 'ma sharha' and 'ma haqiqiyya' relate to nominal and real definitions.

This definition: it is the last part of the explanation phrase. In short, Taftazani intends to explain a benefit that a nominal definition sometimes is the essence of the name itself such that the conceptualization of the positor is identical to the reality of the thing, and sometimes it is different from it. For example, defining man as 'rational animal' — this is both a real definition and identical to the reality of man. And defining man as 'laughing' or 'actual writer' — now 'laughing' and 'actual writer' are conceptualized and imagined, but they are not the reality of man; rather they are accidents. Further support comes from the fact that scholars have said that a nominal definition can also become identical to a real definition. The difference is this: before the existence of the thing is known, the definition is a nominal definition (because it answers the question 'ma sharha' — what is it in terms of explanation?), and after its existence is known, the same definition becomes a real definition (because it answers the question 'ma haqiqiyya' — what is its reality?). For example, at the beginning of geometry, a triangle is defined as 'a figure bounded by three sides' — this is a nominal definition. Then when its existence is known, if the same definition is given, it becomes a real definition. Benefit: I met Maulana Mufti Muhammad Hasan Sahib regarding writing a foreword, and he said that this point is difficult, but a diagram clarifies it. He provided a diagram; for blessing and for the ease of students, we are presenting that diagram on the next page. Diagram: 'Mahiyyah', 'Haqiqah', different definitions of haqiqah: 1. What exists in reality, 2. What is not artificial, 3. What is not dependent on a valid consideration, 4. What is not dependent on a positor's assumption. Example: 'ghudanfar' (lion). 'I'tibariyyah': i'tibariyyah also has various definitions: 1. What is artificial, 2. What depends on a valid consideration, etc. Example: genus, species, differentia. T'aqul wadi' haqiqatan aw... (Nominal definition: e.g., the word 'ghudanfar' is conceived in the mind of the positor as 'the dangerous thing' — i.e., the essence of the word 'ghudanfar' (predatory animal) is present in the mind, before existence. Triangle: before knowledge of the existence of triangle (nominal definition), after knowledge of existence (real definition). Or after existence: i.e., before knowledge of the existence of ghudanfar, 'ghudanfar is a predatory animal' (nominal definition); after knowledge of existence, 'ghudanfar is a predatory animal' (real definition). 'Ma sharha': the definition that seeks the meaning — first the question is asked via it: 'What is ghudanfar?' 'Ghudanfar is a predatory animal' (real definition). 'Ma haqiqiyyah': the definition that seeks the reality — i.e., via it the question is asked: 'Is the predatory animal ghudanfar existent or not?' Answer: 1. Asad — i.e., definition of a non-famous word with a famous word, 2. predatory animal, 3. dangerous thing (nominal definition). Answer: Yes (real definition).
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage discusses the distinction between al-ta'rif al-ismi (definition of the name) and al-ta'rif al-haqiqi (definition of the reality). The author explains that a definition can sometimes be identical to the essence of the thing, like defining 'man' as 'rational animal' which captures his essence. Other times, it defines through accidents like 'laughing' or 'actual writer' — these are not the essence but attributes. The key insight is that the same definition can be nominal before knowing the existence of the thing, and real after knowing it. For example, defining a triangle as 'a figure bounded by three sides' is nominal when you first learn geometry, but after you know that triangles exist, the same definition becomes real. The passage also includes a diagram that visually maps these concepts, distinguishing between 'ma sharha' (the question seeking explanation) and 'ma haqiqiyya' (the question seeking reality). This is an important usul al-fiqh distinction relevant to understanding how definitions function in legal reasoning.

Key Terms
التعريف الإسمي (al-ta'rif al-ismi): A definition that identifies a thing by its name or attributes before its existence is known, answering 'ma sharha' (what is it in explanation?).
التعريف الحقيقي (al-ta'rif al-haqiqi): A definition that captures the essence (haqiqah) of a thing after its existence is known, answering 'ma haqiqiyya' (what is its reality?).
ما شارحة (ma sharha): The interrogative particle that seeks an explanation or description of a thing, not necessarily its essence.
ما حقيقية (ma haqiqiyya): The interrogative particle that seeks the essence or reality of a thing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes a nominal definition from a real definition?
A) A nominal definition uses synonyms while a real definition uses genus and differentia.
B) A nominal definition is given before the existence of the thing is known; the same definition becomes real after existence is known.
C) A nominal definition always includes accidental attributes, while a real definition always includes the essence.
D) A nominal definition is used only for abstract concepts, while a real definition is used for physical objects.

Key Takeaway
A definition's classification as nominal or real depends on whether the existence of the defined thing is known, not on its content or structure.

Types of Definition: Haqiqi and Ismi
Explains the difference between real and nominal definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haqiqi and ismi definitions and classify example definitions.

Core Idea
A real definition captures essence; a nominal definition explains convention.

In Hanafi usul, definitions are either haqiqi (real) or ismi (nominal). The passage explains that haqiqi definitions describe the reality of a thing, while ismi definitions clarify the meaning intended by the positor. Understanding this distinction is foundational for evaluating definitions used in legal argumentation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and the definition
Locate the term being defined (e.g., 'ghudanfar') and the definition provided (e.g., 'hayawan muftaris' or 'shay' mudirr').
2
Determine the basis of the definition
Check whether the definition relies on real attributes (e.g., predatory nature) or conventional understanding (e.g., harmful thing).
If it depends on the positor's intent, it is ismi.
3
Classify as haqiqi or ismi
Based on the basis, decide the type. Haqiqi definitions are used when the essence is known; ismi definitions are used to explain a term's conventional meaning.
Both types must still satisfy tard and 'aks.

Reality (Haqiqah): various definitions: 1. that which exists in reality, 2. that which is not artificial, 3. that which does not depend on a valid consideration, 4. that which does not depend on a presumed assumption. Example: 'ghudanfar' (lion). Conventional (I'tibariyyah) also has various definitions: 1. that which is artificial, 2. that which depends on a valid consideration, etc. Example: genus, species, differentia, etc. The conceptualization of the positor of the reality or the final meaning (nominal definition) (e.g., the word 'muhassaf' is conceived in the mind of the positor) like 'al-ghudanfar huwa shay' mudirr' i.e., the essence of the word 'ghudanfar' (predatory animal) exists in the mind. Before existence: triangle. Before knowledge of the existence of the triangle (definition by 'asi')? After knowledge of the existence of the triangle (real definition). Or after existence: before knowledge of the existence of the ghudanfar: 'ghudanfar huwa hayawan muftaris' (definition by 'ami'?). 'Ma' sharhah: The definition that seeks the meaning. First, by means of it there will be a question: 'What is al-ghudanfar?' 'Al-ghudanfar huwa hayawan muftaris' (real definition). 'Ma' haqiqiyyah: The definition that seeks the reality, i.e., then by means of it there will be a question: 'Is al-ghudanfar al-hayawan al-muftaris existent or not?' Answer -1- 'asad' i.e., definition of an unfamiliar word with a familiar word. 2. 'hayawan muftaris' 3. 'shay' mudirr' (definition by 'asi'?) Answer: 'na'am' (real definition). His statement: 'And it is conditioned for both definitions' i.e., the real and the nominal, [the conditions of] tard and 'aks. As for tard, it is the truth of the definiendum concerning that which the definition is true of, universally, i.e., whenever the definition is true of something, the definiendum is true of it. That is the meaning of their saying 'whenever the definition is found, the definiendum is found.' So by tard, the definition becomes a preventer of the entry of other than the definiendum. As for 'aks, some took it from the converse of tard according to conventional understanding, and it is making the predicate a subject while observing the same quantity, just as it is said 'every human is laughing' and conversely, i.e., 'every laugher is human.' And 'every human is an animal' has no converse, i.e., not every animal is human. For this reason, he said concerning 'aks: 'Whenever the definiendum is true of something, the definition is true of it' as a reversal of our saying 'Whenever the definition is true of something, the definiendum is true of it.' So the result of tard is a universal judgment of the definiendum over the definition, and 'aks is a universal judgment of the definition over the definiendum. And some took it from 'the converse of affirmation is negation,' so he interpreted it as 'whenever the definition is negated, the definiendum is negated,' i.e., whenever the definition is not true of something, the definiendum is not true of it. So 'aks becomes a universal judgment of what is not definiendum over what is not definition. The result is one: that the definition encompasses all individuals of the definiendum. Translation: And a condition is laid for both definitions, i.e., real and nominal, of tard and 'aks. And in any case, tard: then the definiendum is true of that upon which the definition is true universally, i.e., 'whenever the definition is true of something, the definiendum is true of it.' And this is the meaning of their saying 'whenever the definition is found, the definiendum is found.' So by tard, the definition becomes a preventer of the entry of other than the definiendum. And in any case, some took 'aks from the converse of tard according to their conventional understanding, and it is making the predicate a subject while observing the same quantity, just as it is said 'every human is laughing' and its converse 'every laugher is human.' And 'every human is an animal' has no converse, i.e., 'not every animal is human.' For this reason, he said concerning 'aks: 'whenever the definiendum is true of something, the definition is true of it' as a reversal of our saying 'whenever the definition is true of something, the definiendum is true of it.'
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions required for definitions in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It begins by distinguishing between two types of definitions: haqiqi (real) and ismi (nominal). A real definition captures the essence or reality of a thing, such as defining 'ghudanfar' (a predatory animal) by its essential characteristics. A nominal definition merely explains the meaning of a term as understood by the positor, without necessarily reflecting reality. The passage then discusses the two necessary conditions for any valid definition: tard (coextensiveness) and 'aks (converseness). Tard means that whenever the definition applies to something, the definiendum also applies to it; this ensures the definition includes all instances of the definiendum and excludes non-instances. 'Aks means the opposite: whenever the definiendum applies, the definition applies; this ensures the definition is not too broad. The author explains these conditions using examples like 'all humans are laughing' and its converse 'all laughers are humans', noting that not all animals are humans, so the converse fails. The overall requirement is that a definition must be 'jami' (comprehensive) of all individuals of the definiendum and 'mani' (preventive) of what is not part of it.

Key Terms
التعريف الحقيقي (al-ta'rif al-haqiqi): A real definition that captures the essence of a thing, e.g., 'ghudanfar is a predatory animal'.
التعريف الاسمي (al-ta'rif al-ismi): A nominal definition that explains the meaning intended by the positor, e.g., 'ghudanfar is a harmful thing'.
الطرد (al-tard): The property that whenever the definition applies, the definiendum applies; coextensiveness.
العكس (al-'aks): The property that whenever the definiendum applies, the definition applies; converseness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a haqiqi definition according to the passage?
A) 'Ghudanfar is a harmful thing'
B) 'Ghudanfar is a predatory animal'
C) 'Ghudanfar is a word coined by the Arab'
D) 'Ghudanfar is an unknown animal'

Key Takeaway
Real definitions describe essence; nominal definitions explain convention; both must satisfy tard and 'aks.

Conditions of Sound Definition: Tard and 'Aks
Explains the two necessary conditions for any valid definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions of tard and 'aks to evaluate any definition and identify when a definition fails them.

Core Idea
A valid definition must be coextensive (tard) and converse ('aks) — including all instances and excluding all non-instances.

The passage explains that both real and nominal definitions must satisfy two conditions: tard (coextensiveness) and 'aks (converseness). Tard ensures the definition applies to every instance of the definiendum; 'aks ensures the definition applies only to instances of the definiendum. These conditions make the definition both comprehensive and exclusive.

Guided Path
1
State the definition and the definiendum
Identify the term being defined (definiendum) and the definition (definiens).
2
Check tard: Does the definition apply to all instances of the definiendum?
Test if every instance that satisfies the definition is also an instance of the definiendum. If yes, tard holds.
If there is a counterexample, tard fails.
3
Check 'aks: Does the definiendum apply to all instances of the definition?
Test if every instance of the definiendum also satisfies the definition. If yes, 'aks holds.
If the definition is too broad, 'aks fails.
4
Determine if the definition is sound
If both conditions hold, the definition is sound. If either fails, the definition is defective.
Hanafi usul requires both for legal definitions.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Conditions for Definitions: Tard and 'Aks
Explaining tard and 'aks as conditions for definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions of tard and 'aks for definitions and apply them to evaluate the validity of a definition.

Core Idea
A valid definition must be both coextensive (tard) and coextensive in reverse ('aks); otherwise it fails to define.

In this lesson, we examine two critical conditions required for any definition—whether real (haqiqi) or nominal (ismi)—in the Hanafi usul tradition: tard and 'aks. These conditions ensure that a definition precisely captures all instances of the term being defined (comprehensiveness) and excludes everything else (exclusivity). Understanding these logical tools is essential for formulating accurate legal definitions in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Recognize that both tard and 'aks are required for definitions. The passage states they are conditions for both real and nominal definitions.
2
Define tard
Tard means: whenever the definition (hadd) applies, the defined (mahdud) also applies. This ensures the definition is not too narrow—it covers all members of the defined category.
The text says: 'whenever the definition exists, the defined exists.'
3
Define 'aks
'Aks means: whenever the defined applies, the definition applies. This ensures the definition is not too broad—it excludes non-members. Two interpretations are given: (1) the logical converse (every laugher is human) and (2) the contrapositive (if definition is negated, defined is negated). Both achieve the same result.
The ultimate goal is that the definition is jam' (comprehensive) and mani' (exclusive).
4
Apply to a legal example
Test a definition like 'prayer (salah) is actions beginning with takbir and ending with taslim'. Check tard: does every action with takbir and taslim count as salah? Check 'aks: does every salah have takbir and taslim? If either fails, the definition is invalid.
This illustrates how tard and 'aks operate in fiqh.

قَوْلُهُ ) وَشُرِطَ لِكَلَا التَّعْرِيفَيْنِ ) أَى الْحَقِيقِى وَالاسْمِي الطَّرُدُ وَالْعَكْسُ أَمَّا الطَّرُدُ فَهُوَ صِدْقُ المَحْدُودِ عَلَى مَا صَدَقَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ مُطَّرِدًا كُلِّيَّا أَى كُلَّمَا صَدَقَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ صَدَقَ عَلَيْهِ الْمَحْدُودُ ، وَهُوَ مَعْنَى قَوْلِهِمْ كُلَّمَا وُجِدَ الْحَدُّ وُجِدَ المَحْدُودُ فَبِالْأَطْرَادِ يُصِيرُ الْحَدُّ مَانِعًا عَنْ دُخُول غَيْرِ الْمَحْدُودِ وَأَمَّا الْعَكْسُ فَأَخَذَهُ بَعْضُهُمُ مِنْ عَكس الطَّرْدِ بِحَسَبِ مُتَفَاهَم الْعُرْفِ ، وَهُوَ جَعَلُ الْمَحْمُولِ مَوْضُوعًا مَعَ رِعَايَةِ الْكَمِّيَّةِ بِعَيْنِهَا كَمَا يُقَالُ كُلُّ إِنْسَانٍ ضَاحِكَ وَبِالْعَكْسِ أَيْ كُلُّ ضَاحِكٍ إِنْسَانٌ وَكُلُّ إِنْسَانِ حَيَوَانٌ وَلَا عَكْسَ أَى لَيْسَ كُلُّ حَيَوَانٍ إِنْسَانًا فَلِهَذَا قَالَ فِى الْعَكْس إنَّ كُلَّ مَا صَدَقَ عَلَيْهِ الْمَحْدُودُ صَدَقَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ عَكْسًا لِقَوْلِنَا كُلُّ مَا صَدَقَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ صَدَقَ عَلَيْهِ الْمَحْدُودُ فَصَارَ حَاصِلُ الطَّرْدِ حُكْمًا كُلْيا بِالْمَحْدُودِ عَلَى الْحَدِّ وَالْعَكْسُ حُكْمًا كُلِّيًّا بِالْحَدِّ عَلَى الْمَحْدُودِ وَبَعْضُهُمُ أَخَذَهُ مِنْ أَنْ عَكْسَ الْإِثْبَاتِ نَفَى فَفَسَّرَهُ بِأَنَّهُ كُلَّمَا انْتَفَى الْحَدُّ انْتَفَى الْمَحْدُودُ أَيْ كُلَّمَا لَمْ يَصْدُقْ عَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ لَمْ يَصْدُقْ عَلَيْهِ المَحْدُودُ فَصَارَ الْعَكْسُ حُكْمًا كُلِّيًّا بِمَا لَيْسَ بِمَحْدُودٍ عَلَى مَا لَيْسَ بِحَدٍّ وَالْحَاصِلُ وَاحِدٌ ، وَهُوَ أن يَكُونَ الحَدُّ جَامِعًا لِأَفْرَادِ الْمَحْدُودِ كُلِّهَا
His statement: 'And a condition for both definitions' — i.e., the real (haqiqi) and nominal (ismi) — [is] tard and 'aks. As for tard, it is that the defined (mahdud) is true of whatever the definition (hadd) is true of, universally, i.e., whenever the definition is true of something, the defined is true of it. And that is the meaning of their statement: 'Whenever the definition exists, the defined exists.' Through tard, the definition becomes a preventer of entry of what is not the defined. As for 'aks, some took it from the reverse of tard according to common understanding (mutafahim al-'urf). It is making the predicate the subject while observing the same quantity, as it is said: 'Every human is laughing' and conversely 'Every laugher is human.' And 'Every human is an animal' but not conversely, i.e., not every animal is human. Therefore, he said about 'aks: 'Whenever the defined is true of something, the definition is true of it,' as the converse of our statement: 'Whenever the definition is true of something, the defined is true of it.' So the result of tard is a universal judgment of the defined over the definition, and 'aks is a universal judgment of the definition over the defined. Some took it from 'the reverse of affirmation is negation' and interpreted it as: 'Whenever the definition is negated, the defined is negated,' i.e., whenever the definition is not true, the defined is not true. Thus, 'aks becomes a universal judgment of what is not defined over what is not a definition. The conclusion is one: that the definition encompasses all individuals of the defined.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a statement from al-Tawdih, explaining the conditions for both real (haqiqi) and nominal (ismi) definitions. The commentator expands on two essential conditions: tard (coextension) and 'aks (coextensiveness). Tard means that whenever the definition applies, the defined applies; it ensures the definition is not too narrow. 'Aks means that whenever the defined applies, the definition applies; it ensures the definition is not too broad. The commentator presents two interpretations of 'aks: one as the logical converse of the proposition (e.g., 'every human is laughing' and conversely 'every laugher is human'), and another as contrapositive: if the definition is absent, the defined is absent. Both interpretations are functionally equivalent. The ultimate goal is that the definition must be comprehensive (jam') of all individuals of the defined and exclusive (mani') of what is not the defined. This is a foundational principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh for formulating valid definitions of legal terms, though the discussion here is logical and epistemological rather than directly legal. The commentator emphasizes that satisfying both conditions ensures the definition is precise and useful for distinguishing the defined from other categories.

Key Terms
الطرد (al-ṭard): The condition that whenever the definition (hadd) applies, the defined (mahdud) applies; i.e., the definition must be coextensive with the defined.
العكس (al-ʿaks): The condition that whenever the defined applies, the definition applies; i.e., the definition must be exclusive to the defined. Two interpretations: converse or contrapositive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the function of 'aks (coextensiveness) in a definition?
A) It ensures that the definition includes all members of the defined.
B) It ensures that the definition excludes non-members.
C) It ensures that the definition is brief.
D) It ensures that the definition uses synonyms.

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must satisfy both tard (comprehensiveness) and 'aks (exclusiveness); without them, the definition is too narrow or too broad.

Two Meanings of 'Aks in Definition Rules
Clarifying the term 'aks in definition rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two meanings of 'aks in Hanafi definition rules and evaluate why the terminological (logical) 'aks is not intended.

Core Idea
The 'aks in definition rules is either the customary converse or the contradictory — not the logical converse.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, a proper definition must satisfy both ṭard (co-extensiveness) and 'aks (conversely co-extensive). But what exactly does 'aks mean? The term 'aks has several logical and linguistic senses. This lesson unpacks the two primary meanings—naqid (contradictory) and 'aks mustawī (converse)—and their subdivisions. You will see why the immediately apparent logical (terminological) converse fails to establish universal applicability, and why the customary converse or the contradictory must be intended instead.

التَّرُويْحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيح وَالتَّلويح پہلے بطور تمہید کے ایک مقدمہ کو جانا ضروری ہے۔
مقدمہ: عکس کے اول دو معنے ہیں (۱) نقیض یعنی ثبت و نفی کرتا اور منفی وثبت کرنا جسے کل انسان حیوان کی لقیض آتی ہے کیا ئیس بانسان لیس بحیوان (۲) عکس مستوی ۔ پھر عکس مستوی کے دو معنے ہیں (۱) طرد کا عکس مستوی لغوی و عرفی (۲) عکس اصطلاحی عکس مستوی لغوی یہ ہے کہ اصل قضیہ کے موضوع کو مول اور محمول کو موضوع بنا دینا بشر طیکہ کیفیت بھی اپنے حال پر باقی رہے اور کمیت بھی اپنے حال پر باقی رہے کیفیت کے باقی رہنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر اصل قضیہ موجبہ ہو تو اسکے عکس سے حاصل ہونے والا قضیہ بھی موجہ ہو اور کمیت کے باقی رہنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر اصل قضیہ کلیہ ہو تو اسکے عکس سے حاصل ہونے والا قضیہ بھی کلیہ ہو جیسے کل انسان ضاحک کا عکس مستوی لغوی کل ضاحک انسان ہے اور عکس مستوی اصطلاحی میں کیفیت تو اپنے حال پر باقی رہتی ہے لیکن کمیت اپنے حال پر باقی نہیں رہتی یہی وجہ ہے کہ عکس مستوی اصطلاحی میں موجہ کلیہ کا عکس مستوی موجبہ جزئیہ آتا ہے جیسے کل انسان حیوان کا عکس مستوی اصطلاحی بعض الحیوان انسان ہے اور اسکا عکس لغوی چینی کل حیوان انسان سیہ کا ذب ہے۔
کس کی تعیین مراد
سوال:۔ یہ ہے کہ عکس سے مراد متبادر الی الذہن عکس منطقی ہے حالانکہ کہ عکس منطقی مراد نہیں لے سکتے کیونکہ عکس منطقی ( اصطلاحی ) میں وجہ کلیہ کا کس موجہ جزئیہ آتا ہے تو کلماصدق علیہ الصدق علیہ الحمد ود بی طرد ہے اور اسکا عکس موجہ جزئیہ آئے گا یعنی بعض ما صدق علیہ المحدود صدق علیہ الھد یعنی بعض جگہوں پر محدود صادق آئے گا تو اس پر حد صادق آئے گی اب حکم کلی طور پر ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔
جواب (۱):۔ یہاں عکس لغوی مراد ہے اب اس صورت میں طرد سے حاصل ہونے والا قضیہ کا بعنوان ثانی کلمار الحد وجد المحدود كاعس كلما وجد المحدود وجد الحد آئے گا اور طر د سے حاصل ہونے والا قضیہ بعنوان اول كلما صدق عليه الحد صدق عليه المحدود کا عکس مستوى عرفى كلما صدق عليه المحدود صدق علیہ الحد آئے گا گویا کہ کس کا حاصل ضدق الحد كليا على المحدود ہے جس طرح طرد کا حاصل تھا صدق
المحدود كليا على الحد
جواب (۲):۔ یہاں عکس طرد سے مراد نقیض ہے یعنی طرد کی نقیض اور قاعدہ ہے کہ نقیض گل شی رفعہ اس قول کے مطابق طرد کا حاص بعنوان آخرتها كلما وجد الحد وجد المحدود اسکی نقیض ہوگی كلما انتفى الحد انتفى المحدود اور طرو کا حاصل بعنوان اول تھا كلما صدق عليه الحد صدق عليه المحدود اسکی نقیض ہوگی كلما لم يصدق علیہ الحد لم يصدق عليه المحدود خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ یہاں عکس طرد سے عکس مستوی عرفی مراد ہے اور عکس بمعنی نقیض مراد ہے عکس منطقی مراد نہیں ہے۔
سوال: عکس اصطلاحی بھی مراد لے سکتے ہیں کیونکہ مناطقہ نے تصریح کی ہے کہ عام طور پر موجبہ کلیہ کا عکس موجبہ جرسیہ آتا ہے لیکن اگر تالی اور مقدم میں مساوات ہوتو پھر موجہ کلیہ کا عکس موجہ کلیہ ہی آتا ہے جیسے کل انسان ناطق یہاں ناطق انسان کے مساوی ہے تو اس قضیہ کا عکس مستوی موجبہ کلیہ یعنی کل ناطق انسان آئے گا اور یہاں پر بھی کیونکہ حد اور محدود میں مساوات پائی جاتی ہے تو كلما صدق علیہ الحد صدق علیہ الحدود میں تالی مقدم کے مساوی ہوگا تو عکس منطقی موجبہ کلیہ ہی آئے گا یعنی كلما صدق علیہ الحمد ود صدق علیہ الحد اور اس قضیہ سے بھی تعریف کی جامعیت معلوم ہو جائیگی۔
جواب :۔ مذکورہ قضیہ میں تالی مقدم کے مساوی تب ہو سکتا ہے جب حد اور محدود میں مساوات ثابت ہو اور یہ مساوات تب ثابت ہوگی جب طرد اور عکس طرد ثابت ہو جائیں حالانکہ ابھی ہم عکس طرد کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں اس سے تو لازم آئے گا کہ شی اپنے وجود سے پہلے موجود ہو حالانکہ یہ باطل ہے۔
والحاصل واحد : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ نہے غرض شارح یہ ہے کہ عکس کے دونوں معنوں کا مال اور انجام ایک ہے کہ حدا اپنے تمام افراد کو جامع ہو جائے اور کس کے یہ دونوں معانی عین جمع نہیں بلکہ جامع ہونے کوستلزم ہیں تفصیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ عکس عرفی کی صورت میں قضیہ ہوگا کلما صدق علیہ الحد و وصدق علیہ الحد کہ جہاں محدود صادق آئے گا وہاں حد صادق آئے گی تو ظاہر ہے کہ خدا اپنے تمام افراد کو جامع ہوگی اور نقیض والے معنی کے اعتبار سے قضیہ حاصل ہوگا کلما فی الحد انتفی المحمد وداور جہاں یہ صادق آئے تو وہاں یہ بھی صادق آئے گا کلما وجد الحد و دو جدالحد تو یہ دونوں ایک دوسرے کو لازم ہوئے اور یہی حد کا جامع ہوتا ہے۔
AL-TARWĪḤ LI-ḤALL AL-TAWḌĪḤ WA AL-TALWĪḤ. First, as an introduction, knowing a preamble is necessary. Preamble: 'Aks has two meanings: (1) Naqīḍ (contradictory), i.e., affirming negation and negating affirmation, like 'every human is an animal' has its contradictory 'some human is not an animal'. (2) 'Aks mustawī (converse). Then 'aks mustawī has two meanings: (1) The 'aks mustawī of ṭard, linguistic and customary. (2) The terminological 'aks. The linguistic 'aks mustawī is making the subject of the original proposition the predicate and the predicate the subject, provided that the quality remains as it is and the quantity remains as it is. The meaning of the quality remaining is that if the original proposition is affirmative, then the proposition obtained from its converse is also affirmative. The meaning of the quantity remaining is that if the original proposition is universal, then the proposition obtained from its converse is also universal. For example, the linguistic 'aks mustawī of 'every human is laughing' is 'every laughing is human'. And in the terminological 'aks mustawī, the quality remains as it is, but the quantity does not remain as it is. This is why in the terminological 'aks mustawī, the 'aks mustawī of an affirmative universal is an affirmative particular. For example, the terminological 'aks mustawī of 'every human is an animal' is 'some animal is human'. And its linguistic 'aks would be 'every animal is human'? That is impossible.
Determination of what is intended: Question: It is that what is immediately understood from 'aks is the logical 'aks, but we cannot intend the logical 'aks because in the logical (terminological) 'aks, the converse of a universal affirmative comes as a particular affirmative. Thus, from 'wherever the limit applies, the limited applies' (the ṭard) its converse would come as a particular affirmative, i.e., 'from some places where the limited applies, the limit applies'. So the limit would apply to some places, but the judgment would not be universally established.
Answer (1): Here the linguistic 'aks is intended. In this case, the proposition obtained from ṭard as a second title would be 'wherever the limit is found, the limited is found', i.e., 'wherever the limited is found, the limit is found'. And the proposition obtained from ṭard as a first title, 'wherever the limit applies, the limited applies' — its customary 'aks mustawī would be 'wherever the limited applies, the limit applies'. So the result is that the limit applies universally to the limited, just as the result of ṭard was that the limited applies universally to the limit.
Answer (2): Here by 'aks of ṭard is meant the contradictory, i.e., the contradictory of ṭard. And the rule is that the contradictory negates everything. According to this statement, the result of ṭard as the second title was 'wherever the limit is found, the limited is found'; its contradictory would be 'wherever the limit is absent, the limited is absent'. And the result of ṭard as the first title was 'wherever the limit applies, the limited applies'; its contradictory would be 'wherever the limit does not apply, the limited does not apply'. In summary, here by 'aks of ṭard is meant the customary 'aks mustawī, and 'aks in the sense of contradictory is intended, not the logical 'aks.
Question: Can the terminological 'aks also be intended? Because the logician stated that generally the converse of a universal affirmative is a particular affirmative, but if there is equality between the consequent and the antecedent, then the converse of a universal affirmative is itself a universal affirmative. For example, 'every human is rational', here rational is equal to human, so the 'aks mustawī of this proposition is a universal affirmative, i.e., 'every rational is human'. And here too, since there is equality between the limit and the limited, in 'wherever the limit applies, the limited applies', the consequent would be equal to the antecedent, so the logical 'aks would be a universal affirmative, i.e., 'wherever the limited applies, the limit applies'. And from this proposition, the comprehensiveness of the definition would also be known.
Answer: The aforementioned proposition can have the consequent equal to the antecedent only when equality between the limit and the limited is proven, and this equality is proven only when ṭard and 'aks al-ṭard are proven. Yet we are in the process of proving 'aks al-ṭard. This would necessitate that a thing exists before its existence, which is false.
Conclusion: This is the last part of the commentary's expression. The commentator's purpose is that the outcome of both meanings of 'aks is one: that the limit encompasses all its individuals. And these two meanings are not the same as encompassment, but rather necessitate encompassment. The detail is that in the case of customary 'aks, the proposition would be 'wherever the limit applies, the limited applies' — wherever the limited applies, the limit applies. So it is clear that the limit encompasses all its individuals. And according to the meaning of contradictory, the proposition would be 'wherever the limit is negated, the limited is negated' — and where it applies, the other also applies: 'wherever the limit is found, the limited is found'. So these two necessitate each other, and that is the limit's encompassment.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the term 'aks (inverse) as it appears in the rule for definitions in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first distinguishes two primary meanings of 'aks: (1) naqid (contradictory), which is the logical operator that swaps truth values, and (2) 'aks mustawi (converse), which swaps the subject and predicate. The latter is further subdivided into linguistic ('urfi/customary) and terminological (istilahi) varieties. The linguistic converse preserves both quality and quantity (e.g., 'every human is laughing' becomes 'every laughing is human'). The terminological converse preserves only quality, so a universal affirmative becomes a particular affirmative (e.g., 'every human is animal' becomes 'some animal is human').

The central problem is to determine which meaning of 'aks is intended in the rule that a proper definition must satisfy both ṭard (co-extensiveness: the definition applies wherever the definiendum applies) and 'aks (converse: the definiendum applies wherever the definition applies). The immediate intuitive reading is the logical converse, but the author shows this does not work because the logical converse of a universal proposition would be particular, failing to prove universal applicability. Instead, the intended meaning is either the customary 'aks mustawi (linguistic converse preserving universality) or the naqid (contradictory). Both ultimately yield the result that the definition encompasses all individuals of the definiendum.

The author then refutes an objection that the terminological converse could be used if equality between limit and limited is proven, because that would be circular (proving aks requires prior proof of equality, which itself requires aks). Thus, the only viable interpretations are the customary converse or the contradictory. The commentary concludes that both interpretations lead to the same result: the definition's comprehensiveness.

Key Terms
عکس ('aks): General term meaning 'inverse'. In this passage, it has two primary meanings: naqid (contradictory) and 'aks mustawi (converse).
عکس مستوی ('aks mustawī): Converse that swaps subject and predicate. Subdivided into linguistic (preserving quantity) and terminological (preserving only quality).
نقیض (naqīḍ): Contradictory: a proposition that denies the original, e.g., from 'every A is B' to 'some A is not B'.
طرد (ṭard): Co-extensiveness: the definition applies wherever the definiendum applies. Part of the condition for a sound definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why cannot the terminological (logical) 'aks be the intended meaning in the rule for definitions?
A) Because the terminological 'aks of a universal affirmative is a particular affirmative, failing to prove universal applicability.
B) Because the terminological 'aks always requires a circular proof.
C) Because the terminological 'aks is only used in logic, not in fiqh.
D) Because the terminological 'aks changes the quality of the proposition.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi definition rules, 'aks means either the customary converse (preserving universality) or the contradictory, not the logical converse.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
Critique of Defining Asl as Muhtaj Ilayh
Analyzing why defining 'asl' as 'muhtaj ilayh' fails coextensiveness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five causal categories and apply the condition of coextensiveness (intirād) to critique a definition in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Defining 'asl' as 'that which is needed' fails because only the material cause qualifies as an 'asl' linguistically.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary demonstrates how definitions are critically examined. The commentator takes the definition of 'asl' as 'muhtāj ilayh' and tests it against the condition of coextensiveness. By breaking down 'need' into five causal categories—material, formal, efficient, final, and conditional—he shows that only one category truly fits the term 'asl'. Yet the discussion does not end there; four objections are raised that challenge either the necessity of coextensiveness or the exclusion of certain causes. This lesson guides you through the logical steps of definition analysis, a crucial skill for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition under scrutiny
The definition being critiqued is: 'asl = muhtāj ilayh' (that which is needed). This is a nominal definition of the word 'asl' in its linguistic sense.
The commentator clarifies that this is a nominal definition, but lack of coextensiveness corrupts it regardless of type.
2
Break down 'need' into causal categories
The commentator classifies everything needed by a thing into five types: material (mādda), formal (ṣūra), efficient (fāʿil), final (ghāya), and conditional (sharṭ). Understand each category with the example of a bed.
The first two are internal (dākhil), the last three are external (khārij).
3
Apply the linguistic test
Verify which categories are actually called 'asl' in common language. Only the material cause (e.g., the wood of a bed) is called 'asl'. The remaining four are needed but not called 'asl'.
The phrase 'asl of this bed' refers to the material, not the carpenter or the purpose.
4
Assess coextensiveness
The definition fails intirād because it applies to things that are not 'asl' (the other four causes). The definition is too broad: it includes cases that do not match the defined term.
A coextensive definition must apply to all and only the members of the defined set.
5
Consider the four objections
The commentator raises four objections to his own critique: (1) intirād is not always required, especially for nominal definitions; (2) the efficient cause can be seen as 'asl' due to dependence; (3) earlier statements imply every needed thing is an asl; (4) in the definition of thought, known matters are called asl even without direct causal building. Evaluate these counter-arguments.
These objections show flexibility in defining purposes and the nuanced nature of usul discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَولُهُ وَلَا شَكٍّ أَنَّ تَعرِيفَ الأصلِ تَعْرِيفٌ اسمِيٌّ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ تَبِينُ أَنَّ لَفَظَ الأَصلِ فِي اللُّغَةِ مَوضُوعٌ لِلمُرَكَّب الاعتبارى الَّذِى هُوَ الشَّيءُ مَعَ وَصفِ ابْتِنَاءِ الغَيرِ عَلَيْهِ أو احتياج الغَيرِ إِلَيهِ وَهَذَا لَا دَخلَ لَهُ فِي بَيَانِ فَسَادِ التَّعْرِيفِ إِذ عَدَمُ الاطرَادِ مُفسِدٌ لَهُ اسمِيًّا كَانَ أَو غَيْرَهُ فَفِي الجُملَةِ تَعْرِيفُ الأَصْلِ بِالمُحْتَاجِ إِلَيْهِ غَيْرُ مُطَّرِدٍ إِذ لَا يَصدُقُ أَنَّ كُلَّ مُحتاج إِلَيْهِ أَصل ؛ لِأَنَّ مَا يَحتَاجُ إِلَيْهِ الشَّيْءُ إِمَّا دَاخِلٌ فِيهِ أَو خَارِجٌ عَنهُ وَالأَوَّلُ إِمَّا أَن يَكُونَ وُجُودُ الشَّيْءِ مَعَهُ بِالقُوَّةِ وَهُوَ المَادَّةُ لِلسَّرِيرِ أو بِالفِعلِ وَهُوَ الصُّورَةُ كَالهَييَّةِ السَّرِيرِيَّةِ لَهُ ، وَالثَّانِي إِن كَانَ مَا مِنهُ الشَّيءُ فَهُوَ الفَاعِلُ كَالنَّجَارِ لِلسَّرِيرِ وَإِن كَانَ مَا لِأجَلِهِ الشَّيءُ فَهُوَ الغَايَةُ كَالجُلُوسِ عَلَى السَّرِيرِ وَإِلَّا فَهُوَ الشَّرطُ كَالَاتِ النَّجَّارِ وَقَابِلِيَّةِ الخَشَبِ وَنَحوِ ذَلِكَ فَهَذِهِ خَمْسَةُ أَقسَامٍ لِلمُحتاج إِلَيْهِ لَا يُطْلَقُ لَفظُ الْاصِلِ لُغَةٌ إِلَّا عَلَى وَاحِدٍ مِنهَا وَهُوَ المَادَّةُ كَمَا يُقَالُ أَصلُ هَذَا السَّرِيرِ خَشَبْ كَذَا وَالأَربَعَةُ البَاقِيَةُ يَصدُقُ عَلَى كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنهَا أَنَّهُ مُحتَاجٌ إِلَيْهِ وَلَا يَصدُقُ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّهُ أَصل فَلَا يَكُونُ التَّعرِيفُ مُطَّرِدًا مَانِعًا وَهَهُنَا بَحتُ مِن وُجُوهِ أَحَدُهَا مَنعُ اسْتِرَاطِ الطَّرِدِ فِي مُطْلَقِ التَّعْرِيفِ لَا سِيَّمَا فِى الاسمى فَإِنَّ كُتبَ اللُّغَةِ مَشحُونَةٌ بِتَفسِيرِ الْأَلْفَاظِ بِمَا هُوَ أَعَمُّ مِن مَفهُومَاتِهَا وَقَد صَرَّحَ المُحَقِّقُونَ بِأَنَّ التَّعرِيفَاتِ النَّاقِصَةَ يَجُوزُ أَن تَكُونَ أَعَمَّ بحيث لا يُفِيدُ الامتياز إِلَّا عَن بَعضِ مَا عَدَا المَحدُودَ وَأَنَّ الْغَرَضَ مِن تَفسِيرِ الشَّيءِ قَد يَكُونُ تَمَيَّزَهُ عَن شَيءٍ مُعَيَّنٍ فَيُكتَفَى بِمَا يُفِيدُ الامْتِيَازَ عَنهُ كَمَا إِذَا قصِدَ التَّمِيزَ بَينَ الأصلِ وَالفَرْعِ فَيُفَسِّرُ الأَوَّلُ بِالمُحتَاجِ إِلَيهِ وَالثَّانِي بِالمُحتَاجِ وَثَانِيهَا مَنعُ عَدَمِ صِدقِ الأصلِ عَلَى الفَاعِلِ كَيفَ وَالْفِعَلُ مُتَرَتِّبٌ عَلَيْهِ وَمُستَنِدٌ إليهِ وَلا مَعنَى لِلابْتِسَاءِ إِلَّا ذَلِكَ . وَثَالِتُهَا أَنْ كَلَامَهُ فِي بَابِ الْمَجَازِ عِندَ بَيَانِ ( ثم في الصفحة التالية ) التَّرُويْحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيحِ وَالتَّلويج قَولُهُ وَلَا شَكٍّ أَنَّ تَعرِيفَ الأصلِ تَعْرِيفٌ اسمِيٌّ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ تَبِينُ أَنَّ لَفَظَ الأَصلِ فِي اللُّغَةِ مَوضُوعٌ لِلمُرَكَّب الاعتبارى الَّذِى هُوَ الشَّيءُ مَعَ وَصفِ ابْتِنَاءِ الغَيرِ عَلَيْهِ أو احتياج الغَيرِ إِلَيهِ وَهَذَا لَا دَخلَ لَهُ فِي بَيَانِ فَسَادِ التَّعْرِيفِ إِذ عَدَمُ الاطرَادِ مُفسِدٌ لَهُ اسمِيًّا كَانَ أَو غَيْرَهُ فَفِي الجُملَةِ تَعْرِيفُ الأَصْلِ بِالمُحْتَاجِ إِلَيْهِ غَيْرُ مُطَّرِدٍ إِذ لَا يَصدُقُ أَنَّ كُلَّ مُحتاج إِلَيْهِ أَصل ؛ لِأَنَّ مَا يَحتَاجُ إِلَيْهِ الشَّيْءُ إِمَّا دَاخِلٌ فِيهِ أَو خَارِجٌ عَنهُ وَالأَوَّلُ إِمَّا أَن يَكُونَ وُجُودُ الشَّيْءِ مَعَهُ بِالقُوَّةِ وَهُوَ المَادَّةُ لِلسَّرِيرِ أو بِالفِعلِ وَهُوَ الصُّورَةُ كَالهَييَّةِ السَّرِيرِيَّةِ لَهُ ، وَالثَّانِي إِن كَانَ مَا مِنهُ الشَّيءُ فَهُوَ الفَاعِلُ كَالنَّجَارِ لِلسَّرِيرِ وَإِن كَانَ مَا لِأجَلِهِ الشَّيءُ فَهُوَ الغَايَةُ كَالجُلُوسِ عَلَى السَّرِيرِ وَإِلَّا فَهُوَ الشَّرطُ كَالَاتِ النَّجَّارِ وَقَابِلِيَّةِ الخَشَبِ وَنَحوِ ذَلِكَ فَهَذِهِ خَمْسَةُ أَقسَامٍ لِلمُحتاج إِلَيْهِ لَا يُطْلَقُ لَفظُ الْاصِلِ لُغَةٌ إِلَّا عَلَى وَاحِدٍ مِنهَا وَهُوَ المَادَّةُ كَمَا يُقَالُ أَصلُ هَذَا السَّرِيرِ خَشَبْ كَذَا وَالأَربَعَةُ البَاقِيَةُ يَصدُقُ عَلَى كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنهَا أَنَّهُ مُحتَاجٌ إِلَيْهِ وَلَا يَصدُقُ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّهُ أَصل فَلَا يَكُونُ التَّعرِيفُ مُطَّرِدًا مَانِعًا وَهَهُنَا بَحتُ مِن وُجُوهِ أَحَدُهَا مَنعُ اسْتِرَاطِ الطَّرِدِ فِي مُطْلَقِ التَّعْرِيفِ لَا سِيَّمَا فِى الاسمى فَإِنَّ كُتبَ اللُّغَةِ مَشحُونَةٌ بِتَفسِيرِ الْأَلْفَاظِ بِمَا هُوَ أَعَمُّ مِن مَفهُومَاتِهَا وَقَد صَرَّحَ المُحَقِّقُونَ بِأَنَّ التَّعرِيفَاتِ النَّاقِصَةَ يَجُوزُ أَن تَكُونَ أَعَمَّ بحيث لا يُفِيدُ الامتياز إِلَّا عَن بَعضِ مَا عَدَا المَحدُودَ وَأَنَّ الْغَرَضَ مِن تَفسِيرِ الشَّيءِ قَد يَكُونُ تَمَيَّزَهُ عَن شَيءٍ مُعَيَّنٍ فَيُكتَفَى بِمَا يُفِيدُ الامْتِيَازَ عَنهُ كَمَا إِذَا قصِدَ التَّمِيزَ بَينَ الأصلِ وَالفَرْعِ فَيُفَسِّرُ الأَوَّلُ بِالمُحتَاجِ إِلَيهِ وَالثَّانِي بِالمُحتَاجِ وَثَانِيهَا مَنعُ عَدَمِ صِدقِ الأصلِ عَلَى الفَاعِلِ كَيفَ وَالْفِعَلُ مُتَرَتِّبٌ عَلَيْهِ وَمُستَنِدٌ إليهِ وَلا مَعنَى لِلابْتِسَاءِ إِلَّا ذَلِكَ . وَثَالِتُهَا أَنْ كَلَامَهُ فِي بَابِ الْمَجَازِ عِندَ بَيَانِ جَرَيَانِ الْأَصَالَةِ وَالتَّبْعِيَّةِ مِن الجَانِبَينِ يَدُلُّ عَلَىٰ أَنَّ كُلَّ مُحتَاجِ إِلَيْهِ فَهُوَ أَصَلَّ وَرَابِعُهَا أَنَّا إِذَا قُلْنَا الفِكرُ تَرتِيبُ أُمُورٍ مَعْلُومَةٍ فَلَا شَكَ أَنَّ الْأُمُورَ المَعْلُومَةَ مَادَّةٌ للفكرِ وَأَصل لَهُ مَعَ أَنَّ ابْتِنَاءَ الفكرِ عَلَيْهَا لَيسَ حَسْبا رَوَارَ وَلَا عَقلِيًّا بِتَفسِيرِ المُصَنِّفِ وَهُوَ تَرَتُبُ الحُكمِ عَلَى دَلِيلِهِ .
His statement: 'And there is no doubt that defining 'asl' is a nominal definition; because it becomes clear that the word 'asl' in language is placed for a relational compound which is a thing together with the attribute of something else being built upon it or the need of something else for it. And this has no bearing on showing the corruption of the definition, because lack of coextensiveness (intirād) corrupts it whether nominal or otherwise. So in summary, defining 'asl' as 'that which is needed' (muhtāj ilayh) is not coextensive, since it is not true that everything needed is an 'asl'. Because that which something needs is either internal to it or external to it. The first is either such that the thing exists with it potentially (bi-l-quwwa), which is the material (mādda) for the bed, or actually (bi-l-fiʿl), which is the form (ṣūra) like the bed-form for it. The second (external) if it is that from which the thing comes, it is the efficient cause (fāʿil) like the carpenter for the bed; if it is that for the sake of which the thing exists, it is the final cause (ghāya) like sitting on the bed; otherwise it is the condition (sharṭ) like the carpenter's tools and the receptivity of the wood and the like. So these are five divisions of 'that which is needed' (muhtāj ilayh); the word 'asl' in language is only applied to one of them, which is the material, as it is said 'the asl of this bed is such-and-such wood'. The remaining four each are truly called 'that which is needed' but not 'asl'. So the definition is not coextensive and exclusive. And here is a discussion from several aspects: First, denying the condition of coextensiveness for all definitions, especially nominal definitions, for books of lexicography are full of explanations of terms with what is more general than their meanings. And the verifying scholars have explicitly stated that incomplete definitions may be more general, such that they do not effect differentiation except from some of what is other than the defined, and that the purpose of explaining something may be to differentiate it from a specific thing, so one is satisfied with what effects differentiation from it, just as when one intends differentiation between 'asl' and farʿ, so the first is interpreted as 'needed' and the second as 'needing'. Second, denying that the word 'asl' does not apply to the efficient cause; how can it, while the effect is dependent upon it and based on it, and building means nothing else. Third, that his statement in the chapter of metaphor when explaining the running of originality and subsequence from both sides indicates that everything needed is an 'asl'. Fourth, that when we say 'thinking is the arrangement of known matters', there is no doubt that the known matters are the material for thinking and an asl for it, even though thinking is built upon them not in a habitual nor rational way according to the author's explanation, which is the dependence of the ruling on its evidence.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of a definition of the term 'asl' (origin/foundation) in usul al-fiqh. The commentator is discussing why defining 'asl' as 'that which is needed' (muhtāj ilayh) is defective because it lacks coextensiveness (intirād) -- it includes things that are not called 'asl' while excluding some things that are. The author first clarifies that the definition is nominal (ismī), i.e., it defines a term by its linguistic meaning. He then argues that not everything needed is called 'asl'; only the material cause (mādda) is linguistically called 'asl'. He illustrates with the example of a bed: its material (wood) is called its 'asl', but the carpenter (efficient cause), the form, the purpose (sitting), and the conditions (tools, receptivity) are all 'needed' but not 'asl'. After establishing this, he raises four objections (wujūh) against his own critique: First, coextensiveness is not a necessary condition for all definitions, especially in lexicography; one may define a term just enough to distinguish it from a specific other term, as in distinguishing asl from farʿ. Second, the word 'asl' can apply to the efficient cause because the effect depends on it, so it fits the meaning of 'building upon'. Third, the author's previous statements in the chapter on metaphor imply that everything needed is an asl. Fourth, in the definition of thinking (fikr) as 'arrangement of known matters', those known matters are called asl even though the building is not habitual or rational, thus challenging the condition of building being directly causal. This is a dense usul al-fiqh discussion typical of Hanafi works, engaging with Aristotelian causal categories (material, formal, efficient, final, conditional) to test a definition.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-aṣl): The material cause (mādda) that serves as the foundation for something else, as linguistically applied to the material of a bed.
المحتاج إليه (al-muḥtāj ilayh): That which is needed by something for its existence, potentially including five causal categories.
الاطراد (al-iṭṭirād): Coextensiveness of a definition—applying to all members of the defined set and no others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the five causes is linguistically called 'asl'?
A) Efficient cause
B) Material cause
C) Final cause
D) Conditional cause

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the coextensiveness of a definition is a key test, but it is not absolute—especially for nominal definitions where partial differentiation may suffice.

Critiquing the Definition of Asl: The Test of Tard
Critiques the definition of asl as mahtaj ilayh using tard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to critically evaluate the definition of 'asl' in Hanafi usul by applying the criteria of tard (comprehensiveness) and identifying why only material cause qualifies as asl.

Core Idea
The Hanafi definition of asl restricts it to material cause; defining it broadly as 'mahtaj ilayh' fails the test of tard.

In this passage, we examine a fundamental usul exercise: the critique of a definition. The author tests the claim that 'asl' means 'that which is needed' (mahtaj ilayh) and finds it deficient because it includes categories like efficient cause and final cause, which are not called 'asl' in Arabic. By understanding this critique, you will learn how Hanafi scholars ensure precision in legal terminology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition being critiqued
The passage examines the definition: 'asl is everything that is needed by something else' (mahtaj ilayh). This is a broad definition that would cover multiple types of causes.
2
List the five categories of mahtaj ilayh
The passage explains that five types satisfy 'mahtaj ilayh': material cause, formal cause, efficient cause, final cause, and condition (e.g., tools).
These correspond to the Aristotelian causes but adapted to Islamic legal theory.
3
Apply the linguistic test
For each category, ask: 'Is this category called asl in the Arabic language?' The passage asserts that asl is only used for material cause (maddah).
Example: The wood of a bed is its asl, not the carpenter or the form.
4
Assess comprehensiveness (tard)
Since the definition 'mahtaj ilayh' includes categories not called asl, it is not muttarid (comprehensive) — it fails to exclude non-instances (dukhul al-ghayr).
Tard is a key condition for an ideal definition in usul, but incomplete definitions are also accepted for partial distinction.
5
Understand the Hanafi resolution
The Hanafi position restricts asl to material cause, but acknowledges that incomplete definitions (ta'rifat naqisah) can still be useful for distinguishing between similar concepts (e.g., asl vs. far').
The passage includes objections and responses, showing the depth of the debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ج ريَانِ الْأَصَالَةِ وَالتَّبْعِيَّةِ مِن الجَانِبَينِ يَدُلُّ عَلَىٰ أَنَّ كُلَّ مُحتَاجِ إِلَيْهِ فَهُوَ أَصَلَّ وَرَابِعُهَا أَنَّا إِذَا قُلْنَا الفِكرُ تَرتِيبُ أُمُورٍ مَعْلُومَةٍ فَلَا شَكَ أَنَّ الْأُمُورَ المَعْلُومَةَ مَادَّةٌ للفكرِ وَأَصل لَهُ مَعَ أَنَّ ابْتِنَاءَ الفكرِ عَلَيْهَا لَيسَ حَسْبا رَوَارَ وَلَا عَقلِيًّا بِتَفسِيرِ المُصَنِّفِ وَهُوَ تَرَتُبُ الحُكمِ عَلَى دَلِيلِهِ . From the two sides [of asalah and tab'iyyah] indicates that everything that is needed is an asl. Fourth: When we say thought is the arrangement of known matters, there is no doubt that the known matters are a material for thought and an asl for it, even though the dependence of thought on them is neither sensory nor rational according to the author's interpretation, and it is the relation of the ruling to its evidence. Translation: His statement 'there is no doubt' etc. because this is to express that the word asl is coined in the language for a composite i'tibari thing which is described with the attribute of 'bina 'ala al-ghayr' or 'ihtiyaj al-ghayr ilayh'. And the definition being non-mutjarrad is corruptive for the definition, be it ismi or ghair ismi. So the summary is that defining asl with mahtaj ilayh is not muttarid because it is not true that every mahtaj ilayh is an asl. Because that towards which something relates is either included in the thing or excluded. In the first case, the existence of the thing is either potential (bil-quwwa) which is material cause, or actual (bil-fi'l) which is formal cause, like the form of a bed for the bed. In the second case, if the thing proceeds from it, it is efficient cause, like the carpenter for the bed; if the thing proceeds because of it, it is final cause, like sitting on the bed; if it is a condition, like the carpenter's tools and the wood being suitable. So these are five types of mahtaj ilayh. The word asl is not applied in language except to one of them, namely the material, like it is said 'the asl of this bed is such-and-such wood'. The other four are true as mahtaj ilayh but not true as asl, so this definition is not mmani' min dukhul al-ghayr (comprehensive). And there are objections from several aspects: First objection: The condition of tard in every definition, especially in ismi definition, is disputed. Indeed, the books of lexicography are filled with interpretations that are more general than the meanings of the words. Indeed, the verifiers have stated that for incomplete definitions it is permissible that they be important [in distinguishing] from some others. Indeed, the purpose sometimes is to distinguish from a specific thing, so one suffices with something that gives distinction, like when distinguishing between asl and far', the first is defined as mahtaj ilayh and the second as mahtaj. Second objection: That the word asl does not apply to efficient cause is disputed. How can that be when the act depends on it and is attributed to it, and there is no meaning of dependence except this. Third objection: Indeed, the author's statement in the chapter on majaz about jaryan of asalah and tab'iyyah indicates that every mahtaj ilayh is asl. Fourth objection: When we say thought is the arrangement of known matters, there is no doubt that known matters are material for thought and asl for it, even though the dependence of thought on them is neither sensory nor rational according to the author's interpretation, and it is the relation of the ruling to its evidence. Why the definition of asl is ismi? His statement 'la shak': This is the first part of the commentary's expression. Here the commentator explained why the definition of asl is ismi: because the word asl is coined in the language for a composite i'tibari thing with an added attribute, namely 'bina al-ghayr 'alayh' or 'ihtiyaj al-ghayr ilayh', and any definition that involves an i'tibari essence is an ismi definition. His statement 'fahadha': This is the second part. Here the commentator objected to the author. The gist of the objection is that the author's saying 'the definition of asl is ismi' was unnecessary because tard and 'aks are conditions for real definitions as well. Response: It may be that the author just added knowledge and did not mention it as a condition, so there is no objection. His statement 'fi al-jumla': This is the third part where the commentator clarifies the author's objection to Sahib al-Mahsul: that defining asl with mahtaj ilayh is incorrect because material cause, formal cause, efficient cause, final cause, and instrumental condition all satisfy 'mahtaj ilayh', but asl is only said of material, so the definition includes what is not intended, hence not muttarid. The rest of the definition has passed in the text.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the definition of 'asl' (origin/source) in usul al-fiqh. The author begins by presenting the argument that everything that is needed (mahtaj ilayh) is an asl, but then critiques this definition. The commentary explains that the word 'asl' is coined in language for a composite i'tibari (conceptual) thing that is characterized by either being a foundation upon which something else is built (bina al-ghayr 'alayh) or being something that something else needs (ihtiyaj al-ghayr ilayh). The key point is that the definition of asl as 'mahtaj ilayh' is not comprehensive (ghayr muttarid) because it applies to five categories: material cause, formal cause, efficient cause, final cause, and condition. However, the term 'asl' in language is only applied to the material cause (maddah). For example, the asl of a bed is its wood, not the carpenter or the form. Therefore, the definition fails to exclude non-examples (dakhul al-ghayr). The passage then lists four objections to this definition, including arguments about the necessity of tard (comprehensiveness) in definitions, the application of asl to efficient cause, implications from other parts of the text, and the relationship of thought to known matters. The commentator concludes by noting that the definition of asl is ismi (nominal) and defends the author against objections. This passage is essential for understanding how Hanafi usul scholars critically examine definitions and ensure they are precise and comprehensive.

Key Terms
أصل (asl): The material cause (maddah) that is the foundation of something and that something depends on; in language, it is only applied to the material cause, not to efficient, formal, final causes or conditions.
محتاج إليه (mahtaj ilayh): That which is needed by something else; it includes five categories: material cause, formal cause, efficient cause, final cause, and condition.
طرد (tard): Comprehensiveness of a definition: the definition must apply to all instances of the defined term (comprehensive).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in the passage, which of the following is NOT considered an 'asl' (origin) in the strict sense?
A) The wood used to make a bed
B) The carpenter who makes a bed
C) The form of a bed
D) The bed itself (as the product)

Key Takeaway
The precise Hanafi definition of asl as material cause arises from a rigorous critique of broader definitions using the condition of tard.
