Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
The Twelve-Fold Division and the Hasil al-Masdar Solution
Commentary on the division of ma'yati bih al-mukallaf into act and abandonment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the twelve-fold division of legal values and apply the distinction between ma'na masdari and hasil al-masdar to resolve the tautology objection.

Core Idea
The division of legal values into act and abandonment is saved from tautology by interpreting 'act' as hasil al-masdar, not the abstract verbal meaning.

The commentator presents a twelve-fold classification of legal values by splitting each of the six types into act and abandonment. An immediate objection arises: this divides a thing into itself, and the verbal meaning is a mental construct. The answer lies in the linguistic concept of hasil al-masdar, which is externally real.

Guided Path
1
List the six original types
Identify the six types of legal values mentioned: wajib, mandub, mubah, haram, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi.
2
Understand the twelve-fold division
For each type, there is an act (fi'l) and an abandonment (tark), resulting in 12 distinct categories.
The commentator explicitly lists them: (1) act of wajib, (2) abandonment of wajib, etc.
3
Recognize the tautology objection
Dividing 'ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf' into act and non-act seems to divide a thing into itself, because 'act' is both the thing being divided and one of the divisions.
This is the first objection: انقسام الشيء إلى نفسه وإلى غيره.
4
Apply the distinction between verbal meaning and verbal noun
The term 'act' in the division refers to hasil al-masdar (the external form acquired by the doer), not to ma'na masdari (the abstract occurrence).
Thus, the division is between a external form (hasil al-masdar) and its non-existence, which are two distinct things.
5
Verify the solution
The second objection (that verbal meanings are non-existent) also collapses because hasil al-masdar exists externally.
Example: salat – the act of praying (ma'na masdari) is conceptual, but the state of being in prayer (hasil al-masdar) is real.

جواب:۔ سنت اور نفل مندوب میں داخل ہیں لہذا ان کے ذکر کرنے کی ضرورت ہی نہیں ہے۔ اعتراض:- مندوب میں نفل تو داخل ہو سکتا ہے کہ جیسے مندوب کے فعل پر ثواب ہوتا ہے اور ترک پر سزا نہیں ہوتی ایسے ہی نقل کے فعل پر تو اب ہوتا ہے اور ترک پر سزا نہیں ہوتی لیکن سنت اس طرح نہیں ہے کیونکہ سنت کے فعل پر ثواب اور ترک پر عقاب ہوتا ہے تو سنت کو مندوب میں داخل کرنا درست نہ ہوا۔
جواب: سنت کو مندوب میں داخل کرنا درست ہے کیونکہ اس کا تارک سزا کا ستحق نہیں ہوتا بلکہ صرف سلامت کا مستحق ہوتا ہے۔ ولكل منها : یہ شرح کی مہارت کا گیارہواں حصہ ہے یہاں سے یہ ذکر کیا گیا ہیکہ وجہ مصر میں جو چھ قسمیں مذکور ہیں ان میں سے ہر ایک کی دو طرفیں ہیں ، فعل، یعنی معنی مصدری کو واقع کرنا اور ، ترک ، یعنی معنی مصدری کو واقع نہ کرنا تو اس لحاظ سے کل بارہ اقسام ہو گئیں (۱) فعل واجب (۲) ترک واجب (۳) فعل مندوب (۴) ترک مندوب (۵) فعل مباح (۶) ترک مبارح (۷) فعل حرام (۸) ترک حرام (۹) فعل مکروہ تحریمی (۱۰) ترک مکروہ تحریمی (۱۱) فعل مکروہ تنزیہی (۱۲) ترک مکروہ تنز ہیں۔
فعل اور ترک سے مراد حاصل مصدر ہے
والمراد بمایاتی بالمتکلف : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا بارہواں حصہ ہے غرض: اعتراض کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض:- وجہ حصر میں شارح نے مایاتی بہ المکلف (واجب، مندوب وغیرہ) کو طرف فعل اور طرف ترک کی طرف منقسم کیا ہے یہ درست نہیں ہے اس میں دو خرابیاں لازم آتی ہیں (۱) اس سے انقسام اشی الی نفسہ لازم آتا ہے وہ اس طرح کہ مایا تی یہ المکلف بھی فعل ہے اور یہ مقسم کے درجہ میں ہے اور اس کی تقسیم کی ہے فعل اور عدم فعل کی طرف ۔ اور فعل سے مراد معنی مصدری یعنی ایقاع ہے اب ایقاع کی تقسیم ہوگی ایقاع کی طرف اور یہ انقسام المشع الى نفسہ والی غیرہ ہے جو باطل ہے (۲) دوسری خرابی یہ لازم آتی ہے کہ جب مالیاتی یہ المکلف سے مراد فعل ہے اور یہ ایقاع کے معنی میں ہے تو یہ معنی مصدری ہوا اور جتنے بھی معانی مصدر یہ ہیں یہ امور اعتبار یہ اور امور انتزاعیہ ہیں اور امور اعتبار یہ خارج میں موجود نہیں ہوتے بلکہ خارج میں تو صرف فاعل اور مفصول موجود ہوتے ہیں جیسے مثلاً ، اکل، مصدر ہے تو خارج میں آکل اور ماکول تو پائے جاتے ہیں لیکن ان کا معنی مصدری یعنی ایقاع اکل نہیں پایا جاتا تو جب معلی مصدری خارج میں نہیں پایا جاتا تو مالیاتی بہ المکلف کو فعل سے کیسے تعبیر کر سکتے ہیں جبکہ ملیاتی بہ المکلف تو خارج میں پایا جاتا ہے۔
جواب: مصدر میں دو چیزیں ہوتی ہیں (۱) معنی مصدری جو واضح ہے (۲) حاصل مصدر جس سے مراد وہ ہیئت ہے جو فاعل کو معنی مصدری کو واقع کرتے وقت حاصل ہوتی ہے جیسے صلوۃ ، مصدر ہے اس کا معنی مصدری تو نماز پڑھنا ہے لیکن اس کا حاصل مصدر وہ کیفیت ہے جو مصلی کو نماز پڑھتے وقت حاصل ہوتی ہے اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ معنی مصدری خارج میں نہیں پایا جاتا لیکن حاصل مصدر خارج میں پایا جاتا ہے، اب جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم نے فعل جو مقسم کے درجہ میں ہے اس سے حاصل مصدر مرا دلیا ہے جو خارج میں پایا جاتا ہے لہر دوسری خرابی لازم نہیں آئے گی اسی طرح جب فعل مقسم سے مراد حاصل مصدر ہے اور وہ فعل جواس کی قسم بنتا ہے اس سے مراد معنی مصدری ہے تو پہلی خرابی یعنی انقسام الشی الی نفسہ والی غیرہ بھی لازم نہیں آئے گی۔
والامور المذکورہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیر ہواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض: ایک اعتراض کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض: مذکورہ امور (واجب، مندوب وغیرہ) کو آپ نے فعل اور ترک کی طرف تقسیم کیا ہے یہ درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ وجوب حرمت وغیرہ افعال کے اوصاف سے نہیں اور ترک تو فعل نہیں ہے۔
جواب:۔ آپ کی بات ٹھیک ہے کہ یہ امور عام طور پر اوصاف فعل واقع ہوتے ہیں ہم اس کا انکار نہیں کرتے لیکن بعض اوقات ان کا اطلاق ترک پر بھی ہوتا ہے اور یہ ترک کی صفات بھی بنتی ہیں کہا جاتا ہے عدم مباشرة الحرام واجب ،، اور ، عدم مباشرة الواجب حرام اب یہاں واجب عدم کی صفت بن رہا ہے اور عدم ترک ہی کا نام ہے معلوم ہوا کہ وجوب وغیرہ کا ترک پر بھی اطلاق ہوتا ہے۔
ترک کی تفسیر عدم فعل کے ساتھ کیوں کی؟
و انما فسر الترک بعدم الفعل :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چودہواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض شارح: اعتراض کا جواب دیتا ہے اعتراض:۔ مصنف نے ترک کی تفسیر ،، عدم افعل ،، کے ساتھ کی ہے ، کف النفس کے ساتھ کیوں نہیں کی حالانکہ کف
لنفس بھی ترک ہی ہے۔
جواب سے پہلے ایک مقدمہ سمجھیں ۔
مقدمہ :۔ عدم الفعل اور کت النفس میں فرق ہے عدم الفعل کا مطلب ہے فعل کو نہ کرنا چاہے اسکے اسباب ومواقع ہوں یا نہ
Answer: The sunnah and nafil are included in mandub, so there is no need to mention them. Objection: Nafil can be included in mandub because doing a mandub brings reward and leaving it brings no punishment, similarly doing a nafil brings reward and leaving it brings no punishment. But the sunnah is not like this because doing the sunnah brings reward and leaving it brings punishment, so including sunnah in mandub is not correct. Answer: It is correct to include sunnah in mandub because the one who abandons it does not deserve punishment but only deserves safety. And for each of them: This is the eleventh part of the commentary. From here it is mentioned that the six types mentioned in the reason for restriction each have two sides: act, i.e., performing the verbal meaning, and abandonment, i.e., not performing the verbal meaning. So from this perspective, there become twelve types: (1) act of wajib, (2) abandonment of wajib, (3) act of mandub, (4) abandonment of mandub, (5) act of mubah, (6) abandonment of mubah, (7) act of haram, (8) abandonment of haram, (9) act of makruh tahrimi, (10) abandonment of makruh tahrimi, (11) act of makruh tanzihi, (12) abandonment of makruh tanzihi. What is meant by act and abandonment is the verbal noun. And 'al-murad bi ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf': This is the twelfth part of the commentary. Purpose: To answer an objection. Objection: In the reason for restriction, the commentator divided ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf (wajib, mandub, etc.) into act and abandonment. This is not correct because it entails two problems: (1) It entails dividing a thing into itself, because ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf is also an act and it is the thing being divided, and it is divided into act and non-act. And what is meant by act is the verbal meaning, i.e., occurrence. So the occurrence would be divided into occurrence, and this is dividing a thing into itself and something else, which is invalid. (2) The second problem is that when ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf is meant as act, and it is in the sense of occurrence, then it is the verbal meaning. And all verbal meanings are matters of consideration and abstract matters, and matters of consideration do not exist externally. Rather, externally only the doer and the object exist. For example, 'akl' is a verbal noun; externally, the eater and the eaten exist, but their verbal meaning, i.e., the occurrence of eating, does not exist. So when the verbal meaning does not exist externally, how can ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf, which does exist externally, be expressed as an act? Answer: The verbal noun has two things: (1) the verbal meaning, which is clear, and (2) the verbal noun, which refers to the form that the doer acquires when performing the verbal meaning. For example, 'salat' is a verbal noun; its verbal meaning is 'praying', but its verbal noun is the state that the worshipper acquires when praying. The second point is that the verbal meaning does not exist externally, but the verbal noun does exist externally. Now the conclusion of the answer is that we intended by 'act' which is the thing being divided the verbal noun, which exists externally. Therefore the second problem does not arise. Similarly, when by 'act' (the thing being divided) we mean the verbal noun, and by the act that becomes its division we mean the verbal meaning, then the first problem, i.e., dividing a thing into itself and something else, also does not arise. And 'al-umur al-madhkurah': This is the thirteenth part of the commentary. Purpose: To answer an objection. Objection: You have divided the mentioned matters (wajib, mandub, etc.) into act and abandonment. This is not correct because obligation, prohibition, etc. are attributes of acts, and abandonment is not an act. Answer: Your statement is correct that these matters are generally attributes of acts; we do not deny that. But sometimes they are also applied to abandonment, and they become attributes of abandonment. It is said, 'Not directly committing the haram is wajib,' and 'Not directly committing the wajib is haram.' Here wajib is an attribute of non-existence, and non-existence is the name of abandonment. So it is known that obligation, etc. are also applied to abandonment. Why is tark interpreted as adam al-fi'l? And 'innama fussira al-tark bi 'adam al-fi'l': This is the fourteenth part of the commentary. Purpose: The commentator answers an objection. Objection: The author interpreted tark as 'adam al-fi'l. Why did he not interpret it as kaff al-nafs, even though kaff al-nafs is also a form of tark? Before the answer, understand a premise. Premise: There is a difference between 'adam al-fi'l and kaff al-nafs. 'Adam al-fi'l means not doing the act, whether its causes and occasions exist or not.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a previous matn, discussing the classification of the legal values (ahkam) into acts and abandonments. The commentator begins by addressing an objection regarding the inclusion of sunnah in mandub. The objector argued that mandub includes nafil but not sunnah because abandoning sunnah brings punishment. The commentator responds that the one who abandons sunnah does not deserve punishment but only safety, thus sunnah can be included in mandub. Then the commentator introduces the twelve-fold division: each of the six types (wajib, mandub, mubah, haram, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi) has an act and abandonment aspect. The term 'act' in this division means the verbal noun (hasil al-masdar), not the verbal meaning (ma'na masdari). Next, an objection is raised: dividing 'ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf' (the actions of the legally responsible person) into act and non-act leads to dividing a thing into itself (since the action itself is an act) and also the verbal meaning is a mental construct not existing externally. The commentator answers by distinguishing between the verbal meaning (ma'na masdari) which is an abstract concept, and the verbal noun (hasil al-masdar) which is the external form or quality that exists. When the commentator says 'act' in the division, he means the verbal noun (hasil al-masdar), which does exist externally. This avoids both problems: the division is not into itself, and the entity being divided exists externally. Then another objection: legal values like obligation and prohibition are attributes of acts, not of abandonment. The commentator responds that although generally these are attributes of acts, they can also apply to abandonment. For example, 'not directly committing haram is wajib' – here wajib qualifies the abandonment. Thus the division into act and abandonment is valid. Finally, the commentator addresses why tark (abandonment) is defined as 'adam al-fi'l (non-act) rather than kaff al-nafs (self-restraint). A premise is introduced: 'adam al-fi'l is simply not doing the act regardless of whether the means and occasions exist, while kaff al-nafs implies restraining oneself when the means are present. The passage breaks off mid-sentence, but the discussion likely continues to show that 'adam al-fi'l is more comprehensive.

Key Terms
معنى مصدري (ma'na masdari): The abstract meaning of a verbal noun, e.g., the occurrence of eating.
حاصل مصدر (hasil al-masdar): The external form or quality that the doer acquires when performing the action, e.g., the state of being in prayer.
تقسيم الشيء إلى نفسه (taqsim al-shay' ila nafsih): Dividing a thing into itself, a logical fallacy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key concept used to resolve the objection that the twelve-fold division involves 'dividing a thing into itself'?
A) The distinction between wajib and haram.
B) The concept of hasil al-masdar (external form of the verbal noun).
C) The inclusion of sunnah in mandub.
D) The definition of tark as kaff al-nafs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi division of legal values into act and abandonment is logically sound once 'act' is understood as the external result (hasil al-masdar) rather than the abstract verbal meaning.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
Legal Values as Attributes of Abandonment
Commentary on the division of ma'yati bih al-mukallaf into act and abandonment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that legal values can qualify abandonment and cite the example 'not committing haram is wajib'.

Core Idea
For the Hanafi school, wajib and haram can describe abandonment, as seen in the phrase 'Not directly committing haram is wajib'.

A critic argues that legal values like obligation and prohibition are inherently linked to positive acts, not to the absence of action. The Hanafi commentator counters by pointing to sharia usage where abandonment is described as wajib or haram. This illustrates that legal values can be attributes of both act and abandonment.

Guided Path
1
State the objection
The objector argues that legal values (wajib, mandub, etc.) are attributes (awṣāf) of acts only; abandonment is not an act, so these values cannot apply to it.
The objection is found in the thirteenth part of the commentary: 'وجوب حرمت وغیرہ افعال کے اوصاف سے نہیں اور ترک تو فعل نہیں ہے۔'
2
Analyze the Hanafi response
The commentator agrees that generally these values qualify acts, but shows that they sometimes apply to abandonment as well.
He says: 'آپ کی بات ٹھیک ہے کہ یہ امور عام طور پر اوصاف فعل واقع ہوتے ہیں' but then provides counterexamples.
3
Identify the evidence
The commentator cites two examples: 'عدم مباشرة الحرام واجب' (not directly committing haram is wajib) and 'عدم مباشرة الواجب حرام' (not directly committing wajib is haram).
In these phrases, 'wajib' and 'haram' describe 'adam' (non-existence), which is a form of tark.
4
Understand the implication
Since 'adam' is the name of tark, and these values qualify 'adam', it follows that legal values can be attributes of abandonment.
Thus, the division of legal values into act and abandonment is valid because the values themselves can apply to both.
5
Conclude the Hanafi view
The Hanafi position is that legal values like wajib, haram, etc. can qualify abandonment, supporting the twelve-fold classification.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence): the twelve-fold division is accepted.

جواب:۔ سنت اور نفل مندوب میں داخل ہیں لہذا ان کے ذکر کرنے کی ضرورت ہی نہیں ہے۔ اعتراض:- مندوب میں نفل تو داخل ہو سکتا ہے کہ جیسے مندوب کے فعل پر ثواب ہوتا ہے اور ترک پر سزا نہیں ہوتی ایسے ہی نقل کے فعل پر تو اب ہوتا ہے اور ترک پر سزا نہیں ہوتی لیکن سنت اس طرح نہیں ہے کیونکہ سنت کے فعل پر ثواب اور ترک پر عقاب ہوتا ہے تو سنت کو مندوب میں داخل کرنا درست نہ ہوا۔
جواب: سنت کو مندوب میں داخل کرنا درست ہے کیونکہ اس کا تارک سزا کا ستحق نہیں ہوتا بلکہ صرف سلامت کا مستحق ہوتا ہے۔ ولكل منها : یہ شرح کی مہارت کا گیارہواں حصہ ہے یہاں سے یہ ذکر کیا گیا ہیکہ وجہ مصر میں جو چھ قسمیں مذکور ہیں ان میں سے ہر ایک کی دو طرفیں ہیں ، فعل، یعنی معنی مصدری کو واقع کرنا اور ، ترک ، یعنی معنی مصدری کو واقع نہ کرنا تو اس لحاظ سے کل بارہ اقسام ہو گئیں (۱) فعل واجب (۲) ترک واجب (۳) فعل مندوب (۴) ترک مندوب (۵) فعل مباح (۶) ترک مبارح (۷) فعل حرام (۸) ترک حرام (۹) فعل مکروہ تحریمی (۱۰) ترک مکروہ تحریمی (۱۱) فعل مکروہ تنزیہی (۱۲) ترک مکروہ تنز ہیں۔

جواب: مصدر میں دو چیزیں ہوتی ہیں (۱) معنی مصدری جو واضح ہے (۲) حاصل مصدر جس سے مراد وہ ہیئت ہے جو فاعل کو معنی مصدری کو واقع کرتے وقت حاصل ہوتی ہے جیسے صلوۃ ، مصدر ہے اس کا معنی مصدری تو نماز پڑھنا ہے لیکن اس کا حاصل مصدر وہ کیفیت ہے جو مصلی کو نماز پڑھتے وقت حاصل ہوتی ہے اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ معنی مصدری خارج میں نہیں پایا جاتا لیکن حاصل مصدر خارج میں پایا جاتا ہے، اب جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم نے فعل جو مقسم کے درجہ میں ہے اس سے حاصل مصدر مرا دلیا ہے جو خارج میں پایا جاتا ہے لہر دوسری خرابی لازم نہیں آئے گی اسی طرح جب فعل مقسم سے مراد حاصل مصدر ہے اور وہ فعل جواس کی قسم بنتا ہے اس سے مراد معنی مصدری ہے تو پہلی خرابی یعنی انقسام الشی الی نفسہ والی غیرہ بھی لازم نہیں آئے گی۔
والامور المذکورہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیر ہواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض: ایک اعتراض کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض: مذکورہ امور (واجب، مندوب وغیرہ) کو آپ نے فعل اور ترک کی طرف تقسیم کیا ہے یہ درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ وجوب حرمت وغیرہ افعال کے اوصاف سے نہیں اور ترک تو فعل نہیں ہے۔
جواب:۔ آپ کی بات ٹھیک ہے کہ یہ امور عام طور پر اوصاف فعل واقع ہوتے ہیں ہم اس کا انکار نہیں کرتے لیکن بعض اوقات ان کا اطلاق ترک پر بھی ہوتا ہے اور یہ ترک کی صفات بھی بنتی ہیں کہا جاتا ہے عدم مباشرة الحرام واجب ،، اور ، عدم مباشرة الواجب حرام اب یہاں واجب عدم کی صفت بن رہا ہے اور عدم ترک ہی کا نام ہے معلوم ہوا کہ وجوب وغیرہ کا ترک پر بھی اطلاق ہوتا ہے۔
ترک کی تفسیر عدم فعل کے ساتھ کیوں کی؟
و انما فسر الترک بعدم الفعل :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چودہواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض شارح: اعتراض کا جواب دیتا ہے اعتراض:۔ مصنف نے ترک کی تفسیر ،، عدم افعل ،، کے ساتھ کی ہے ، کف النفس کے ساتھ کیوں نہیں کی حالانکہ کف
لنفس بھی ترک ہی ہے۔
جواب سے پہلے ایک مقدمہ سمجھیں ۔
مقدمہ :۔ عدم الفعل اور کت النفس میں فرق ہے عدم الفعل کا مطلب ہے فعل کو نہ کرنا چاہے اسکے اسباب ومواقع ہوں یا نہ
Answer: The sunnah and nafil are included in mandub, so there is no need to mention them. Objection: Nafil can be included in mandub because doing a mandub brings reward and leaving it brings no punishment, similarly doing a nafil brings reward and leaving it brings no punishment. But the sunnah is not like this because doing the sunnah brings reward and leaving it brings punishment, so including sunnah in mandub is not correct. Answer: It is correct to include sunnah in mandub because the one who abandons it does not deserve punishment but only deserves safety. And for each of them: This is the eleventh part of the commentary. From here it is mentioned that the six types mentioned in the reason for restriction each have two sides: act, i.e., performing the verbal meaning, and abandonment, i.e., not performing the verbal meaning. So from this perspective, there become twelve types: (1) act of wajib, (2) abandonment of wajib, (3) act of mandub, (4) abandonment of mandub, (5) act of mubah, (6) abandonment of mubah, (7) act of haram, (8) abandonment of haram, (9) act of makruh tahrimi, (10) abandonment of makruh tahrimi, (11) act of makruh tanzihi, (12) abandonment of makruh tanzihi. What is meant by act and abandonment is the verbal noun. And 'al-murad bi ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf': This is the twelfth part of the commentary. Purpose: To answer an objection. Objection: In the reason for restriction, the commentator divided ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf (wajib, mandub, etc.) into act and abandonment. This is not correct because it entails two problems: (1) It entails dividing a thing into itself, because ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf is also an act and it is the thing being divided, and it is divided into act and non-act. And what is meant by act is the verbal meaning, i.e., occurrence. So the occurrence would be divided into occurrence, and this is dividing a thing into itself and something else, which is invalid. (2) The second problem is that when ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf is meant as act, and it is in the sense of occurrence, then it is the verbal meaning. And all verbal meanings are matters of consideration and abstract matters, and matters of consideration do not exist externally. Rather, externally only the doer and the object exist. For example, 'akl' is a verbal noun; externally, the eater and the eaten exist, but their verbal meaning, i.e., the occurrence of eating, does not exist. So when the verbal meaning does not exist externally, how can ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf, which does exist externally, be expressed as an act? Answer: The verbal noun has two things: (1) the verbal meaning, which is clear, and (2) the verbal noun, which refers to the form that the doer acquires when performing the verbal meaning. For example, 'salat' is a verbal noun; its verbal meaning is 'praying', but its verbal noun is the state that the worshipper acquires when praying. The second point is that the verbal meaning does not exist externally, but the verbal noun does exist externally. Now the conclusion of the answer is that we intended by 'act' which is the thing being divided the verbal noun, which exists externally. Therefore the second problem does not arise. Similarly, when by 'act' (the thing being divided) we mean the verbal noun, and by the act that becomes its division we mean the verbal meaning, then the first problem, i.e., dividing a thing into itself and something else, also does not arise. And 'al-umur al-madhkurah': This is the thirteenth part of the commentary. Purpose: To answer an objection. Objection: You have divided the mentioned matters (wajib, mandub, etc.) into act and abandonment. This is not correct because obligation, prohibition, etc. are attributes of acts, and abandonment is not an act. Answer: Your statement is correct that these matters are generally attributes of acts; we do not deny that. But sometimes they are also applied to abandonment, and they become attributes of abandonment. It is said, 'Not directly committing the haram is wajib,' and 'Not directly committing the wajib is haram.' Here wajib is an attribute of non-existence, and non-existence is the name of abandonment. So it is known that obligation, etc. are also applied to abandonment. Why is tark interpreted as adam al-fi'l? And 'innama fussira al-tark bi 'adam al-fi'l': This is the fourteenth part of the commentary. Purpose: The commentator answers an objection. Objection: The author interpreted tark as 'adam al-fi'l. Why did he not interpret it as kaff al-nafs, even though kaff al-nafs is also a form of tark? Before the answer, understand a premise. Premise: There is a difference between 'adam al-fi'l and kaff al-nafs. 'Adam al-fi'l means not doing the act, whether its causes and occasions exist or not.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a previous matn, discussing the classification of the legal values (ahkam) into acts and abandonments. The commentator begins by addressing an objection regarding the inclusion of sunnah in mandub. The objector argued that mandub includes nafil but not sunnah because abandoning sunnah brings punishment. The commentator responds that the one who abandons sunnah does not deserve punishment but only safety, thus sunnah can be included in mandub. Then the commentator introduces the twelve-fold division: each of the six types (wajib, mandub, mubah, haram, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi) has an act and abandonment aspect. The term 'act' in this division means the verbal noun (hasil al-masdar), not the verbal meaning (ma'na masdari). Next, an objection is raised: dividing 'ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf' (the actions of the legally responsible person) into act and non-act leads to dividing a thing into itself (since the action itself is an act) and also the verbal meaning is a mental construct not existing externally. The commentator answers by distinguishing between the verbal meaning (ma'na masdari) which is an abstract concept, and the verbal noun (hasil al-masdar) which is the external form or quality that exists. When the commentator says 'act' in the division, he means the verbal noun (hasil al-masdar), which does exist externally. This avoids both problems: the division is not into itself, and the entity being divided exists externally. Then another objection: legal values like obligation and prohibition are attributes of acts, not of abandonment. The commentator responds that although generally these are attributes of acts, they can also apply to abandonment. For example, 'not directly committing haram is wajib' – here wajib qualifies the abandonment. Thus the division into act and abandonment is valid. Finally, the commentator addresses why tark (abandonment) is defined as 'adam al-fi'l (non-act) rather than kaff al-nafs (self-restraint). A premise is introduced: 'adam al-fi'l is simply not doing the act regardless of whether the means and occasions exist, while kaff al-nafs implies restraining oneself when the means are present. The passage breaks off mid-sentence, but the discussion likely continues to show that 'adam al-fi'l is more comprehensive.

Key Terms
عدم مباشرة (adam mubashara): Non-commission, not directly doing an action.
وصف (wasf): Attribute or quality, e.g., wajib is an attribute of an act or abandonment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What evidence does the commentator provide to show that legal values can apply to abandonment?
A) The inclusion of sunnah in mandub.
B) The twelve-fold list of acts and abandonments.
C) The phrases 'عدم مباشرة الحرام واجب' and 'عدم مباشرة الواجب حرام'.
D) The definition of tark as kaff al-nafs.

Key Takeaway
Legal values (wajib, haram, etc.) can describe abandonment, as shown by sharia usage, thus validating the twelve-fold division.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Defining Tark: Adam al-Fi'l vs. Kaff al-Nafs
Commentary on the division of ma'yati bih al-mukallaf into act and abandonment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'adam al-fi'l and kaff al-nafs as definitions of tark and explain why the commentator prefers the former.

Core Idea
Tark is defined as non-performance (adam al-fi'l) because it is broader than self-restraint, covering cases where the means are absent.

The author of the matn defined tark as 'adam al-fi'l, prompting an objection: why not define it as kaff al-nafs, which is also a form of abandonment? The commentator sets up a premise to show that 'adam al-fi'l is more comprehensive, including both voluntary restraint and involuntary non-action.

Guided Path
1
Note the definition in the matn
The matn (base text) defined tark (abandonment) as 'adam al-fi'l (non-act).
This is stated in the passage: 'ترک کی تفسیر عدم فعل کے ساتھ کی'
2
Formulate the objection
The objector asks: Why is tark defined as 'adam al-fi'l instead of kaff al-nafs (self-restraint)? After all, kaff al-nafs is also a type of tark.
The objector acknowledges that kaff al-nafs is a form of abandonment, so it could be a candidate definition.
3
Understand the premise
The commentator introduces a premise: 'Adam al-fi'l means not doing the act whether its causes and occasions exist or not. Kaff al-nafs means restraining oneself when the causes and occasions for the act are present.
The passage states: 'عدم الفعل کا مطلب ہے فعل کو نہ کرنا چاہے اسکے اسباب ومواقع ہوں یا نہ'
4
Recognize the commentator's reasoning
Since 'adam al-fi'l covers both cases (with or without ability/means), it is more comprehensive and suitable as a definition of tark. Kaff al-nafs is only applicable when the person has the ability to act.
The commentator implies that the broader definition avoids complications.
5
Apply the definition
In legal reasoning, tark is defined as mere non-act, so that rulings (like 'abandoning a wajib is haram') apply even if the person never had the intention or ability to perform the act.
For example, someone who never prayed due to ignorance still 'abandoned' prayer in the sense of 'adam al-fi'l.

جواب:۔ سنت اور نفل مندوب میں داخل ہیں لہذا ان کے ذکر کرنے کی ضرورت ہی نہیں ہے۔ اعتراض:- مندوب میں نفل تو داخل ہو سکتا ہے کہ جیسے مندوب کے فعل پر ثواب ہوتا ہے اور ترک پر سزا نہیں ہوتی ایسے ہی نقل کے فعل پر تو اب ہوتا ہے اور ترک پر سزا نہیں ہوتی لیکن سنت اس طرح نہیں ہے کیونکہ سنت کے فعل پر ثواب اور ترک پر عقاب ہوتا ہے تو سنت کو مندوب میں داخل کرنا درست نہ ہوا۔
جواب: سنت کو مندوب میں داخل کرنا درست ہے کیونکہ اس کا تارک سزا کا ستحق نہیں ہوتا بلکہ صرف سلامت کا مستحق ہوتا ہے۔ ولكل منها : یہ شرح کی مہارت کا گیارہواں حصہ ہے یہاں سے یہ ذکر کیا گیا ہیکہ وجہ مصر میں جو چھ قسمیں مذکور ہیں ان میں سے ہر ایک کی دو طرفیں ہیں ، فعل، یعنی معنی مصدری کو واقع کرنا اور ، ترک ، یعنی معنی مصدری کو واقع نہ کرنا تو اس لحاظ سے کل بارہ اقسام ہو گئیں (۱) فعل واجب (۲) ترک واجب (۳) فعل مندوب (۴) ترک مندوب (۵) فعل مباح (۶) ترک مبارح (۷) فعل حرام (۸) ترک حرام (۹) فعل مکروہ تحریمی (۱۰) ترک مکروہ تحریمی (۱۱) فعل مکروہ تنزیہی (۱۲) ترک مکروہ تنز ہیں۔

So from this perspective, there become twelve types: (1) act of wajib, (2) abandonment of wajib, (3) act of mandub, (4) abandonment of mandub, (5) act of mubah, (6) abandonment of mubah, (7) act of haram, (8) abandonment of haram, (9) act of makruh tahrimi, (10) abandonment of makruh tahrimi, (11) act of makruh tanzihi, (12) abandonment of makruh tanzihi. What is meant by act and abandonment is the verbal noun. And 'al-murad bi ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf': This is the twelfth part of the commentary. Purpose: To answer an objection. Objection: In the reason for restriction, the commentator divided ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf (wajib, mandub, etc.) into act and abandonment. This is not correct because it entails two problems: (1) It entails dividing a thing into itself, because ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf is also an act and it is the thing being divided, and it is divided into act and non-act. And what is meant by act is the verbal meaning, i.e., occurrence. So the occurrence would be divided into occurrence, and this is dividing a thing into itself and something else, which is invalid. (2) The second problem is that when ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf is meant as act, and it is in the sense of occurrence, then it is the verbal meaning. And all verbal meanings are matters of consideration and abstract matters, and matters of consideration do not exist externally. Rather, externally only the doer and the object exist. For example, 'akl' is a verbal noun; externally, the eater and the eaten exist, but their verbal meaning, i.e., the occurrence of eating, does not exist. So when the verbal meaning does not exist externally, how can ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf, which does exist externally, be expressed as an act? Answer: The verbal noun has two things: (1) the verbal meaning, which is clear, and (2) the verbal noun, which refers to the form that the doer acquires when performing the verbal meaning. For example, 'salat' is a verbal noun; its verbal meaning is 'praying', but its verbal noun is the state that the worshipper acquires when praying. The second point is that the verbal meaning does not exist externally, but the verbal noun does exist externally. Now the conclusion of the answer is that we intended by 'act' which is the thing being divided the verbal noun, which exists externally. Therefore the second problem does not arise. Similarly, when by 'act' (the thing being divided) we mean the verbal noun, and by the act that becomes its division we mean the verbal meaning, then the first problem, i.e., dividing a thing into itself and something else, also does not arise. And 'al-umur al-madhkurah': This is the thirteenth part of the commentary. Purpose: To answer an objection. Objection: You have divided the mentioned matters (wajib, mandub, etc.) into act and abandonment. This is not correct because obligation, prohibition, etc. are attributes of acts, and abandonment is not an act. Answer: Your statement is correct that these matters are generally attributes of acts; we do not deny that. But sometimes they are also applied to abandonment, and they become attributes of abandonment. It is said, 'Not directly committing the haram is wajib,' and 'Not directly committing the wajib is haram.' Here wajib is an attribute of non-existence, and non-existence is the name of abandonment. So it is known that obligation, etc. are also applied to abandonment. Why is tark interpreted as adam al-fi'l? And 'innama fussira al-tark bi 'adam al-fi'l': This is the fourteenth part of the commentary. Purpose: The commentator answers an objection. Objection: The author interpreted tark as 'adam al-fi'l. Why did he not interpret it as kaff al-nafs, even though kaff al-nafs is also a form of tark? Before the answer, understand a premise. Premise: There is a difference between 'adam al-fi'l and kaff al-nafs. 'Adam al-fi'l means not doing the act, whether its causes and occasions exist or not.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a previous matn, discussing the classification of the legal values (ahkam) into acts and abandonments. The commentator begins by addressing an objection regarding the inclusion of sunnah in mandub. The objector argued that mandub includes nafil but not sunnah because abandoning sunnah brings punishment. The commentator responds that the one who abandons sunnah does not deserve punishment but only safety, thus sunnah can be included in mandub. Then the commentator introduces the twelve-fold division: each of the six types (wajib, mandub, mubah, haram, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi) has an act and abandonment aspect. The term 'act' in this division means the verbal noun (hasil al-masdar), not the verbal meaning (ma'na masdari). Next, an objection is raised: dividing 'ma ya'ti bih al-mukallaf' (the actions of the legally responsible person) into act and non-act leads to dividing a thing into itself (since the action itself is an act) and also the verbal meaning is a mental construct not existing externally. The commentator answers by distinguishing between the verbal meaning (ma'na masdari) which is an abstract concept, and the verbal noun (hasil al-masdar) which is the external form or quality that exists. When the commentator says 'act' in the division, he means the verbal noun (hasil al-masdar), which does exist externally. This avoids both problems: the division is not into itself, and the entity being divided exists externally. Then another objection: legal values like obligation and prohibition are attributes of acts, not of abandonment. The commentator responds that although generally these are attributes of acts, they can also apply to abandonment. For example, 'not directly committing haram is wajib' – here wajib qualifies the abandonment. Thus the division into act and abandonment is valid. Finally, the commentator addresses why tark (abandonment) is defined as 'adam al-fi'l (non-act) rather than kaff al-nafs (self-restraint). A premise is introduced: 'adam al-fi'l is simply not doing the act regardless of whether the means and occasions exist, while kaff al-nafs implies restraining oneself when the means are present. The passage breaks off mid-sentence, but the discussion likely continues to show that 'adam al-fi'l is more comprehensive.

Key Terms
عدم الفعل (adam al-fi'l): Non-act, i.e., the absence of performing the act regardless of whether its causes exist.
كف النفس (kaff al-nafs): Self-restraint, i.e., intentionally refraining from an act despite having the ability to do it.
مقدمہ (muqaddimah): Premise, a foundational statement used in reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator define tark as 'adam al-fi'l rather than kaff al-nafs?
A) Because kaff al-nafs is a type of act, not abandonment.
B) Because 'adam al-fi'l is broader and covers non-performance even when the person lacks ability.
C) Because kaff al-nafs only applies to wajib acts.
D) Because the matn explicitly chose 'adam al-fi'l and the commentator follows it blindly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of tark as 'adam al-fi'l (non-act) is intentionally broad to cover all forms of non-performance, regardless of the presence of causes or ability.

Distinguishing Imkan Khas and Imkan 'Am in Hanafi Usul
Distinguishing two types of possibility and their application to jawaz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between imkan khas and imkan 'am and apply the distinction to interpret the term jawaz in usul al-fiqh contexts.

Core Idea
Possibility in Hanafi usul is twofold: specific (contingent) and general (broader). Jawaz here means modal possibility, not legal permissibility.

In this passage, the commentator introduces a crucial terminological distinction before addressing an objection about the meaning of jawaz. You will learn the precise definitions of imkan khas and imkan 'am, their subcategories, and why this distinction matters for interpreting the term jawaz in the earlier discussion of malha wa ma alayha.

Guided Path
1
Define imkan khas and imkan 'am
State the definitions from the text: imkan khas negates necessity from both existence and non-existence; imkan 'am only negates necessity from the opposite side.
2
Analyze the subcategories of imkan 'am
Work through the three levels: impossibility (when opposite side is existential and agreeing side necessary), necessity (when opposite side is non-existential and agreeing side necessary), and specific possibility (when agreeing side is not necessary).
3
Apply the distinction to jawaz
Understand why the author's use of jawaz as possibility raises the question of which type of imkan is meant. The objection hinges on this ambiguity.
The objection is not fully resolved in this passage; it sets up the framework.
4
Identify the objection
Note that the passage introduces an objection regarding the interpretation of jawaz in the fourth and fifth probabilities of malha wa ma alayha.
The answer is expected in subsequent sections.

والثانى ان المراد بالجواز :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا انیسواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض دوسری بحث کو بیان کرنا جو کہ ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے لیکن اس سے پہلے بطور تمہید ایک مقدمہ جانا ضروری ہے۔ مقدمہ:- امکان کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) امکان خاص (۲) امکان عام (۱) امکان خاص اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جانبین جانب وجود اور جانب عدم ) سے ضرورت کی نفی ہو یعنی نہ جانب وجود ضروری ہو اور نہ جانب عدم جیسے الانسان موجود بالا مکان الخاص اس کا مطلب ہے کہ انسان کا نہ وجود ضروری ہے نہ عدم (۲) امکان عام : اس کا مطلب ہے کہ جانب مخالف سے ضرورت کا سلب ہو یعنی جانب مخالف ضروری نہ ہو پھر اس کے تین درجے ہیں (۱) امتناع (۲) وجوب (۳) امکان خاص اور ان کی وضاحت یہ ہے کہ امکان عام کی جانب مخالف وجودی ہوگی یا عدمی اگر جانب مخالف وجودی ہو تو جانب موافق (عدم) ضروری ہوگی یا نہیں اگر ضروری ہو تو یہ امتناع ہے ( کیونکہ جانب موافق عدمی ہے اور عدم کا ضروری ہونا امتناع ہی ہے ) اور اگر جانب موافق (عدم ) ضروری نہیں تو یہ امکان خاص ہے ( کیونکہ اس کی جانب موافق اور جانب مخالف دونوں کا سلب ہو گیا ہے ) اور اگر جانب مخالف عدمی ہو تو پھر جانب موافق (وجود) ضروری ہوگی یا نہیں اگر ضروری ہو تو یہ وجوب ہے کیونکہ اس کا عدم ضروری نہیں اور وجود ضروری ہے اور یہ چیز واجب ہی میں ہوتی ہے ) اور اگر جانب موافق ( وجود ) ضروری نہیں تو یہ پھر امکان خاص ہے۔ اعتراض:۔ مصنف نے مالہا و ما علیہا کے چوتھے اور پانچویں احتمال میں مالبا سے مراد جواز لیا ہے اور یہ جواز بالاتفاق امکان کے معنی میں ہے اب سوال یہ ہے کہ اس امکان سے امکان خاص مراد ہے یا امکان عام اگر امکان خاص مراد لیا جائے
And the second: that what is meant by jawaz: this is the nineteenth part of the commentary's expression. Purpose: to explain the second discussion, which is an answer to an objection, but before that it is necessary to know a preliminary: Two types of possibility: (1) specific possibility (imkan khas) (2) general possibility (imkan 'am). (1) Specific possibility: its meaning is that necessity is negated from both sides (the side of existence and the side of non-existence); i.e., neither existence is necessary nor non-existence, like 'man exists in a specific place'; its meaning is that man's existence is not necessary nor is his non-existence. (2) General possibility: its meaning is that necessity is stripped from the opposite side; i.e., the opposite side is not necessary. Then it has three levels: (1) impossibility (imtina'), (2) necessity (wujud), (3) specific possibility (imkan khas). And their clarification: the opposite side of general possibility is either existential or non-existential. If the opposite side is existential, then the agreeing side (non-existence) is either necessary or not; if necessary, then this is impossibility (because the agreeing side is non-existential and the necessity of non-existence is impossibility); and if the agreeing side (non-existence) is not necessary, then this is specific possibility (because both the agreeing side and the opposite side have been negated). And if the opposite side is non-existential, then the agreeing side (existence) is either necessary or not; if necessary, then this is wujub (necessity) because its non-existence is not necessary and existence is necessary, and this occurs only in the wajib; and if the agreeing side (existence) is not necessary, then this is again specific possibility. Objection: The author (musannif) in the fourth and fifth probabilities of malha wa ma alayha took mal-hu to mean jawaz, and this jawaz by agreement is in the meaning of possibility. Now the question is: is this possibility meant as specific possibility or general possibility? If specific possibility is intended...
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a preliminary to answering an objection. It defines two types of possibility (imkan) in usul al-fiqh. Specific possibility (imkan khas) means something is neither necessary nor impossible; it is the middle state. General possibility (imkan 'am) is broader: it means the opposite side is not necessary, and it includes impossibility, necessity, and specific possibility as subcategories. The commentator then applies this to the term jawaz (permissibility) used by the author in earlier probabilities. The objection is whether jawaz as possibility means specific or general possibility. The passage sets up the framework for the answer. The distinction is crucial for understanding the hanafi classification of acts (wajib, haram, etc.) since possibility is a modal category used in defining hukm.

Key Terms
امکان خاص (imkan khas): Specific possibility: both existence and non-existence are non-necessary; contingent.
امکان عام (imkan 'am): General possibility: the opposite side is not necessary; includes impossibility, necessity, and specific possibility.
جواز (jawaz): Here interpreted as possibility (imkan), not legal permissibility in the sense of mubah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Neither existence nor non-existence is necessary.
B) Existence is necessary.
C) Non-existence is necessary.
D) Both existence and non-existence are necessary.

Key Takeaway
The passage establishes the terminological distinction between specific and general possibility, which is foundational for understanding modal categories in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

The Two Types of Possibility and the Meaning of Jawaz
Defining jawaz via two types of possibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between imkan khas and imkan 'amm in Hanafi usul and explain how the meaning of jawaz changes based on which type of possibility is intended.

Core Idea
Jawaz can mean specific or general possibility, which determines whether wujub is included or opposed.

In this passage from a Hanafi usul commentary, the author clarifies the term 'jawaz' by distinguishing two types of possibility: specific (imkan khas) and general (imkan 'amm). This distinction is crucial because the matn (base text) uses 'jawaz' in two different senses across different contexts, leading to potential contradictions. The commentary resolves these contradictions by carefully assigning the correct type of possibility to each context.

Guided Path
1
State the two types of possibility
Identify the definitions of imkan khas and imkan 'amm as given in the premise. Imkan khas negates necessity from both sides; imkan 'amm negates it from the opposite side only and includes three levels.
2
Understand the first objection
The objector argues that if jawaz means imkan khas, then wujub is opposite, but the matn made haram opposite; if imkan 'amm, then wujub is included, but the matn made wujub opposite in the fourth probability.
This contradiction is apparent, not real.
3
Analyze the commentator's resolution
The commentator assigns different meanings to different probabilities: in the fourth probability, jawaz means imkan khas (so wujub is opposite); in the fifth probability, jawaz means imkan 'amm (so haram is opposite).
Thus, no contradiction arises.
4
Apply the distinction to further objections
The passage introduces a second objection about the inclusion of wajib acts in the fourth probability. The commentator's resolution is incomplete, but the principle of contextual meaning remains key.
The second objection extends the same logic.

خاص ہے ( کیونکہ اس کی جانب موافق اور جانب مخالف دونوں کا سلب ہو گیا ہے ) اور اگر جانب مخالف عدمی ہو تو پھر جانب موافق (وجود) ضروری ہوگی یا نہیں اگر ضروری ہو تو یہ و بوب ہے کیونکہ اس کا عدم ضروری نہیں صورت میں جواز سے وہ امور مراد ہونگے جن کا فعل بھی ضروری نہیں اور ترک بھی ضروری نہیں تو اس اعتبار سے وجوب جواز کا مقابل بنتا ہے جواز میں داخل نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ وجوب میں جانب فعل ضروری ہوتی ہے لیکن ماتن جواز کے مقابل حرام کو لیکر آئے ہیں جو اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ وجوب جواز میں داخل ہے اور یہ غلط ہے اور اگر امکان سے امکان عام مرا دلیا جائے تو چوتھا احتمال غلط بنتا ہے کیونکہ اس وقت جواز سے وہ امور مراد ہونگے جن کا عدم ضروری نہیں یعنی ترک ضروری نہیں اور وجود یعنی فعل عام ہے کہ ضروری ہو یا نہ ہو اور اس اعتبار سے وجوب جواز میں داخل ہوتا ہے اسکے مقابل نہیں آتا کیونکہ امکان عام کے تین درجے ہیں اور ان میں واجب بھی داخل ہے لیکن ماتن چوتھے احتمال میں واجب کو جواز کے مقابل لے کر آئے ہیں یہ غلط ہے۔
جواب: دونوں صورتوں میں ایک ہی احتمال مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ چوتھے احتمال میں امکان خاص مراد ہے یعنی جانین سے ضرورت کا سب سے بعنوان دیگر عدم منع الفعل والترک الی لا يمنع فعله و ترکه یه یعنی نہ انتفاء فعل ممنوع ہو نہ ترک ممنوع ہو تو وجوب اس کا مقابل ہوگا کیونکہ اس کا وجود ضروری ہے بعنوان دیگر اس کا ترک ممنوع ہے
اور پانچویں احتمال میں امکان عام مراد ہے لہذا جب چوتھے احتمال میں جواز سے مراد امکان خاص ہے تو وجوب جواز کے مقابل ہوگا اور پانچویں صورۃ میں جب جواز سے مراد امکان عام ہوگا تو وجوب جواز میں داخل ہوگا کیونکہ جواز بمعنی امکان عام کے تین درجے ہیں ان میں وجوب بھی داخل ہے ان میں فعل حرام اس کے مقابل ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں جو از عدم منع الفعل کے معنی میں ہوگا یعنی اس کا فعل ممنوع نہ ہو جبکہ حرام کا فعل ممنوع ہے۔ تو اس سے کوئی خرابی لازم نہ آئے گی ۔
فان قلت ان ارید : ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا بیسواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض: اعتراض کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض:۔ آپ نے کہا چو تھے احتمال میں امکان خاص مراد ہے اور ماتن نے چوتھے احتمال میں فعل ماسوی الحرام ، فعل ما سوى المكروه تحریماً اور ترک ماسوی الواجب کو جواز میں داخل کیا ہے اور یہ درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ فعل ما سوى الحرام والمكروه تحریماً میں چارشخص داخل میں فعل واجب فعل مندوب فعل مباح ، اور فعل مکروہ تنزیہی اور ترک ماسوی الواجب میں پانچ ترک داخل میں ترک حرام ، ترک مکروہ تحریمی ، ترک مکروہ تنزیہی ترک مندوب اور ترک مباح تو ماتن نے کہا کہ فعل حرام اور فعل مکروہ تحریمی کے علاوہ تمام فعل جواز میں داخل ہیں اور ان میں فصل واجب بھی ہے حالانکہ اگر جوازت مراد امکان خاص مراد لیا جائے تو فعل واجب جواز میں داخل نہیں ہوتا لہذا یہ غلط ہے اسی طرح ماتن نے ترک واجب کے علاوہ سب تروک کو بھی جواز میں داخل کیا ہے اور ان میں ترک حرام اور ترک مکروہ تحریمی بھی داخل ہیں حالانکہ وہ بھی امکان
Statement of the second discussion: 'And the second is that what is meant by jawaz...' This is the nineteenth part of the commentary's expression. Purpose: to explain the second discussion, which is a response to an objection. But before that, it is necessary to know a premise by way of introduction. Premise: Possibility (imkan) has two types: (1) specific possibility (imkan khas) (2) general possibility (imkan 'amm). (1) Specific possibility: its meaning is that necessity is negated from both sides (the side of existence and the side of non-existence), i.e., neither the side of existence is necessary nor the side of non-existence, like 'man exists' in the specific sense. Its meaning is that neither the existence of man is necessary nor his non-existence. (2) General possibility: its meaning is that necessity is removed from the opposite side, i.e., the opposite side is not necessary. Then it has three levels: (1) Impossibility (imtina'), (2) Obligation (wujub), (3) Specific possibility (imkan khas). Their explanation: the opposite side of general possibility is either existential or non-existential. If the opposite side is existential, then the congruent side (non-existence) is either necessary or not. If necessary, this is impossibility (because the congruent side is non-existential and the necessity of non-existence is impossibility). If the congruent side (non-existence) is not necessary, then this is specific possibility (because the necessity of both its congruent and opposite sides is negated). If the opposite side is non-existential, then the congruent side (existence) is either necessary or not. If necessary, this is obligation (wujub) (because its non-existence is not necessary and existence is necessary, and this occurs only in the wajib). If the congruent side (existence) is not necessary, then this is again specific possibility. Objection: The author (musannif) in the fourth and fifth probabilities of 'what is for it and what is against it' took 'what is for it' to mean jawaz, and this jawaz, by consensus, means possibility. Now the question is: by this possibility, is specific possibility meant or general possibility? If specific possibility is meant, then the fifth probability does not become correct, because in the case of taking specific possibility, jawaz refers to matters whose action is not necessary and whose abandonment is not necessary. From this aspect, wujub becomes the opposite of jawaz, not included in jawaz, because in wujub the side of action is necessary. But the matn author brought haram as the opposite of jawaz, which is evidence that wujub is included in jawaz, and this is incorrect. And if general possibility is meant from possibility, then the fourth probability becomes incorrect, because then jawaz refers to matters whose non-existence is not necessary (i.e., abandonment is not necessary) and existence (i.e., action) is general, whether necessary or not. From this aspect, wujub enters into jawaz, not its opposite, because general possibility has three levels and among them wajib is included. But the matn author in the fourth probability brought wajib as the opposite of jawaz – this is incorrect. Answer: In both cases, the same probability is not meant. Rather, in the fourth probability, specific possibility is meant, i.e., the negation of necessity from both sides under another aspect: 'there is no prevention of action and abandonment, i.e., neither its action is prevented nor its abandonment.' Then wujub will be its opposite because its existence is necessary under another aspect, its abandonment is prevented. And in the fifth probability, general possibility is meant. Therefore, when in the fourth probability jawaz means specific possibility, wujub is opposite to jawaz, and in the fifth case, when jawaz means general possibility, wujub enters into jawaz, because jawaz in the sense of general possibility has three levels, and among them wujub is included. In it, the act of haram will be its opposite because here jawaz is in the sense of 'not preventing the act', i.e., its act is not prevented, while the act of haram is prevented. So no problem arises. 'For if you say, that what is intended...' This is the twentieth part of the commentary's expression. Purpose: to answer the objection. Objection: You said that in the fourth probability, specific possibility is meant, and the matn author included in the fourth probability 'the act of other than haram, the act of other than makruh tahrimi, and the abandonment of other than wajib' in jawaz. This is not correct, because the act of other than haram and makruh tahrimi includes four things: the act of wajib, the act of mandub, the act of mubah, and the act of makruh tanzihi. And the abandonment of other than wajib includes five abandonments: abandonment of haram, abandonment of makruh tahrimi, abandonment of makruh tanzihi, abandonment of mandub, and abandonment of mubah. So the matn author said that all acts except the act of haram and the act of makruh tahrimi are included in jawaz, and among them is the act of wajib, whereas if jawaz is taken to mean specific possibility, the act of wajib is not included in jawaz; therefore this is incorrect. Similarly, the matn author included all abandonments except the abandonment of wajib in jawaz, and among them are the abandonment of haram and the abandonment of makruh tahrimi, whereas they are also [possibility].
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih is a definitional discussion about the term 'jawaz' (permissibility). The author first establishes a premise about two types of possibility (imkan): specific possibility (imkan khas) and general possibility (imkan 'amm). Specific possibility means that neither existence nor non-existence of a thing is necessary – the thing is purely contingent. General possibility means only that the opposite side is not necessary, and it encompasses three levels: impossibility (imtina'), obligation (wujub), and specific possibility. The discussion arises from an objection: when the matn author (the original text) uses 'jawaz' in the sense of possibility, does it mean specific or general possibility? The objection argues that if specific possibility is meant, then wujub becomes opposite to jawaz, but the matn author made haram the opposite, implying wujub is included – a contradiction. Conversely, if general possibility is meant, then wujub is included, but the matn author set wujub as opposite in one of the probabilities. The commentator resolves this by distinguishing the two probabilities: in the fourth probability, jawaz means specific possibility, so wujub is indeed its opposite; in the fifth probability, jawaz means general possibility, so wujub falls within jawaz, and haram becomes the opposite. The passage then introduces a further objection questioning the inclusion of wajib acts and haram abandonments within jawaz under specific possibility, but the text cuts off. This is a classic Hanafi usul exercise in refining definitions to avoid logical inconsistencies.

Key Terms
امکان خاص (imkan khas): Specific possibility: the state where neither existence nor non-existence is necessary; contingency.
امکان عام (imkan 'amm): General possibility: the state where the opposite side of a proposition is not necessary, encompassing impossibility, obligation, and specific possibility.
جواز (jawaz): Permissibility, equated here with possibility (imkan) and further analyzed into two types.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation: the state where existence is necessary and non-existence is not necessary; a level within imkan 'amm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if 'jawaz' is taken in the sense of imkan khas, which of the following is true regarding wujub?
A) Wujub is included within jawaz.
B) Wujub is the opposite of jawaz.
C) Wujub is a subset of imkan 'amm, not related to jawaz.
D) Wujub and jawaz are synonymous.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul distinction between imkan khas and imkan 'amm resolves apparent contradictions in the use of the term 'jawaz' across different legal contexts.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
The Necessity of 'Istidlal' in the Definition of Fiqh
Dispute over redundancy of 'istidlal' in fiqh definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school includes 'istidlal' in the definition of fiqh and critically evaluate the redundancy objection.

Core Idea
'Istidlal' excludes prophetic intuitive knowledge, not just muqallid knowledge—saving the definition from redundancy.

The definition of fiqh has long been debated. One key point is whether the term 'istidlal' (inference) is redundant when 'from detailed evidences' already appears. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position that 'istidlal' is necessary to exclude the intuitive knowledge of prophets and angels, and examines the scholarly exchange between the commentator and the author of the matn.

Guided Path
1
State the definitional problem
Identify the standard definition: 'knowledge of detailed legal rulings from their detailed evidences with istidlal'. Note that some scholars argue that 'istidlal' is redundant because 'from detailed evidences' already implies inference.
The redundancy argument was made by the author of the matn (possibly Ibn al-Hajib).
2
Distinguish necessary and theoretical knowledge
Recognize that knowledge from evidence can be necessary (ḍarūrī) or theoretical (naẓarī). Necessary knowledge is obtained without reflection (e.g., prophets and angels). Theoretical knowledge requires inference (istidlal).
Fiqh technically only covers theoretical knowledge.
3
Evaluate the opponent's dalīl
The opponent claims that 'min adillatiha' already implies istidlal, so adding the term is redundant. Understand the reasoning: if knowledge is taken from evidence, that very process is inference.
The opponent uses the same phrase to argue redundancy.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi commentator gives two responses: (1) 'min adillatiha' does not necessarily imply inference—it includes knowledge without reflection. (2) Even if it did, mentioning istidlal serves purposes like explicit statement, removal of misunderstanding, or clarification, which are common in definitions.
Three benefits: taṣrīḥ (explicit statement), dafʿ al-wahm (removing misunderstanding), bayān (clarification).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilāf
If 'istidlal' were dropped, the definition would include necessary knowledge (e.g., Jibril's knowledge of rulings), which is incorrect. Thus, the practical consequence is that the definition must explicitly include istidlal to correctly delimit fiqh.
This ensures fiqh remains a human intellectual discipline.

اس میں تکرار نہ ہوا لہذا ماتن کا اس قید کو مکرر کہہ کر اس کو رد کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ ماتن کی طرف سے جواب فان قبیل حصول العلم : سے شرح کی عبارت کا دوسراحصہ ہے۔ غرض: شارع پر ایک اعتراض ہے۔ اعتراض:۔ اگر علم ادلہ سے ماخوذ ہو یعنی ادلہ میں غور و فکر کرنے کے بعد وہ علم حاصل ہوا ہو اور استدلال کا بھی یہی معنی ہے لہذا امن ادلتها استدلال کی قید کی طرف مشعر ہے تو جب من ادلتہا استدلال کی قید کی طرف مشعر ہے تو حضرت جبریل علیہ السلام اور نبی علیہ السلام کا علم من ادلتہا کی قید سے خارج ہو گیالہذا استدلال کی قید کو ذکر کرنا تکرار ہے۔ شاریخ کی طرف سے جواب الجواب قلنا لوسلم :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شارع نے دو جواب دئے ہیں (۱) ہم تسلیم ہی نہیں کرتے کہ من اولتها استدلال کی قید کی طرف مشعر ہے (۲) اگر تسلیم کر لیں کہ من ادلتہا استدلال کی قید کی طرف مشعر ہے پھر بھی استدلال کی قید میں تکرار نہیں ہے کیونکہ تکرار اس وقت ہوتا ہے جب اس کو ذکر کرنے میں کوئی فائدہ نہ ہو اور استدلال کی قید میں فائدہ ہے لہذ ا تکرار نہ ہوا اور وہ فائدہ کیا ہے؟ اس میں تین احتمال ہیں (۱) یہ قید تصریح بما علم التزاما کے قبیل سے ہے یعنی جوشئی پہلے
It is called fiqh idiomatically, so it is necessary to add the restriction of istidlal or istinbat to exclude it (the knowledge of the muqallid). The author (Ibn al-Hajib) imagined that it is an exclusion of the knowledge of the muqallid, so he decided that it is redundant because it is excluded by his statement 'from its detailed evidences'. If it is said: the attainment of knowledge from the evidence implies istidlal, because there is no meaning to that except that knowledge is taken from the evidence, so the knowledge of Jibril and the Messenger (peace be upon them) would also be excluded. We say: if conceded, then the mention of istidlal is for explicit statement of what is known implicitly, or for removal of misunderstanding, or for clarification, not for exclusion. Such is common in definitions. Translation: Ibn al-Hajib argued that knowledge of rulings from evidences can be of two types: necessary, like the knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet, and inferential, like the knowledge of the mujtahid. The first is not called fiqh idiomatically, so there is no escape from adding the restriction of istidlal/istinbat to exclude it. The author mistakenly thought it is to exclude the muqallid's knowledge, so he deemed it redundant because it is excluded by 'min adillatiha al-tafṣīliyyah'. If it is said: attainment of knowledge from evidence implies istidlal, because it means knowledge is taken from evidence, so Jibril and the Prophet's knowledge would also be excluded. We say: if conceded, then Ibn al-Hajib mentioned istidlal for explicit statement of what is known implicitly, or for removal of misunderstanding, or for clarification, not for exclusion. Such is common in definitions. Istidlal according to the commentator: the restriction of istidlal is not redundant. Explanation: His statement 'There is no doubt that it is redundant' is the first part of the commentary's text. From here, the commentator is objecting to the author (matn). But before that, as an introduction, understand a premise. Premise: The knowledge of rulings obtained from evidence is of two types: theoretical (naẓarī) and necessary (ḍarūrī). Theoretical is that knowledge of rulings is obtained from their evidences after reflection and pondering, i.e., through inference. Necessary is that knowledge of rulings is obtained along with the evidences themselves, i.e., both knowledge of rulings and knowledge of their evidences are obtained, but without needing reflection on those evidences. So if knowledge of both the cause and the ruling is obtained without reflection, it is necessary knowledge, like the knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet. That knowledge is not called fiqh; rather fiqh is called the knowledge obtained after reflection on the evidence. Objection: The author said that in the definition of fiqh, the restriction of istidlal added by Ibn al-Hajib is unnecessary and redundant, because Ibn al-Hajib added this restriction to exclude the knowledge of the muqallid, and that is already excluded by the phrase 'min adillatiha', so there is no need to add 'istidlal'. Now the commentator objects to the author: O sir, you considered the restriction of istidlal to be superfluous and redundant because you thought it is meant to exclude the muqallid's knowledge, whereas it is not meant to exclude the muqallid's knowledge, but rather to exclude the knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet, because they have intuitive and necessary knowledge. Since 'min adillatiha' includes this knowledge (Jibril and the Prophet's knowledge is also based on evidence), but because it is not obtained through inference (reflection), it is excluded by the restriction of istidlal. Hence there is no redundancy, so the author's deeming it redundant and rejecting it is incorrect. The author's response: 'For if it is said: attainment of knowledge...' is the second part of the commentary's text. Purpose: There is an objection to the commentator. Objection: If the restriction of istidlal is meant to exclude the knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet, then still there is redundancy because the restriction of istidlal is already present in 'min adillatiha'. This is because 'min adillatiha' means that knowledge is taken from evidence after reflection, which is the same meaning as istidlal. Therefore 'min adillatiha' indicates the restriction of istidlal, so when 'min adillatiha' indicates istidlal, the knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet is excluded by 'min adillatiha' anyway, so mentioning istidlal is redundant. The commentator's response: 'We say: if conceded...' is the third part of the commentary's text. Here the commentator gives two answers: (1) We do not concede that 'min adillatiha' indicates the restriction of istidlal. (2) Even if we concede that 'min adillatiha' indicates the restriction of istidlal, still there is no redundancy in the restriction of istidlal because redundancy only occurs when there is no benefit in mentioning it, and there is benefit in the restriction of istidlal. What is that benefit? There are three possibilities: (1) This restriction is of the type of explicit statement of what is known implicitly, i.e., something that was already known...
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the definition of fiqh. The commentator (sharih) is refining the objection made by the author (matn) to Ibn al-Hajib's definition. The key issue is whether the term 'istidlal' (inference) is redundant in the standard Hanafi definition of fiqh: 'knowledge of the detailed legal rulings from their detailed evidences with istidlal'. The author thought it was redundant because the phrase 'from their detailed evidences' already implies inference, and that it was only meant to exclude the muqallid's knowledge. The commentator shows that the phrase 'from their detailed evidences' includes any knowledge derived from evidence, including the intuitive knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet (which is not called fiqh). Therefore, adding 'istidlal' is necessary to exclude that intuitive knowledge. The objection is further refined: even if 'from their detailed evidences' implies inference, the mention of 'istidlal' is still beneficial for explicit statement, removal of misunderstanding, or clarification. Thus the commentator defends the Hanafi position that the definition of fiqh must include the term 'istidlal' to properly distinguish it from necessary knowledge.

Key Terms
استدلال (istidlal): Inference or reasoning from evidence to derive a ruling, involving reflection and intellectual effort.
من أدلتها التفصيلية (min adillatiha al-tafṣīliyyah): From their detailed evidences, meaning the specific textual proofs (Qur'an verses, hadith) and not just general principles.
علم المقلد (ʿilm al-muqallid): Knowledge of the muqallid; one who follows a madhhab without knowledge of the evidence or derivation process.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi commentator, why is the term 'istidlal' necessary in the definition of fiqh?
A) To exclude the knowledge of the muqallid.
B) To exclude the intuitive knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet.
C) To emphasize the importance of the Qur'an as evidence.
D) To include the knowledge of all Muslims.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of fiqh must include 'istidlal' to correctly restrict it to human inferential knowledge, distinguishing it from prophetic necessary knowledge.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

8 min
Dispute on the Condition of Inference in the Definition of Fiqh
Super-commentary refuting the sharh's defense of the condition 'bi al-istidlal'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the redundancy of the condition 'bi al-istidlal' in the Hanafi definition of fiqh by analyzing the logical arguments for and against its inclusion.

Core Idea
The phrase 'min adillatiha' already implies inference; adding 'bi al-istidlal' is redundant unless it serves to exclude necessary knowledge.

In defining fiqh as 'knowledge of practical shar'i rulings from their evidences,' the condition 'min adillatiha' (from their evidences) seems to already require reasoning. The matn author argued that adding 'bi al-istidlal' is a repetition. The commentator defended it, and the super-commentator refuted that defense. This lesson dissects the linguistic and logical arguments, sharpening your ability to critique legal definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The matn author claims 'bi al-istidlal' is redundant; the commentator claims it excludes necessary knowledge. Note the two positions.
2
Analyze the linguistic meaning of 'min adillatiha'
The preposition 'min' in Arabic indicates extraction or temporality. In the definition, it suggests that knowledge comes from evidence after a process. Consider whether this process necessarily involves inference.
Hanafi usul emphasizes the difference between 'min' and 'ma'a'.
3
Examine the commentator's two defenses
First: denial that 'min adillatiha' implies inference. Second: even if it does, the explicit mention adds benefits (clarification, repelling misunderstanding, detail). Study each defense.
4
Evaluate the super-commentator's refutations
The super-commentator shows self-contradiction in the commentator's own statements and argues that the supposed benefits are invalid. Determine which refutation is strongest.
5
Draw a conclusion on the redundancy
Based on the linguistic analysis and the refutations, decide whether the condition 'bi al-istidlal' is redundant. Recognize that this remains a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The later Hanafi tradition largely adopts the super-commentator's view.

السلام اورنبی اکرم کا علم اوراس علم کو فقہ ہیں کہتے بلکہ فقہ اس علم کو کہتے ہیں جو دلیل میں غوروفکر کرنے کے بعد حاصل ہوا ہو اعتراض: ماتن نے کہا فقہ کی تعریف میں ابن حاجب نے جو استدلال کی قید لگائی ہے اس کی ضرورت نہیں بلکہ اس میں تمرار ہے کیونکہ علامہ ابن حاجب نے یہ قید مقلد کے علم کو خارج کرنے کے لئے لگائی ہے اور وہ تو من ادلتہا کی قید سے ہی خارج ہو جاتا ہے بالاستدلال کی قید لگانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اب شاریخ ماتن پر اعتراض کرتے ہیں کہ جناب آپ نے یہ سمجھ کر استدلال کی قید کو زائد اور مکرر کہا ہے کہ اس سے مقصود مقلد کے علم کو خارج کرنا ہے حالانکہ اس سے مقصود مقلد کے علم کو خارج کرنا نہیں ہے بلکہ حضرت جبریل علیہ السلام اور نبی اکر میں اللہ کے علم کو خارج کرنا مقصود ہے کیونکہ ان کو علم بدیہی اور ضروری حاصل ہے کیونکہ من ادلتہا میں یہ علم داخل تھا کہ جبریل علیہ السلام و نبی کریم اے کا علم بھی دلیل کے ساتھ ہے لیکن چونکہ یہ علم استدلال ( غور و فکر) سے حاصل نہیں ہوا اس لئے استدلال کی قید سے اس کو خارج کر دیا تو اس میں تکرار نہ ہوا لہذا ماتن کا اس قید کو مکرر کہہ کر اس کو رد کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔
ماتن کی طرف سے جواب

شاریخ کی طرف سے جواب الجواب
قلنا لوسلم :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شارع نے دو جواب دئے ہیں (۱) ہم تسلیم ہی نہیں کرتے کہ من ادلتہا استدلال کی قید کی طرف مشعر ہے (۲) اگر تسلیم کر لیں کہ من ادلتہا استدلال کی قید کی طرف مشعر ہے پھر بھی استدلال کی قید میں تکرار نہیں ہے کیونکہ تکرار اس وقت ہوتا ہے جب اس کو ذکر کرنے میں کوئی فائدہ نہ ہو اور استدلال کی قید میں فائدہ ہے لہذا تکرار نہ ہوا اور وہ فائدہ کیا ہے؟ اس میں تین احتمال ہیں (۱) یہ قید تصریح بما علم التزاما کے قبیل سے ہے یعنی جوشئی پہلے التزاماً معلوم ہوئی دوبارہ اس کی تصریح کردی تو یہاں من ادلتہا کی قید سے استدلال کی قید التزاماً سمجھ میں آرہی تھی پھر استدلال کو ذکر کر کے اس کی تصریح کردی (۲) یہ قید دفع وہم کے لئے ہے کہ من ادلتہا کے بعد کسی کو وہم ہو سکتا تھا کہ اس سے علم ضروری ( جبریل علیہ السلام و نبی اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کا علم ) خارج نہیں ہوا تو اس وہم کے ازالہ کے لئے یہ قید لگادی (۳) استدلال کی قید من ادلتہا سے معلوم ہو رہی تھی لیکن اس کے بیان اور تفصیل کی خاطر اس کو دوبارہ ذکر کر دیا گویا بالاستدلال اس استدلال کا بیان اور تفصیل ہے جو من ادلتہا سے معلوم ہو رہا ہے۔
