جواب الجواب کی تردید
تردید اول:۔ پہلے جواب کو دو وجہوں سے رد کیا گیا ہے (۱) ابھی گذشتہ قول کے آخر میں شارع نے خود کہا کہ من ادلتہا کا مطلب ہے کہ وہ علم دلیل میں غور و فکر کرنے کے بعد حاصل ہوا ہو تو گویا خود اس بات کا اقرار کیا کہ من ادلتہا استدلال کی قید کی طرف مشعر ہے اور اب خود اس کی تردید کر رہے ہیں لہذا شاریخ کا یہ جواب درست نہیں ہے (۲) شرح مختصر المعانی کے حواشی میں تاریخ نے بیان فرمایا کہ علم ضروری اور بدیہی دلیل کی معیت میں ہوتا ہے یعنی دونوں ( علم و دلیل ) اکٹھے حاصل ہوتے ہیں اور علم استدلالی وہ ہوتا ہے جس میں دلیل پہلے معلوم ہو اور علم بعد میں حاصل ہو اب یہاں جب من ادلتہا کہا تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ بھی علم استدلالی ہے کہ دلیل پہلے معلوم ہو علم بعد میں حاصل ہو ورنہ تو من کی بجائے مع ادلتہا ہونا چاہیے تھا خلاصہ یہ کہ شاریخ کی اپنی کلام سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ من ادلتہا کی قید بالاستدلال کی طرف مشعر ہے تو پھر بھی شاریخ کا یہ کہنا کہ ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے یہ صرف سینہ زوری ہے۔
تردید ثانی شاری نے استدلال کی قید کے جو تین فائدے ذکر کئے ہیں یہ سب غلط ہیں کیونکہ ہم پوچھتے ہیں کہ آپ نے جو کہا ہے کہ یہ تصریح بما علم التزاما کے قبیل سے ہے اگر یہ مقلد کے علم کو خارج کرنے کے اعتبار سے ہے تو مقلد کا علم تو دونوں قیدوں سے التزاماً خارج ہورہا ہے تو پھر بالاستدلال کی قید تفریح بما علم التزاما کے قبیل سے نہ ہوئی بلکہ یہ تو التزام بعد بما علم التزاما کے قبیل سے ہے اور یہ کہنا کہ یہ قید دفع وہم کے لئے ہے تو ہم پوچھتے ہیں کہ من ادلتہا کی قید مقصود کے موافق ہے یا نہیں اگر مقصود کے موافق ہے تو پھر کسی کو وہم نہیں ہوگا اور اگر یہ مقصود کے موافق نہیں تو پھر اس قید کی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ صرف استدلال کو ذکر کر دیتے تو اس سے علم ضروری بھی خارج ہو جاتا اور مقلد کا علم بھی خارج ہو جاتا تو اس صورت میں من ادلتہا کی قید زائد ہوتی اور اسی طرح آپ نے کہا ہے کہ یہ قید بیان اور تفصیل کے لئے ہے یہ بھی درست نہیں کیونکہ ہم پوچھتے ہیں کہ من
Al-Tarwih li-Halli al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. The knowledge of as-Salam? and the Noble Prophet and this knowledge is called fiqh, rather fiqh is that knowledge which is obtained after reflection in the evidence. Objection: The matn author said: In the definition of fiqh, the condition of inference that Ibn al-Hajib added is unnecessary, rather it is repetition because Allamah Ibn al-Hajib added this condition to exclude the knowledge of the muqallid, and that is already excluded by the condition 'min adillatiha', so there is no need for the condition 'bi al-istidlal'. Now the commentator objects to the matn author saying: You considered the condition 'bi al-istidlal' redundant and repetitive thinking that the purpose was to exclude the knowledge of the muqallid, whereas the purpose is not to exclude the knowledge of the muqallid, but rather to exclude the knowledge of Hadrat Jibril alayhissalam and the Noble Prophet, because their knowledge is intuitive and necessary, because that knowledge was included under 'min adillatiha', that the knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet is also with evidence, but since this knowledge was not obtained through inference (reflection), it is excluded by the condition of inference, so there is no repetition. Therefore, the matn author's rejection of this condition as repetitive is incorrect. Reply from the matn author: 'Fa in qabīl ḥusūl al-ʿilm' is the second part of the sharh's text. Aim: There is an objection on the commentator. Objection: If excluding the knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet is the purpose of the condition of inference, then there is still repetition in this condition because the condition of inference is found in 'min adillatiha', because 'min adillatiha' means that knowledge is derived from evidences, i.e., obtained after reflection in the evidences, and inference has the same meaning. Therefore, 'min adillatiha' points to the condition of inference. So when 'min adillatiha' points to the condition of inference, then the knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet is excluded by the condition 'min adillatiha', thus mentioning the condition of inference is repetition. Response from the commentator: 'Qulnā law sallamnā' is the third part of the sharh's text. From here the commentator gives two answers: (1) We do not concede that 'min adillatiha' points to the condition of inference. (2) If we concede that 'min adillatiha' points to the condition of inference, there is still no repetition in the condition of inference because repetition occurs when there is no benefit in mentioning it, and the condition of inference has benefit. What is the benefit? There are three possibilities: (1) This condition is of the type 'taṣrīḥ bīmā ʿulima al-tizāmā' i.e., something known implicitly is explicitly mentioned again; so here the condition of inference was implicitly understood from 'min adillatiha' and then explicit mention of inference was made. (2) This condition is for repelling a misunderstanding, that after 'min adillatiha' someone might misunderstand that necessary knowledge (knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet) is not excluded, so this condition is added to remove that misunderstanding. (3) The condition of inference was known from 'min adillatiha', but for its explanation and detail it was mentioned again, as if 'bi al-istidlal' is the explanation and detail of that inference which is known from 'min adillatiha'. Rejection: Both answers of the commentator are rejected. Refutation of the response to the objection: First refutation: The first answer is rejected for two reasons: (1) At the end of the previous statement, the commentator himself said that 'min adillatiha' means that knowledge is obtained after reflection in the evidence, so he himself admitted that 'min adillatiha' points to the condition of inference, and now he denies it. Therefore, this answer of the commentator is not correct. (2) In the glosses of Sharh Mukhtasar al-Ma'ani, Taftazani stated that necessary and intuitive knowledge occurs with evidence, i.e., both (knowledge and evidence) are obtained together, whereas inferential knowledge is that in which the evidence is known first and knowledge is obtained later. Now when 'min adillatiha' is said, it indicates that this is also inferential knowledge, because the evidence is known first and knowledge later; otherwise it should have been 'ma'a adillatiha' instead of 'min'. So it is clear from the commentator's own statement that the condition 'min adillatiha' points to inference, so the commentator's saying 'we do not concede' is mere obstinacy. Second refutation: The three benefits that the commentator mentioned for the condition of inference are all wrong because we ask: As for your statement that it is of the type 'taṣrīḥ bīmā ʿulima al-tizāmā', if it is for excluding the knowledge of the muqallid, then the muqallid's knowledge is already excluded by both conditions implicitly, so the condition 'bi al-istidlal' is not of the type 'taṣrīḥ bīmā ʿulima al-tizāmā', but rather of the type 'iltizām baʿd mā ʿulima al-tizāmā'. And your saying that this condition is for repelling a misunderstanding, we ask: Is the condition 'min adillatiha' consistent with the purpose or not? If it is consistent, then no one would misunderstand; if it is not consistent, then this condition is unnecessary, rather simply mentioning inference would exclude both necessary knowledge and muqallid's knowledge, so in that case the condition 'min adillatiha' would be redundant. Similarly, your saying that this condition is for explanation and detail is also not correct because we ask: 'Min'?
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary (Al-Tarwih li-Halli al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih) on a dispute within the Hanafi usul tradition regarding the definition of fiqh. The definition of fiqh is 'knowledge of the practical shar'i rulings derived from detailed evidences'. The key point of contention is whether the condition 'bi al-istidlal' (by inference) is redundant given the phrase 'min adillatiha' (from their evidences). The matn author (likely Sadr al-Shariah) argues that it is redundant because 'min adillatiha' already implies that the knowledge is acquired through reasoning (istidlal), so the additional condition serves no purpose except to exclude the knowledge of a muqallid (one who follows without reasoning), which is already excluded. The commentator (sharh) responds that the condition is not redundant; it serves to exclude the necessary and intuitive knowledge of angels like Jibril and the Prophet Muhammad (saw), which is not acquired through deliberative inference even though it is evidence-based. The matn author rebuts that even so, 'min adillatiha' already implies inference because the preposition 'min' indicates that knowledge comes after evidence, not with it, so knowledge that is simultaneous with evidence (like necessary knowledge) is excluded. The commentator then offers two answers: (1) denial that 'min adillatiha' implies inference, and (2) assertion that even if it does, the explicit mention of 'bi al-istidlal' adds benefits like clarifying the implicit meaning, repelling misunderstandings, or providing detail. The super-commentator (the author of Al-Tarwih) refutes both answers. First, he demonstrates that the commentator himself earlier defined 'min adillatiha' as implying reflection, contradicting his denial. Second, he argues that the supposed benefits are invalid: the clarification is not of a previously known implicit meaning but rather a mere repetition; repelling a misunderstanding would only be needed if 'min adillatiha' were ambiguous, but it is not; and providing detail would be unnecessary because the meaning is already clear. Thus, the super-commentator concludes that the matn author's original objection stands: the condition 'bi al-istidlal' is indeed redundant. This passage illustrates the Hanafi usul method of rigorous linguistic and logical analysis in defining key terms, as well as the internal scholarly debate within the madhhab.

Key Terms
استدلال (istidlal): Deliberative inference from evidence through reflection and reasoning.
من ادلتہا (min adillatiha): Knowledge that is derived from evidences, implying that evidence precedes knowledge and inference occurs.
علم ضروری (ilm daruri): Necessary, intuitive knowledge that is not acquired through deliberate reasoning (e.g., knowledge of prophets and angels).
مقلد (muqallid): One who follows a mujtahid without knowing the evidence or reasoning behind the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the super-commentator's final position, why is the condition 'bi al-istidlal' considered redundant in the definition of fiqh?
A) Because 'min adillatiha' already implies inference, so the condition is a repetition without benefit.
B) Because the muqallid's knowledge is already excluded by 'min adillatiha'.
C) Because the commentator admitted that 'min adillatiha' points to inference.
D) Because the condition is meant to exclude necessary knowledge, which is already excluded.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'min adillatiha' inherently requires inference, making the explicit condition 'bi al-istidlal' redundant, unless one adopts a different reading of the preposition.

Resolving the Objection to the Definition of Hukm: The Role of Alif Lam Li al-Jins
Resolving an objection by applying alif lam li al-jins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi usuli uses the principle of alif lam li al-jins to resolve the objection that the definition of hukm would require totality, and apply that principle to similar phrases.

Core Idea
Alif lam li al-jins on a plural removes the implication of inclusivity, saving the definition from requiring all acts of all mukallafin.

In this passage from Al-Tarweeh, the commentator answers an objection that the definition of hukm as 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi af'al al-mukallafin' would imply only an address covering all acts of all responsible persons qualifies as hukm. By identifying the 'al' in 'al-mukallafin' as li al-jins, he shows the phrase means 'acts of the category of mukallafin,' thus applying to any act of any mukallaf. This crucial linguistic insight preserves the definition's comprehensiveness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base definition and the objection
The definition is 'hukm is khitab Allah related to the acts of the mukallafin'. The objection says because both 'acts' and 'mukallafin' are plural in idafah, it implies totality—so hukm would only be an address covering all acts of all mukallafin, which is impossible and excludes the Prophet's special rulings.
2
Understand the problem with idafah of plural to plural
When a plural noun is in idafah to another plural, it normally implies ikhtisas and hasr (specification and limitation), meaning the phrase refers to all of the first thing belonging to all of the second thing.
3
Analyze the commentator's response using alif lam li al-jins
The commentator points out that 'al-mukallafin' has alif lam li al-jins (generic article). This article removes the plural meaning and turns the noun into a genus (jins), so the idafah no longer implies totality. The phrase now means 'acts of the category of mukallafin'—i.e., any act of any mukallaf.
This is a key Hanafi principle: alif lam li al-jins on a plural cancels the implication of all individuals.
4
See how the resolution saves the definition
With the corrected meaning, the definition applies to any address of Allah related to any act of any mukallaf, making it both possible and inclusive of the Prophet's special rulings.
5
Note the second objection (incomplete)
The text begins a second objection about 'idafat al-khitab' but cuts off. This is left as an exercise in understanding how such objections are posed and answered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و معنی تعلقہ با فعال المتلقین : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے غرض شارع ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔ اعتراض: خطاب کی تعریف میں افعال المتکلمین کا ذکر ہے افعال بھی جمع ہے اور اس کا مضاف الیہ یعنی مکلفین بھی جمع ہے اور جب جمع کی اضافت جمع کی طرف کی جائے تو وہ مضاف اور مضاف الیہ دونوں کے اختصاص اور حصر کا فائدہ دیتی ہے تو اب مطلب یہ ہو گیا کہ حکم اللہ تعالیٰ کے اس خطاب کا نام ہے جو تمام مکلفین کے تمام افعال سے متعلق ہو وہ تو حکم ہے اور جو اس جو ہو ۔ طرح نہ ہو وہ حکم نہیں ہے تو اب کوئی حکم موجودہی نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ کوئی خطاب ایسا ہے ہی نہیں جو تمام مکلفین کے تمام افعال سے متعلق ہو اور دوسری خرابی یہ لازم آئی کہ تعریف جامع جمع الافراد نہیں رہی کیونکہ اس سے نبی اکرم نے کی خصوصیات خارج ہو گئیں (مثلاً چار بیویوں سے زیادہ کے ساتھ نکاح کا مباح ہونا ) حالانکہ یہ خطاب ہے لیکن تمام مکلفین کے ساتھ خطاب نہیں ہے۔ جواب: المکلفین پر الف لام جنس کا ہے اور جب جمع پر الف لام جنس داخل ہوتا ہے تو اس میں جمعیت والا معنی ختم ہو جاتا ہے اور جنسیت والا معنی آجاتا ہے اور جنس قلیل کثیر سب پر صادق آتی ہے اور جب ہمکلفین میں جمعیت والا معنیٰ ختم ہوا تو افعال میں بھی استغراق والا معنی ختم ہو گیا کیونکہ اب جمع کی اضافت جمع کی طرف نہ رہی تو اب مطلب یہ ہو گیا کہ حکم نام ہے اللہ کے خطاب کا جو متعلق ہو بعض مکلفین کے بعض افعال کے ساتھ یعنی کسی مکلف کے کسی فعل کے ساتھ جو خطاب اللہ متعلق ہوگا اس کا نام حکم ہے۔ و خرج خطاب اللہ:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چھٹا حصہ ہے یہاں سے المتعلق بافعال المکلفین کی قید کا فائدہ ذکر کیا ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کا وہ خطاب خارج ہو گیا جو اسکی ذات اس کی صفات اس کی تنزیبات یا اسکے علاوہ ایسی چیز سے متعلق ہو جو مکلف کا فعلی نہیں ہے کیونکہ ایسا خطاب حکم نہیں ہوتا۔ لا يقال اضافة الخطاب:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ ایک اعتراض کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض:۔ آپ نے حکم کی تعریف میں خطاب کی نسبت اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف کی ہے اس سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ حکم خطاب اللہ
And the meaning of 'related to the acts of the addressees': This is the fifth part of the commentary. The commentator is answering an objection. Objection: In the definition of khitab, 'af'al' (acts) is mentioned, which is plural, and its idafah (genitive construct) is to 'mukallafin', also plural. When a plural is in idafah to a plural, it implies specification and limitation (ikhtisas and hasr). So the meaning becomes: hukm is the name of Allah's address that is related to ALL acts of ALL mukallafin; what is not like that is not hukm. Then no hukm would exist because no address relates to all acts of all mukallafin. Another problem: the definition would not include the special rulings for the Prophet, e.g., marrying more than four wives, which is a khitab but not to all mukallafin. Response: The 'al' in 'al-mukallafin' is alif lam li al-jins (generic article). When alif lam li al-jins enters a plural, the meaning of plurality is removed and genericity takes over, which applies to few or many. Since the plural meaning is gone in 'mukallafin', the meaning of istighraq (inclusivity) is also removed from 'af'al'. Thus the meaning becomes: hukm is the name of Allah's address related to some acts of some mukallafin, i.e., whatever address of Allah relates to any act of any mukallaf, that is called hukm. 'And excludes the address of Allah': This is the sixth part. Here the benefit of the restriction 'related to the acts of the mukallafin' is mentioned: it excludes Allah's address that relates to His essence, attributes, glorifications, or anything that is not an act of the mukallaf, because such address is not hukm. 'It is not said the idafah of the address': This is the seventh part. He answers an objection. Objection: You added 'khitab' to Allah in the definition of hukm, indicating that hukm is khitab Allah...
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage addresses a critical objection to the definition of hukm as 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi af'al al-mukallafin'. The objection argues that since both 'af'al' and 'mukallafin' are plural in idafah, the definition would imply that hukm refers only to a khitab that covers all acts of all mukallafin, which is impossible, and would exclude special rulings for the Prophet. The response uses the principle of 'alif lam li al-jins' (generic article) on 'al-mukallafin', which removes the plural sense and thus the idafah no longer implies totality. The phrase then means 'related to acts of the category of mukallafin', i.e., any act of any mukallaf. This saves the definition and makes it inclusive. Then the commentator notes that the restriction 'related to acts of mukallafin' excludes divine addresses about Allah's essence or attributes, which are not legal rulings. Finally, a new objection is raised about the idafah of khitab to Allah, but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
الف لام الجنس (alif lam li al-jins): A definite article that indicates the genus or kind, removing the implication of inclusiveness (istighraq).
اختصاص و حصر (ikhtisas wa hasr): Specification and limitation that would arise from idafah of a plural to a plural.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) By stating that 'al-mukallafin' has alif lam li al-jins, which removes the plural meaning.
B) By claiming that the acts of the Prophet are excluded.
C) By saying that the definition is only for some rulings.
D) By ignoring the objection.

Key Takeaway
Alif lam li al-jins on a plural noun removes the implication of inclusivity, a crucial principle in Hanafi usul for defining legal terms.

The Definition of Hukm: Hanafi vs Ash'ari
Explains and defends Hanafi definition of hukm, addresses Ash'ari objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi and Ash'ari definitions of hukm and identify the key objections to the Ash'ari definition.

Core Idea
Hukm is contingent in Hanafi usul and eternal in Ash'ari kalam—a definitional divergence with deep implications.

The definition of hukm (shar'i ruling) is a foundational debate in usul al-fiqh. In this lesson, we examine two major objections raised by Hanafi scholars against the Ash'ari definition. Understanding this dispute clarifies the epistemological commitments of each school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
State the Hanafi definition (ma thabata bil-khitab, i.e., contingent attributes like wujub) and the Ash'ari definition (khitab Allah, the eternal address itself).
Hanafis focus on the effect of the address; Ash'aris on the address as an attribute of Allah.
2
Understand the first objection
The Ash'ari definition defines hukm as an eternal attribute of Allah, while jurists consider hukm contingent on the mukallaf's actions. This is a definition by opposition (ta'rif bi al-mubayin).
3
Review the second objection
The definition excludes rulings concerning children, who are not mukallaf, e.g., validity of a child's sale, correctness of his Islam, and recommendability of his prayer. These are legitimate shar'i rulings but not covered.
The objection is that the definition is not comprehensive (ghayr jami').
4
Analyze the Ash'ari response and Hanafi rebuttal
Ash'aris respond that such rulings relate to the guardian, who is mukallaf. Hanafis rebut that not all of a child's actions are attributable to the guardian; for example, the child's own Islam (if he converts) is not an action of the guardian.
The rebuttal is incomplete in the source, but the point stands.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafis consider rulings as created attributes (hadith), Ash'aris as uncreated (qadim). This affects whether rulings can be known by reason alone and the ontological status of divine address.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اور فاعتبروا کی مثل حکم کی تعریف سے اس لئے کہ وہ دونوں افعال قلب سے ہیں۔
اشاعرہ پر وارد ہونے والے پانچ اعتراضات
تشریح: قولہ پیر د علیہ:۔ جن اشاعرہ نے حکم کی تعریف خطاب اللہ تعالٰی کیساتھ کی ہے ان پر پانچ اعتراضات ہوتے ہیں یہاں سے انہیں اعتراضات کو نقل کیا جارہا ہے اور ساتھ ساتھ بعض کے جوابات بھی دیئے گئے ہیں۔ اعتراض (۱): اشاعرہ نے جو حکم کی تعریف کی ہے وہ فقہاء کی اصطلاح کے مطابق نہیں کیونکہ فقہاء نے حکم کی تعریف ما شبت بالخطاب کیسا تھ کی ہے یعنی وجوب حرمت وغیرہ کے ساتھ اور یہ مکلف کی صفات بنتی ہیں اور حادث ہیں اور اشاعرہ نے تعریف کی خطاب اللہ الخ سے اور یہ اللہ تعالیٰ کی صفت ہے اور قدیم ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ فقہا کے نزدیک حکم حادث ہے اور اشاعرہ اس کی تعریف قدیم کے ساتھ کر رہے ہیں تو یہ تعریف بالمبائین ہے۔ لہذا اشاعرہ کو حکم کی ایسی تعریف کرنے چاہیے تھی جو فقہاء کی اصطلاح کے مطابق ہوتی۔ اعتراض (۲):- اشاعرہ نے جو حکم کی تعریف کی ہے وہ جامع نہیں کیونکہ اس سے بعض احکام خارج ہو جاتے ہیں جیسے بچے کے افعال کے متعلق جو خطابات ہیں مثلاً بچے کی بیع شراء کا جائز ہونا اس کے اسلام لانے کا صحیح ہونا اس کی نماز کا مستحب ہونا یہ سب احکام شرعیہ ہیں لیکن اشاعرہ کی تعریف میں یہ داخل نہیں بعد ہے کیونکہ تعریف میں کہا حکم وہ خطاب ہے جو مکلفین کے افعال سے متعلق ہو اور بچہ مکلف نہیں ہے لہذا یہ تعریف جامع نہ ہوتی ہے
فان قیل ہو حکم : سے ماتن نے بعض حضرات کی طرف سے جواب نقل کیا ہے اور پھر اس کا رد کیا ہے۔ جواب: ہماری تعریف جامع ہے کیونکہ بچے کے افعال کے متعلق جو خطابات ہیں وہ بچے کے واسطے سے اس کے ولی کے متعلق ہوتے ہیں مثلاً اگر بچے کے مال میں سے زکوۃ ادا کرنا واجب ہے تو اس کی ادائیگی ولی پر واجب ہوتی ہے نہ کہ بچے پر اور ولی مکلف ہے لہذا بچے کے افعال بھی مکلف کے افعال ہوئے لہذ ا ہماری تعریف جامع ہوئی۔ رو:۔ ماتن نے اس جواب کو رد اس طرح کیا کہ اول تو ہم مانتے ہی نہیں کہ بچے کے تمام افعال اس کے واسطہ سے ولی کی
The repetition: and the answer to the preceding objection emerges, and that is his saying: 'like آمِنُوا and فَاعْتَبِرُوا are excluded, because they are from the actions of the heart.' Urdu explanation follows. Then: five objections against the Ash'aris. Explanation: ... The first objection: The Ash'aris' definition of hukm does not agree with the jurists' terminology because the jurists define hukm as what is established by the address, i.e., obligation, prohibition etc., and these are attributes of the mukallaf and are contingent, while the Ash'aris define it as the address of Allah, which is an attribute of Allah and eternal. So the definition is of opposite things. Second objection: The definition is not comprehensive because it excludes rulings related to a child's actions, such as the validity of his sale, his Islam, his prayer being recommended, etc. Response: The definition is comprehensive because such rulings relate to the guardian, who is mukallaf. Rebuttal: We do not accept that all of the child's actions are attributed to the guardian.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Altarweehurdu, a Hanafi sharh of Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih. It begins by discussing a previous objection regarding repetition in the definition of fiqh. The author explains that by 'actions' they mean bodily actions, excluding heart actions, so commands like 'Believe' and 'Consider' are not included in the definition of hukm as they are heart actions. Then the text moves to five objections against the Ash'ari definition of hukm as 'the address of Allah related to the actions of the mukallaf.' The first objection: The Ash'ari definition defines hukm as eternal (Allah's attribute), whereas jurists consider hukm to be contingent (the ruling itself). This is a definition by opposition. The second objection: The definition is not comprehensive because it excludes rulings for non-mukallaf like children. The response from some scholars is that such rulings relate to the guardian. The author then rebuts this, saying that not all of the child's actions are attributed to the guardian. The text cuts off during this rebuttal.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): In this passage, hukm is discussed in two senses: the Hanafi sense (contingent attribute established by address) and the Ash'ari sense (the address of Allah itself).
خطاب (khitab): The divine address (Qur'an or Sunnah) that contains a command, prohibition, or permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response to the second objection, why is the Ash'ari definition of hukm still considered comprehensive despite excluding children?
A) Because children are considered mukallaf in some cases
B) Because rulings for children are attributed to their guardians who are mukallaf
C) Because children's actions are not subject to rulings
D) Because the definition was later amended to include children

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm as the contingent effect of the address is more precise for jurisprudence than the Ash'ari definition of the address itself.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Objections 4 and 5: Exclusion of Internal Acts and Redundancy of 'Practical' and the Response
Fourth and fifth objections to Ash'ari definition of hukm and joint refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two objections to the definition of hukm and explain how the Hanafi response uses the distinction between general (amm) and specific (khass) terms to resolve them.

Core Idea
The definition includes internal acts because 'af'al' is general; 'amaliyyah' specifies external acts—no redundancy.

In this passage, we encounter two objections that challenge the comprehensiveness and coherence of the Ash'ari definition of hukm. The fourth objection argues that commands involving heart acts, such as 'Believe', are excluded if 'acts' only means limb actions. The fifth objection claims that the term 'practical' is redundant when 'acts' already implies practical deeds. The response clarifies that 'af'al' is a general term covering both heart and limb acts, while 'amaliyyah' is a specific qualifier for external acts—thus neither objection stands. This illustrates a key usul principle: a general term (amm) retains its scope unless a specific exclusion (takhsis) is proven.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
Read the fourth and fifth objections carefully. Notice that the fourth targets the definition's scope (exclusion of heart acts like 'Believe'), and the fifth targets internal redundancy (the term 'practical' being superfluous).
2
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response hinges on a linguistic distinction: 'af'al' (acts) is general (amm), including both external and internal actions. The term 'amaliyyah' (practical) is a qualifier specifying external acts, not a repetition. Thus, the definition remains comprehensive and non-redundant.
3
Apply the amm-khass principle
Recognize that the general term 'af'al' covers all acts, and the specific qualifier 'amaliyyah' does not negate that generality but rather restricts the focus in context. This is a standard Hanafi usul tool.
4
Confirm the resolution
Verify that by treating 'af'al' as general, the obligation of heart acts (like tasdiq) are included. And by treating 'amaliyyah' as a separate qualifier, no redundancy occurs. The objections are thereby refuted.

Source Text

اعتراض (۴):- آپ کی تعریف جامع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس سے آمنوا اور فاعتبر واجیسے خطاب نقل جاتے ہیں حالانکہ آمنوا سے وجوب تصدیق کا اور فاعتبروا سے وجوب قیاس کا حکم ہے یہ حکم کی تعریف سے خارج اس طرح ہو رہے ہیں کہ آپ نے کہا المتعلق با فعال المکلفین اور وجوب تصدیق اور وجوب قیاس افعال میں سے نہیں ہیں کیونکہ افعال سے مراد افعال جوارح ہیں

ويقع التكرار بين العملیہ :۔ يہاں سے پانچواں اعتراض ہے۔
اعتراض (۵):۔ آپ کی تعریف میں جو العملیہ کی قید ہے اس میں تکرار ہے کیونکہ حکم سے مراد آپ نے لیا خطاب اللہ تعالٰی المتعلق بافعال المکلفین اور افعال سے مراد اعمال جوارح ہیں اب احکام کی جگہ خطاب اللہ کو ذکر کریں ( کیونکہ حکم کا معنیٰ خطاب اللہ ہے ) تو تعریف کا حاصل ہوگا العلم بخطاب اللہ تعالٰی المتعلق بافعال المکلفین الشرعیة العملیہ پس عملیہ کی قید میں تکرار
لا زم آیا کیونکہ جب عملیہ کی قید؛ افعال لمکلفین کی صورت میں اس حکم میں ماخوذ تھی تو دو بار اس کو ذکر کر محض تکرار ہے۔ الا ان يقال نعنی بالا فعال :۔ يہاں سے دونوں اعتراضوں کا جواب ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ محکم کی تعریف میں جو افعال کا لفظ ہے وہ عام ہے فعل جوارح کو بھی اور فعل قلب کو بھی اور عملیہ سے مراد صرف وہ فعل ہیں جن کا تعلق جوارح کے ساتھ ہے لہذا عملیہ کی قید میں تکرار نہ ہوا اور اسی طرح وجوب تصدیق وغیرہ بھی حکم سے خارج نہ ہوئے کیونکہ افعال کی قید فعل جوارح اور فعل قلب دونوں کو شامل ہے اور وجوب تصدیق وغیرہ کا تعلق دل سے ہے لہذا یہ تعریف میں داخل ہیں۔

And also, 'Believe' and 'So take heed' are excluded. Here the fourth objection is narrated. Objection (4): Your definition is not comprehensive because it excludes addresses like 'Believe' and 'So take heed', whereas from 'Believe' there is a ruling of obligation of affirmation, and from 'So take heed' there is a ruling of obligation of analogy. These are excluded from the definition of hukm in that you said 'related to the acts of the legally responsible', and the obligation of affirmation and the obligation of analogy are not among the acts because by acts you mean acts of the limbs, and these two are not acts of the limbs; rather they are acts of the heart. And redundancy occurs with the term 'practical'. Here the fifth objection is narrated. Objection (5): In your definition, the restriction 'practical' involves redundancy because you have understood hukm as 'the address of Allah the Most High related to the acts of the legally responsible', and by acts you mean works of the limbs. Now if you substitute hukm with 'address of Allah' (since hukm means address of Allah), the definition becomes 'knowledge of the address of Allah related to the acts of the legally responsible, the Shariah-based practical'. Thus the restriction 'practical' entails redundancy, because when the restriction 'practical' was already taken in the form of 'acts of the legally responsible' in this ruling, mentioning it twice is mere repetition. Unless it is said: 'We mean by acts...' Here the answer to both objections is given, the gist of which is that in the definition of hukm, the word 'acts' is general, including both acts of the limbs and acts of the heart, and by 'practical' is meant only those acts that are related to the limbs. Thus there is no redundancy in the restriction 'practical', and similarly the obligation of affirmation etc. are not excluded from the ruling because the restriction 'acts' includes both acts of the limbs and acts of the heart, and the obligation of affirmation etc. are related to the heart. Therefore they are included in the definition. Talwih: His statement 'there occurs to it an indication' points to objections against the definition of hukm along with the answer to some. The first is that the intended meaning is the definition of hukm as a technical term among the jurists, and it is what is established by the address, like obligation, prohibition, and other things that are attributes of the action of the legally responsible, not...
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage presents two more objections to the Ash'ari definition of hukm. The fourth objection argues that commands like 'Believe' (آمنوا) and 'Take heed' (فاعتبروا) are excluded because they involve internal acts (heart's actions) whereas the definition only mentions 'acts of the legally responsible', which the objector interprets as only external limb acts. The fifth objection points out redundancy in the term 'practical' (العملیہ) because if 'acts' already implies practical acts, adding 'practical' is superfluous. The response clarifies that 'acts' in the definition covers both external and internal acts, while 'practical' specifically qualifies external acts, so no redundancy occurs. Hence, obligations of the heart (like affirming faith) are included, and the definition remains comprehensive. The Talwih commentary adds that the definition refers to the technical term among jurists, encompassing attributes of the responsible agent's action.

Key Terms
افعال (af'al): Acts; includes both acts of the limbs (جوارح) and acts of the heart (قلوب) in this context.
العملیہ (al-'amaliyyah): Practical; a qualifying term restricting 'acts' to those performed by the external limbs, to distinguish from internal acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It redefines 'hukm' to exclude internal acts.
D) It accepts the redundancy but considers it stylistically acceptable.

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm is comprehensive: 'af'al' is general, covering internal and external acts, while 'amaliyyah' is a non-redundant specification for external acts.

Refining the Definition of Hukm: Heart Actions and the Non-Redundancy of 'Amaliyya
Refutation of two objections via terminological precision

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school distinguishes fi'l (action) from 'amal (deed) in usul definitions and apply this distinction to rebut objections against the definition of hukm.

Core Idea
The Hanafi definition of hukm includes heart actions via fi'l; 'amaliyya excludes only theoretical rulings, not heart-based obligations.

The Hanafi definition of hukm and fiqh faces two intertwined objections: first, that it excludes rulings related to heart actions (like belief), and second, that the term 'amaliyya (practical) is redundant. The passage defends the definition by clarifying the scope of 'action' (fi'l) and 'deed' ('amal), showing that the objections rest on a misunderstanding of the terms. This lesson will guide you through the precise terminological distinctions that safeguard the Hanafi definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
Read the fourth and fifth objections: the definition excludes heart actions (like obligation of faith), and mentioning 'amaliyya is redundant because 'action' already implies limb acts.
These objections target the definitions of hukm (ruling) and fiqh (jurisprudence).
2
Understand the fi'l/'amal distinction
The response distinguishes fi'l (general, includes heart and limbs) from 'amal (specific to limbs). Accepting that fi'l includes heart actions answers the fourth objection.
This distinction is critical: fiqh deals with 'amal (limb actions), but the definition of hukm uses the broader fi'l.
3
Apply the distinction to the redundancy claim
Even if hukm uses fi'l broadly, the term 'amaliyya in fiqh's definition is not redundant because it explicitly excludes theoretical matters that do not involve limb actions, such as purely doctrinal beliefs.
Thus 'amaliyya serves a precise limiting function.
4
Analyze the counterargument
The objector argues that if hukm is taken in its technical sense, 'amaliyya becomes redundant. The response shows that this would incorrectly include matters like the authority of ijma into fiqh, which is undesirable.
This demonstrates that the technical definition must align with the purpose of fiqh.
5
Conclude the refinement
The passage concludes that the Hanafi definition stands firm when the fi'l/'amal distinction is maintained, and 'amaliyya retains its non-redundant role.
This is a classic example of critical refinement in usul al-fiqh.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرَّابِعُ أَنَّهُ غَيْرُ شَامِلٍ لِلاحْكامِ الْمُتَعَلَّقَةِ بِأَفْعَالِ الْقَلْبِ ، مِثْلُ وُجُوبِ الْإِيمَانِ أَى التَّصْدِيقِ وَوُجُوبِ الاعْتِبَارِ أَى الْقِيَاسِ ؛ لأنَّ الظَّاهِرَ مِنَ الْأَفْعَالِ أَفْعَالُ الْجَوَارِحِ.
الخَامِسُ أَنَّهُ لَمَّا أَخَذَ فِى تَعْرِيفِ الْحُكْمِ الْمُتَعَلّقِ بِفِعْل الْمُكَلَّفِ اخْتَصَّ بِالْعَمَلِيَّاتِ وَخَرَجَتْ النَّظَرِيَّاتُ بِنَاءً عَلَى اخْتِصَاصِ الْفِعْلِ بِالْجَوَارِحِ فَيَكُونُ ذِكْرُ الْعَمَلِيَّةِ فِي تَعْرِيفِ الْفِقْهِ مُكَرَّرًا وَأَجَابَ عَنْهُمَا بِأَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِالْفِعْلِ مَا يَعُمُ الْقَلْبَ وَالْجَوَارِحَ وَبِالْعَمَلِ مَا يَخُصُّ الْجَوَارِحَ فَلا يَخْرُجُ مِثْلُ وُجُوبِ الْإِيمَانِ وَالِاعْتِبَارِ عَنْ تَعْرِيفِ الْحُكْمِ وَلَا يَكُونُ ذِكْرُ الْعَمَلِيَّةِ مُكَرَّرًا لِإِفَادَتِهِ خُرُوجَ مَا لَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِفِعْلِ الْجَوَارِحِ عَنْ تَعْرِيفِ الْفِقْهِ وَلِقَائِلِ أَنْ يَقُولَ إِذَا حُمِلَ الْحُكْمُ فِي تَعْرِيفِ الْفِقْهِ عَلَى الْمُصْطَلَحٍ فَذِكْرُ الْعَمَلِيَّةِ مُكَرَّرٌ قَطْعًا ؛ لأنَّ مِثْلَ وُجُوبِ الْإِيمَانِ خَارِجٌ بِقَيْدِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ وَمِثْلَ كَوْنِ الْإِجْمَاعِ حُجَّةً غَيْرُ دَاخِل فِى الْحُكْمِ الْمُصْطَلَحِ لِخُرُوجِهِ بِقَيْدِ الِاقْتِضَاء أَو التَّخْسِيرِ لَا يُقَالُ مَعْنَى كَوْنِ السُّنَّةِ وَالْإِجْمَاعِ وَالْقِيَاسِ حُجَجًا وُجُوبُ الْعَمَلِ بِمُقْتَضَاهَا فَيَدْخُلُ فِي الاقْتِصَاءِ الصِّمُنِيُّ ؛ لأنَّا نَقُولُ فَحِينَئِذٍ لَا يَخْرُجُ بِقَيْدِ العَمَلِيَّةِ وَيَلْزَمُ أنْ يَكُونَ العِلْمُ بِهِ مِنْ الْفِقْهِ وَيُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُقَالَ
إِنَّ التَّقْسِيدَ بِالْعَمَلِيَّةِ يُفَسِدُ إِخْرَاجَ مِثْلِ جَوَازِ الْإِجْمَاعِ وَوُجُوبِ الْقِيَاسِ ، وَهُوَ حُكُمْ شَرْعِيٌّ ترجمہ:۔ اور نہیں وارد ہوتا یہ سوال اس شخص کے مذہب پر جس نے تعریف کی ہے حکم کی اس تعریف مذکور کے ساتھ پس بیشک
The fourth: that it does not include the rulings related to actions of the heart, such as the obligation of faith, i.e., belief, and the obligation of consideration, i.e., qiyas, because the apparent meaning of 'actions' is actions of the limbs. The fifth: that when he took in the definition of hukm what is related to the action of the mukallaf, it is restricted to practical matters, and theoretical matters are excluded, based on the restriction of 'action' to the limbs, so mentioning 'amaliyya (practical) in the definition of fiqh would be redundant. And he answered both [objections] that by 'action' is meant what includes both heart and limbs, and by 'amal (work/deed) is meant what is specific to the limbs. So something like the obligation of faith and consideration is not excluded from the definition of hukm, and mentioning 'amaliyya is not redundant because it benefits the exclusion of what does not pertain to the action of the limbs from the definition of fiqh. And if someone says: When hukm in the definition of fiqh is taken in the technical sense, then mentioning 'amaliyya is definitely redundant, because something like the obligation of faith is excluded by the condition of shari' (as previously mentioned), and something like the fact that ijma is a proof does not enter into the technical hukm because it is excluded by the condition of iqtida' or takhyir? It cannot be said that the meaning of the Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas being proofs is the obligation of acting upon their implications, so it enters into iqtida' (necessity). Because we say: Then in that case it is not excluded by the condition of 'amaliyya, and it would be necessary that knowledge of it is part of fiqh. And it can be said that the restriction by 'amaliyya spoils the exclusion of something like the permissibility of ijma and the obligation of qiyas, and it is a shari' ruling. Translation: And this objection does not arise according to the school of the one who defined hukm with this mentioned definition, so indeed...
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth and fifth objections together with a combined response. The fourth objection is that the definition of hukm excludes rulings related to heart actions (e.g., obligation of belief and obligation of qiyas as a mental act). The fifth objection is that since 'action' (fi'l) is commonly understood only as limb actions, the definition becomes restricted to practical matters (amaliyya), making the term 'amaliyya in the definition of fiqh redundant (since fiqh is already defined as knowledge of practical rulings). The response is that 'action' in the definition of hukm includes both heart and limb actions, so heart-related rulings are included. As for the term 'amaliyya in the definition of fiqh, it is not redundant because it specifically excludes rulings that do not involve limb actions, such as purely theoretical beliefs (like the attributes of Allah) that are not acts of the limbs. The passage then addresses a counterargument: if 'hukm' in the definition of fiqh is taken in its technical sense (as the address of Allah), then things like the obligation of faith are already excluded by the condition 'shar'i' (since they are rational or doctrinal), and things like the authority of ijma do not fit the technical definition of hukm because they are not necessarily binding in the same sense. The response argues that if we interpret the authority of proofs as 'obligation to act on their implications,' then they would enter the definition of hukm, and knowledge of them would be part of fiqh; but the restriction by 'amaliyya would then fail to exclude them. The commentator concludes that defining hukm in a particular way avoids all these objections.

Key Terms
فعل القلب (fi'l al-qalb): Action of the heart, such as belief (iman) and intellectual consideration (i'tibar).
فعل الجوارح (fi'l al-jawarih): Action of the limbs, such as prayer, fasting, etc.
عملي (amali): Practical, pertaining to actions of the limbs.
نظري (nazari): Theoretical, pertaining to matters of belief or abstract reasoning.
فقه (fiqh): Knowledge of the practical shari' rulings derived from their detailed proofs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the term 'amaliyya (practical) not considered redundant in the definition of fiqh according to the response?
A) Because it restricts fiqh to rulings derived from the Quran and Sunnah.
B) Because it excludes rulings that do not involve actions of the limbs, such as purely doctrinal matters.
C) Because it includes actions of the heart.
D) Because it emphasizes that fiqh is only about worship.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm uses fi'l to include heart actions and retains 'amaliyya in fiqh to exclude theoretical matters, making both terms non-redundant and precise.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
Distinguishing Kull Kullī from Kull Fardī in Ijtihād
Critical refinement of matn's classification and rebuttal of objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish kull kullī from kull fardī in terms of temporal scope and apply the relationship of ʿumūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh to resolve objections about the classification of aḥkām in ijtihād.

Core Idea
Kull kullī covers past+future (infinite), kull fardī covers only past (finite) — distinct by scope.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary on Al-Tawḍīḥ tackles a subtle objection: are total collective and total individual the same when applied to legal rulings? The commentator refines the matn's classification by clarifying that kull kullī includes all rulings until Judgment Day, while kull fardī includes only those up to the mujtahid's time. This distinction preserves the validity of the original three-probability division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Categories
The matn mentions three probabilities for interpreting 'aḥkām' in ijtihad: kull kullī (total collective), kull fardī (total individual), and baʿḍ muʿayyan (some specific). A critic raises a fifth probability: some specific rulings not attributed to the whole.
The commentator absorbs this fifth probability into kull fardī.
2
Understand the Objection
Some argue that in the context of knowledge of aḥkām, kull kullī and kull fardī are identical, because knowing all rulings collectively implies knowing each individually, and vice versa. If so, the matn's division into two distinct types is invalid.
The objection relies on an assumed synonymy.
3
Examine the Counter-Responses
A flawed response claims that kull kullī is general (ʿāmm) and kull fardī is specific (khāṣṣ). The commentator refutes this because if kull kullī included only some rulings, the author's evidence of non-finiteness would not apply.
The commentator then provides his own resolution.
4
Apply the Commentator's Resolution
Kull kullī refers to all rulings past and future (infinite), proven by the evidence of non-finiteness; kull fardī refers only to past rulings (finite), proven by the evidence of lā adrī (I do not know). They are distinct with a ʿumūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh relationship.
This preserves the matn's classification as valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوال:۔ وہ یہ ہے کہ چار احتمال نہیں بلکہ پانچواں احتمال بھی ہے کہ بعض متعین احکام مراد ہوں لیکن ان کی نسبت کل کی طرف نہ ہو مثلا دو ہزار یا چار ہزار مسائل ہوں یہ مراد لیا جا سکتا ہے لہذا اچار میں حضر درست نہیں ہے یہ احتمال کیوں نہیں ذکر کیا جواب:۔ کہ بعض متعین جن کی نسبت کل کی طرف نہ ہو یہ کل واحد میں داخل ہیں۔ کیونکہ وہ بھی متعین ہوتے ہیں لہذا جب آپ ایک ہزار کی تعین کرتے ہیں مثلا فقیہ وہ ہے جو ایک ہزار مسائل مستقبط کر سکتا ہے تو ہوسکتا ہے کہ کوئی فقیہ انہیں سے بعض کا جواب نہ دے سکے تو یہ کل واحد میں داخل ہے سوال :۔ یہ ہے کہ نصف سے اکثر مجہول نہیں اس لئے کہ اگر کل مجہول ہیں تو یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ اکثر بھی مجہول ہوں ہو سکتا ہے کہ اکثر یقینی ہوں اور کل مجہول ہوں جس طرح گندم کا ڈھیر دو حصوں میں تقسیم کریں ایک حصہ بڑا ہے اور ایک حصہ چھوٹا ہے اب کل مجہول ہے لیکن اکثر یقینی ہے؟ جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ مسائل کو گندم پر قیاس نہیں کیا جا سکتا یہ مسائل ایسے ہیں کہ ان کو ضبط نہیں کیا جاسکتا نہ حواس ظاہرہ سے اور نہ حواس باطنہ سے اور گندم کو حواس ظاہرہ سے یعنی آنکھ سے ضبط کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ لھذا اس پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہوگا۔ ماتن نے چوتھا احتمال اجمالا بیان کیا ہے
و هذا مذکور: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شارع سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال: یہ ہے کہ چوتھا احتمال ماتن نے بیان نہیں کیا ماتن نے صرف تین احتمال بیان کئے تھے (۱) کل مجموعی (۲) کل واحد یعنی کل افرادی اور (۳) بعض متعین اور بعض غیر متعین کو ماتن نے ذکر نہیں کیا۔
جواب:- شاریخ نے کہا کہ اعتراض کے اندر فی الجملہ ذکر کر دیا ہے کہ جب مصنف نے فرمایا کہ احکام سے بعض مسائل مراد نہیں وان قل تو اس سے اس احتمال کی بھی نفی ہو گئی اس لئے دوبارہ اعتراض میں اسکی صراحت نہیں کی بلکہ لفظ ثم سے اشارہ کر دیا یعنی جس طرح بعض غیر متعین احکام مراد نہیں لے سکتے اس طرح کل مجموعی یا کل واحد یا بعض متعین احکام بھی مراد نہیں لے سکتے۔
وہنا بحث:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے غرض شارع ماتن پر اعتراض کرنا ہے اس سے پہلے ایک مقدمہ کا جاننا ضروری ہے بطور تمہید کے۔
مقدمہ: کل مجموعی اور کل افرادی کے درمیان نسبت عموم خصوص من وجہ کی ہے بعض اوقات دونوں جمع ہو نگے بعض اوقات کل مجموعی ہو گا کل افرادی نہیں ہو گا اور بعض اوقات کل افرادی ہو گا کل مجموعی نہیں ہو گا مثلا کل القوم برفع ہذا الحجر یعنی قوم کا مجموعه افراد مل کر پتھر اٹھا سکتا ہے لیکن کل واحد نہیں اٹھا سکتا تو کل مجموعی ہے کل افرادی نہیں ہے اور کل واحد من الناس یکفیہ ہذا الطعام اس مثال میں کل انفرادی ہے کل مجموعی نہیں کیونکہ طعام سب کے مجموعہ کو کافی نہیں ہے اور کبھی دونوں جمع ہو جاتے ہیں جیسے ضربت کل القوم یہ مجموعہ پر بھی صادق ہے کل واحد پر بھی صادق ہے کہ مجموعہ افراد کی پٹائی علیحدہ علیحدہ کی پٹائی کو ستلزم ہے وکل واحد کی پٹائی مجموعہ کی پٹائی کو ستلزم ہے۔ سوال:۔ یہ ہے کہ یہ علم بالا حکام اس کے قبیل سے ہے کہ یہاں کل مجموعی بھی اور کل افرادی بھی صادق آتا ہے یعنی تمام احکام کے مجموعہ کو پہچان لیں یا ہر ہر حکم کو پہچان لیں جب دونوں ایک ہی چیز ہیں تو ماتن کا کل مجموعی اور کل واحد کے درمیان تقابل کرنا اور ان کی تقسیم کرنا اور ان کی دو قسمیں بنا نا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
وان التزم : ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے غرض بعض حضرات کے جواب کو ذکر کر کے اس پر رد کرتا ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بعض نے جواب دیا کہ تقابل صحیح ہے کیونکہ کل مجموعی عام ہے اور کل افرادی خاص ہے یعنی کل مجموعی جس سے تمام احکام مراد ہوں یا بعض یہ عام ہے اور کل واحد سے مراد ہر ہر حکم لیا ہے یہ خاص ہے یہ فرق ہے اس بناء پر تقابل صحیح ہے۔ رو شارح:۔ اس جواب کو شاریخ نے رد کیا ہے کہ اگر کل مجموعی سے مراد عام ہے کہ کل احکام مراد لیں یا بعض تو ماتن نے جو دلیل دی ہے اس پر کہ کل مجموعی مراد نہیں لے سکتے کیونکہ یہ احکام غیر متناہی ہیں تو یہ عدم تناہی اس وقت دلیل بن سکتی ہے جب سب احکام مراد ہوں اور اگر یہ عام ہو مجموعہ احکام کو اور بعض کو تو یہ دلیل ذکر کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔
والظاہرانہ:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض:۔ اس میں شارخ نے اپنی طرف سے جواب دیا ہے۔ جواب: کل مجموعی سے مراد وہ احکام ہیں جو مجتہد کے زمانہ سے پہلے گزر چکے ہیں اور قیامت تک آنے والے ہیں یہ سب مراد ہیں اور کل واحد سے مراد وہ احکام ہیں جو مجتہد کے زمانہ تک گذر چکے قرینہ یہ ہے کہ کل مجموعی مراد نہ لینے پر دلیل عدم تناہی والی دی ہے یہ دلیل اس وقت بن سکتی ہے جب احکام ماضیہ اور آتیہ سب مراد ہوں اور کل واحد پر دلیل ثبوت لا ادری کے ساتھ دی ہے اور لا ادری اسی وقت ہو گا جب پہلے احکام موجود ہوں تو معلوم ہوا کہ کل واحد والا حکم احکام ماضیہ کے لئے ہے اور کل مجموعی کا حکم احکام ماضیہ اور آسیہ دونوں کے لئے ہے تو اب تقابل صحیح ہے۔
Question: That is, there are not four probabilities, but rather a fifth probability: that some specific rulings are intended but their attribution to the whole is not made – for example, two thousand or four thousand issues could be intended. So why is this probability not mentioned? Answer: That some specific rulings not attributed to the whole are included in the ‘total individual’. Because they are also specific. Hence, when you specify one thousand – for example, a jurist is one who can derive one thousand issues – then it is possible that a jurist cannot answer some of them; so that is included in the total individual. Question: That is, half to most is not unknown, because if the whole is unknown, it does not necessarily follow that most is also unknown. It is possible that most is certain while the whole is unknown – just as a heap of wheat divided into two parts, one large and one small; the whole is unknown but most is certain? Answer: That issues cannot be analogized to wheat. These issues cannot be grasped, neither by the external senses nor by the internal senses, whereas wheat can be grasped by the external senses, i.e., by the eye. Hence, analogizing to it would be analogizing with a difference. The author (matn) mentioned the fourth probability in summary. 'And this is mentioned': This is the second part of the commentary’s statement; the objective is for the commentator to answer an implicit question. The question is that the author did not mention the fourth probability; the author only mentioned three probabilities: (1) total collective (kull kullī), (2) total individual (kull fardī), and (3) some specific; some unspecific was not mentioned by the author. Answer: The commentator said that the objection within it (the matn) mentions it in brief: when the author said that some issues are not intended from the rulings, then that probability is also negated. Therefore, he did not specify it again in the objection, but indicated with the word ‘thumma’ – just as some unspecific rulings cannot be intended, similarly total collective or total individual or some specific rulings cannot be intended. 'And here is a discussion': This is the third part of the commentary’s statement; the objective is for the commentator to criticize the author. Before that, it is necessary to know a preamble as an introduction. Preamble: The relationship between total collective and total individual is the relationship of general and specific in one respect. Sometimes both combine, sometimes there is total collective without total individual, and sometimes total individual without total collective. For example, “The entire people lift this stone” – meaning the collective of the people can lift the stone, but each individual cannot; so it is total collective, not total individual. And “Each individual among the people suffices for this food” – in this example, it is total individual, not total collective, because the food does not suffice for the entire collective. And sometimes both combine, such as “I beat the entire people” – this applies to the collective and also to each individual, because beating the collective entails beating each individual severally, and beating each individual entails beating the collective. Question: That is, this knowledge of the rulings is of a type where both total collective and total individual apply – i.e., recognizing the entire set of rulings or recognizing each ruling. When both are the same thing, then the author’s contrast between total collective and total individual and their division into two types is incorrect. 'And if he insists': This is the fourth part of the commentary’s statement; the objective is to mention the response of some people and then refute it. The summary is that some responded that the contrast is correct because total collective is general and total individual is specific – i.e., total collective meaning all rulings or some – this is general, and total individual meaning each ruling – this is specific. This is the difference; based on this, the contrast is correct. The commentator refuted this response, saying that if total collective intends general, meaning all rulings or some, then the author’s evidence that total collective cannot be intended because these rulings are non-finite – this non-finiteness can only be evidence when all rulings are intended. If it is general, including the totality of rulings and some, then citing this evidence is not correct. 'And the apparent is that': This is the fifth part of the commentary’s statement. Objective: In it, the commentator gives his own response. Answer: Total collective refers to those rulings that occurred before the time of the mujtahid and those that will occur until the Day of Judgment – all are intended. Total individual refers to those rulings that occurred up to the time of the mujtahid. The clue is that the evidence of non-finiteness given for not taking total collective applies when both past and future rulings are intended. For total individual, the evidence is given with the proof of ‘lā adrī’ (I do not know), and ‘lā adrī’ only occurs when previous rulings exist. So it is known that the ruling regarding total individual is for past rulings, and the ruling regarding total collective is for both past and future rulings. Thus, the contrast is correct.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from a commentary on Al-Tawḍīḥ, where the commentator (Shāriḥ) addresses a series of objections and counter-arguments about the classification of aḥkām (legal rulings) into three types: total collective (kull kullī), total individual (kull fardī), and some specific (baʿḍ muʿayyan). The author (Mātin) had mentioned only three probabilities, but a critic raises a fifth probability: that some specific rulings (e.g., two thousand or four thousand issues) could be intended without attributing them to the whole. The commentator answers that such specific rulings fall under the ‘total individual’ category because they are also specific. Another objection questions whether ‘half to most’ being unknown is problematic: the critic argues that most can be certain even if the whole is unknown, using the analogy of a heap of wheat. The commentator rejects this analogy because legal issues (masā’il) cannot be grasped by the senses, unlike wheat, making the analogy invalid. Then, the discussion turns to the relationship between total collective and total individual. The preamble explains they have a relationship of general and specific in one respect (ʿumūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh): sometimes both combine, sometimes only one applies, with examples like ‘the entire people lift a stone’ (only collective) and ‘each individual suffices for this food’ (only individual). A critic argues that in the context of knowledge of aḥkām, total collective and total individual are the same, so the author’s distinction is incorrect. The commentator then presents a response from some who claim they are different because total collective is general (including all or some rulings) and total individual is specific (each ruling). The commentator refutes this by showing that if total collective includes only some rulings, then the author’s argument about non-finiteness fails. Finally, the commentator gives his own resolution: total collective refers to all past and future rulings (infinite), while total individual refers only to past rulings (finite). This preserves the distinction and validates the author’s contrast.

Key Terms
کل مجموعی (kull kullī): The total collective set of rulings, including all past and future rulings
کل افرادی (kull fardī): The total individual rulings, i.e., each ruling individually, but limited to those occurring up to the mujtahid’s time
لا ادری (lā adrī): The statement ‘I do not know’, used by the mujtahid to indicate ignorance of some specific past rulings
عموم خصوص من وجہ (ʿumūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh): A relationship where two terms overlap in some respects but differ in others, i.e., general and specific in one aspect

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the difference between kull kullī (total collective) and kull fardī (total individual) in terms of temporal scope?
A) Both include past rulings only.
B) Kull kullī includes past and future rulings, while kull fardī includes only past rulings.
C) Kull kullī includes only future rulings, while kull fardī includes past rulings.
D) Both include past and future rulings.

Key Takeaway
The classification of rulings into kull kullī and kull fardī is valid because the commentator clarified they differ in temporal scope (infinite vs. finite), thereby resolving the objection of synonymy and preserving the matn's tripartite division.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
Collective vs Individual Whole in Knowledge of Ahkam
Analyzes ratio of collective/individual whole in fiqh knowledge definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi definition of knowledge (ʿilm) of rulings as a faculty (malaka) by distinguishing the collective and individual whole and critiquing the readiness (tahayyuʾ) theory.

Core Idea
Knowledge of rulings is a faculty enabling derivation, not readiness or actual knowledge of infinite rulings.

This lesson examines a foundational debate in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: how should we define 'knowledge of rulings'? The author analyzes the logical relationship between collective and individual wholes to argue that the Hanafi definition—knowledge as a faculty (malaka)—is superior to the alternative 'readiness' (tahayyuʾ) theory of Ibn al-Ḥājib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the precise definition of knowledge (ʿilm) of rulings in fiqh? The passage contrasts two views.
This sets up the debate.
2
Understand the collective vs individual whole distinction
The author uses examples (lifting a stone, food sufficiency, beating a group) to show the ratio (عموم خصوص من وجه) between collective whole (کل مجموعی) and individual whole (کل افرادی).
These examples illustrate the logical relationship.
3
Examine the Hanafi critique of Ibn al-Ḥājib's readiness theory
The author refutes readiness by arguing that remote readiness exists in non-jurists and near readiness is undefined, and that the word ʿilm indicates a faculty, not readiness.
This is the core of the critical refinement.
4
Analyze the four refutation points from the Arabic section
The author gives four counterarguments: (1) error/ignorance does not negate readiness; (2) no ruling is beyond ijtihad (hadith of Muʿādh); (3) linguistic evidence for malaka; (4) comparison of knowledge and life.
These systematically dismantle the readiness theory.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi position
Learn how the Hanafi school defines ʿilm al-fiqh as a malaka, which explains how a mujtahid can know infinite rulings potentially.
This is the mufta bihi position.

مقدمہ: کل مجموعی اور کل افرادی کے درمیان نسبت عموم خصوص من وجہ کی ہے بعض اوقات دونوں جمع ہو نگے بعض اوقات کل مجموعی ہو گا کل افرادی نہیں ہو گا اور بعض اوقات کل افرادی ہو گا کل مجموعی نہیں ہو گا مثلا کل القوم برفع ہذا الحجر یعنی قوم کا مجموعه افراد مل کر پتھر اٹھا سکتا ہے لیکن کل واحد نہیں اٹھا سکتا تو کل مجموعی ہے کل افرادی نہیں ہے اور کل واحد من الناس یکفیہ ہذا الطعام اس مثال میں کل انفرادی ہے کل مجموعی نہیں کیونکہ طعام سب کے مجموعہ کو کافی نہیں ہے اور کبھی دونوں جمع ہو جاتے ہیں جیسے ضربت کل القوم یہ مجموعہ پر بھی صادق ہے کل واحد پر بھی صادق ہے کہ مجموعہ افراد کی پٹائی علیحدہ علیحدہ کی پٹائی کو ستلزم ہے ورکل واحد کی پٹائی مجموعہ کی پٹائی کو ستلزم ہے۔ سوال:۔ یہ ہے کہ یہ علم بالا حکام اس کے قبیل سے ہے کہ یہاں کل مجموعی بھی اور کل افرادی بھی صادق آتا ہے یعنی تمام احکام کے مجموعہ کو پہچان لیں یا ہر ہر حکم کو پہچان لیں جب دونوں ایک ہی چیز ہیں تو ماتن کا کل مجموعی اور کل واحد کے درمیان تقابل کرنا اور ان کی تقسیم کرنا اور ان کی دو قسمیں بنا نا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
وان التزم : ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے غرض بعض حضرات کے جواب کو ذکر کر کے اس پر رد کرتا ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بعض نے جواب دیا کہ تقابل صحیح ہے کیونکہ کل مجموعی عام ہے اور کل افرادی خاص ہے یعنی کل مجموعی جس سے تمام احکام مراد ہوں یا بعض یہ عام ہے اور کل واحد سے مراد ہر ہر حکم لیا ہے یہ خاص نے یہ فرق ہے اس بناء پر تقابل صحیح ہے۔ رو شارح:۔ اس جواب کو شاریخ نے رد کیا ہے کہ اگر کل مجموعی سے مراد عام ہے کہ کل احکام مراد لیں یا بعض تو مانتن نے جو دلیل دی ہے اس پر کہ کل مجموعی مراد نہیں لے سکتے کیونکہ یہ احکام غیر متناہی ہیں تو یہ عدم تنا ہی اس وقت دلیل بن سکتی ہے جب سب احکام مراد ہوں اور اگر یہ عام ہو مجموعہ احکام کو اور بعض کو تو یہ دلیل ذکر کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔
والظاہرانہ:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض:۔ اس میں شارخ نے اپنی طرف سے جواب دیا ہے۔ جواب: کل مجموعی سے مراد وہ احکام ہیں جو مجتہد کے زمانہ سے پہلے گزر چکے ہیں اور قیامت تک آنے والے ہیں یہ سب مراد ہیں اور کل واحد سے مراد وہ احکام ہیں جو مجتہد کے زمانہ تک گذر چکے قرینہ یہ ہے کہ کل مجموعی مراد نہ لینے پر دلیل عدم تنا ہی والی دی ہے یہ دلیل اس وقت بن سکتی ہے جب احکام ماضیہ اور آتیہ سب مراد ہوں اور کل واحد پر دلیل ثبوت لا ادری کے ساتھ دی ہے اور لا ادری اسی وقت ہو گا جب پہلے احکام موجود ہوں تو معلوم ہوا کہ کل واحد والا حکم احکام ماضیہ کے لئے ہے اور کل مجموعی کا حکم احکام ماضیہ اور آسیہ دونوں کے لئے ہے تو اب تقابل صحیح ہے۔
وَلَمَّا أَجَابَ ابْنُ الْحَاجِبِ بِأَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِالْأحْكَامِ الْمَجُمُوعُ ، وَمَعْنَى الْعِلْمِ بِهَا التَّهَيُّؤُ لِذَلِكَ رَدَّهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ بِأَنَّ التَّهَيُّوَ الْبَعِيدَ حَاصِلٌ لِغَيْرِ الْفَقِيهِ ، وَالْقَرِيبُ غَيْرُ مَضْبُوطٍ ، إِذْ لَا يُعْرَف أَنَّ أَى قَدْرٍ مِنْ الاسْتِعْدَادِ يُقَالُ لَهُ التَّهَيُّزُ الْقَرِيبُ وَلَمَّا فَسَّرَ التهيؤ يكون الشخص بِحَيْثُ يَعْلَمُ بِالاجْتِهَادِ حُكْمَ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْحَوَادِثِ لاسْتِجُمَاعِهِ الْمَآخِذَ وَالْأَسْبَابَ وَالشَّرَائِطَ الَّتِي يَتَمَكَّنُ بِهَا مِنْ تَحْصِيلِهَا وَيَكْفِيهِ الرُّجُوعُ إِلَيْهَا فِي مَعْرِفَةِ الْأَحْكَامِ رَدَّهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ بِأَرْبَعَةِ أَوْجُهِ يُمْكِنُ الجَوَابُ عَنْهَا بِأَنَّا لَا نُسَلّمُ أَنَّ عَدَمَ تَيَسُّرِ مَعْرِفَةِ بَعْضِ الْأَحْكَامِ لِبَعْضِ الْفُقَهَاءِ أَوْ الْخَطَأَ فِي الاجْتِهَادِ يُنَافِى التَّهَيُّوَ بِالْمَعْنَى الْمَذْكُورِ لِجَوَازِ أَن يَكُونَ ذَلِكَ لِتَعَارُض الأدِلَّةِ أو وُجُودِ الْمَوَانِعِ أَوْ مُعَارَضَةِ الْوَهُمِ الْعَقْلِى أَوْ مُشَاكَلَةِ الْحَقِّ الْبَاطِلَ وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ وَلَا تُسَلَّمُ أَنَّ شَيْئًا مِنْ الْأَحْكَامِ الَّتِى لَمْ يَرِدُ بِهَا نَضٌ وَلَا إِجْمَاعٌ يَكُونُ بِحَيْثُ لَا مَسَاعَ فِيهِ لِلاجْتِهَادِ وَيَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ حَدِيثُ مُعَاذِ رَصَى اللَّهُ عَنْهُ حَيْثُ اعْتَمَدَ الاجْتِهَادَ بِرَابِهِ فِيمَا لَا يَجِدُ فِيهِ النَّصَّ وَلَمْ يَقُلِ النَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مَحَلٌّ لِلاجْتِهَادِ وَلَا نُسَلِّمُ أَنْ لَا دَلَالَةَ لِلَفْظِ الْعِلْمِ عَلَى التَّهَيُّرِ الْمَخْصُوصِ فَإِنَّ مَعْنَاهُ مَلَكَةٌ يَقْتَدِرُ بِهَا عَلَى إدْرَاكِ جُزْئِيَّاتِ الْأَحْكَامِ ، وَإِطْلَاقُ الْعِلْمِ عَلَيْهَا شَائِعٌ ذَائِعٌ فِي الْعُرْفِ كَقَوْلِهِمْ فِى تَعْرِيفِ الْعُلُومِ عِلْمُ كَذَا وَكَذَا فَإِنَّ الْمُحَقِّقِينَ عَلَى أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِهِ هَذِهِ الْمَلِكَةُ وَيُقَالُ لَهَا أَيْضًا الصَّنَاعَةُ لَا نَفْسُ الْإِدْرَاكِ وَكَقَوْلِهِمْ وَجُهُ الشَّبَهِ بَيْنَ الْعِلْمِ وَالْحَيَاةِ كَوْنُهُمَا جِهَتَى الْإِدْرَاكِ .
ترجمہ:۔ اور جب جواب دیا ابن حاجب نے کہ مراد ا حکام سے مجموعہ احکام ہیں اور علم کا معنیٰ اس کے ساتھ نہیں ہے اس (علم) کے لئے ۔ رد کیا ہے اس کو مصنف نے بایں طور کہ تہیہ بعیدی حاصل ہوتی ہے غیر فقیہ کو بھی اور قریبی غیر منضبط ہے اس لئے نہیں۔ پہچانی جاتی یہ بات کہ کتنی مقدار ہے استعداد میں سے کہ کہا جائے اسکو جہیو قریبی ۔ اور جب تفسیر کی اس (ابن حاجب) نے
Introduction: The relationship between the collective whole and the individual whole is that of general-special from one perspective. Sometimes both come together, sometimes the collective whole exists but not the individual, sometimes the individual whole exists but not the collective. For example: "The whole group lifts this stone" – the collective individuals of the group together can lift the stone, but each individual cannot. So it is collective whole, not individual whole. And "Each individual of the people is satisfied with this food" – here it is individual whole, not collective, because the food is not sufficient for the whole group. Sometimes both come together, like "I beat the whole group" – this applies to the collective and also to each individual because beating the group implies beating each individual separately, and beating each individual implies beating the group. Question: This knowledge of rulings is of the type where both the collective whole and the individual whole apply? That is, one knows the totality of all rulings or each individual ruling? When both are the same thing, the author's comparison between collective whole and individual whole and their division into two types is not correct.

"Wa in iltazam" – This is the fourth part of the commentary. The point: He mentions the response of some people and then refutes it. Summary: Some responded that the comparison is correct because the collective whole is general and the individual whole is specific. That is, the collective whole from which all rulings are intended or some – this is general, and the individual whole from which each individual ruling is intended – this is specific. Based on this difference, the comparison is correct. The commentator refuted this response: If by collective whole is meant the general that includes all rulings or some, then the proof given by the author that the collective whole cannot be intended because these rulings are infinite – this proof can only count when all rulings are intended. But if it is general to the collection and some, then mentioning this proof is not correct.

"Wa al-zahir anna" – This is the fifth part of the commentary. The point: The commentator gives a response from himself. Answer: By collective whole is meant those rulings that passed before the time of the mujtahid and those that will come until the Day of Judgment – all are intended. By individual whole is meant the rulings that passed up to the time of the mujtahid. The indication is that for not intending the collective whole, he gave the proof of infinitude; this proof can only apply when both past and future rulings are intended. And for the individual whole, he gave the proof with "la adri" (I do not know), and "la adri" only applies when previous rulings exist. So it becomes clear that the individual whole ruling is for past rulings, and the collective whole ruling is for both past and future rulings. Hence the comparison is correct.

"Wa lamma ajaba Ibn al-Hajib bi anna al-murada bi al-ahkam al-majmu', wa ma'na al-ilm biha al-tahayyu' li-dhalika raddahu al-musannif bi anna al-tahayyu' al-ba'ida hasilun li-ghayr al-faqih, wa al-qarib ghayru mabdut, idh la yu'raf anna ayyu qadrin min al-isti'dad yuqalu lahu al-tahayyu' al-qarib. Wa lamma fassara al-tahayyu' bi-anna al-shakhs bi-haythu ya'lamu bi al-ijtihadi hukma kulli wahidin min al-hawadith li-istijma'ihi al-ma'akhidha wa al-asbaba wa al-shara'ita allati yatamakkanu biha min tahsiliha wa yakfihi al-ruju'u ilayha fi ma'rifati al-ahkam raddahu al-musannif bi-arba'ati awjuhin yumkinu al-jawabu 'anha bi anna la nusallimu anna 'adama tayassuri ma'rifati ba'di al-ahkam li-ba'di al-fuqaha' aw al-khata'a fi al-ijtihadi yunafi al-tahayyu'a bi al-ma'na al-madhkur li-jawazi an yakuna dhalika li-ta'arudi al-adillati aw wujudi al-mawani'i aw mu'aradati al-wahmi al-'aqliyyi aw mushakalati al-haqqi al-batila wa nahwi dhalik. Wa la nusallimu anna shay'an min al-ahkami allati lam yarid biha nassun wa la ijma'un yakunu bi-haythu la masa'a fihi li al-ijtihadi wa yadullu 'alayhi hadithu Mu'adh radiya Allahu 'anhu haythu i'tamada al-ijtihada bi-ra'yihi fima la yajidu fihi al-nassa wa lam yaquli al-nabiyyu 'alayhi al-salamu fa in lam yakun mahallun li al-ijtihadi. Wa la nusallimu anna la dalalata li-lafzi al-ilm 'ala al-tahayyu'i al-makhsusi fa inna ma'anahu malakatun yaqtadiru biha 'ala idraki juz'iyyati al-ahkam, wa itlaqu al-ilm 'alayha sha'i'un dha'i'un fi al-'urfi ka-qawlihim fi ta'rifi al-'ulumi 'ilmu kadha wa kadha fa inna al-muhaqqiqina 'ala anna al-murada bihi hadhihi al-malakat, wa yuqalu laha aydan al-sina'atu la nafsu al-idraki wa ka-qawlihim wajhu al-shabahi bayna al-ilm wa al-hayati kawnuhuma jihata al-idraki.

Translation: And when Ibn al-Hajib answered that the intended meaning of rulings is the collection, and the meaning of knowledge of them is readiness for that, the author refuted him that remote readiness is attained by non-jurists as well, and near readiness is not well-defined, since it is not known what amount of aptitude is called near readiness. And when he interpreted readiness as the person being such that by ijtihad he knows the ruling of each incident because he has gathered the sources, causes, and conditions by which he can obtain them, and it suffices for him to refer to them in knowing the rulings, the author refuted him with four points, to which a response is possible: [First] we do not concede that the lack of ease of knowing some rulings for some jurists or error in ijtihad contradicts readiness in the mentioned sense, because it may be due to conflicting evidences, presence of impediments, opposition of rational imagination, or resemblance of truth to falsehood, etc. [Second] we do not concede that any ruling for which there is no text or consensus is beyond the scope of ijtihad; the hadith of Mu'adh (may Allah be pleased with him) indicates this, as he relied on ijtihad by his opinion in what he did not find a text, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not say that there is no room for ijtihad. [Third] we do not concede that the word 'ilm has no indication of the specific readiness; indeed its meaning is a faculty (malaka) by which one is able to perceive the particulars of rulings, and applying 'ilm to it is common and widespread in usage, as in their definition of sciences as 'ilm such and such; indeed the investigators hold that what is meant by it is this faculty, and it is also called skill, not perception itself. And as they say: The aspect of similarity between knowledge and life is that both are bases of perception.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the definition of knowledge (ʿilm) in relation to fiqh rulings, specifically whether knowledge of rulings is collective (knowledge of all rulings) or individual (knowledge of each ruling). The author first explains the logical ratio between the collective whole (al-kull al-majmūʿī) and the individual whole (al-kull al-ifrādī) using examples: lifting a stone collectively vs. individually, food sufficiency, and beating a group. He then raises a question: since knowledge of rulings could be understood both collectively and individually, the author's distinction between the two seems contradictory. Some scholars responded that the comparison is valid because the collective is general (including all or some rulings) while the individual is specific (each ruling). The commentator rejects this, arguing that if the collective is general, then the proof of infinitude (tahārat al-aḥkām) only applies if all rulings are intended. The commentator then provides his own answer: the collective whole refers to all rulings (past and future), while the individual whole refers only to past rulings up to the mujtahid's time. This makes the comparison valid. The Arabic section addresses Ibn al-Ḥājib's objection that knowledge of rulings means readiness (tahayyuʾ). The author refutes this by arguing that remote readiness (tahayyuʾ baʿīd) is available even to non-jurists, while near readiness (tahayyuʾ qarīb) is undefined. The author also refutes Ibn al-Ḥājib's definition of readiness as the ability to know each ruling through ijtihad by collecting sources, causes, and conditions. The author responds with four arguments: (1) ignorance or error in some rulings does not negate readiness because of conflicting evidences or impediments; (2) no ruling is beyond ijtihad if there is no text or consensus, as shown by the hadith of Muʿādh; (3) the word ʿilm indicates a faculty (malaka) that allows perception of particulars, not readiness; this usage is common in defining sciences and in comparing knowledge to life as bases of perception. The passage thus defends the Hanafi position that fiqh knowledge is a faculty (malaka) enabling derivation of rulings, not mere readiness.

Key Terms
الكل المجموعي (al-kull al-majmūʿī): The collective whole: all rulings (past and future) taken together as a single entity
الكل الإفرادي (al-kull al-ifrādī): The individual whole: each individual ruling considered separately, here limited to past rulings
التَّهَيُّؤُ (al-tahayyuʾ): Readiness or preparedness to derive rulings through ijtihad
مَلَكَة (malaka): A stable faculty (like a skill) that enables perception of particulars

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position defended in this passage, what does the word 'ilm (knowledge) mean in the context of fiqh?
A) Readiness (tahayyu') to derive rulings
B) A faculty (malaka) that enables perception of particular rulings
C) Actual knowledge of all rulings (collective whole)
D) The sum of all transmitted texts and consensus

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of fiqh is a faculty (malaka) to derive rulings, not actual knowledge of infinite rulings nor an undefined readiness.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

8 min
Five Objections to Qiyas as an Asl Mutlaq and Their Hanafi Responses
Presents five objections against qiyas being an absolute source and their Hanafi rebuttals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the five objections against qiyas as an absolute source and articulate the Hanafi rebuttals for each objection.

Core Idea
Qiyas is not an absolute source like ijma, but remains a valid, necessary tool for derivation, manifesting rulings from primary texts.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary defends qiyas against five objections that deny it the status of an absolute source (asl mutlaq). The objections attack the very definition of 'asl', the role of causality, the necessity of hierarchy in division, the possibility of change without qiyas, and a comparison with ijma. The Hanafi responses carefully delineate the function of qiyas: it does not create rulings but manifests them from the Quran, Sunnah, and ijma. Understanding this debate sharpens your appreciation of how Hanafi usul positions qiyas within the hierarchy of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify each objection
List the five objections as presented in the passage. They concern: (1) definition of asl, (2) proximate vs distant cause, (3) necessity of prioritizing categories in division, (4) possibility of changing a ruling without qiyas, (5) dependency of ijma on proof.
2
Understand the basis of each objection
For each objection, determine what premise the objector is relying on. For example, the first objection argues that 'asl' must be independent; the fifth argues that since ijma needs a proof, it should not be considered an absolute source either.
3
Articulate the Hanafi response
Extract the Hanafi rebuttal from the text. For instance, to the first objection, the Hanafi says 'asl' is used ambiguously (tashkik); qiyas is still an asl in a certain sense. To the fifth, the response distinguishes ijma from qiyas: ijma adds definitiveness, qiyas does not.
4
Compare qiyas and ijma
Focus on the fifth objection and response. Note how the Hanafi argues that ijma, though needing a proof, provides an additional quality (qat'iyyah) that qiyas lacks. This highlights the epistemological difference.
5
Evaluate the strength of the Hanafi position
Consider whether the rebuttals are convincing. Note the use of tashkik (ambiguous usage) and the distinction between reality and knowledge.
