تشریح: واعترض علیہ بوجوہ :۔ یہ عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے یہاں سے شارخ نے پانچ اعتراض نقل کئے ہیں۔
And regarding the fourth [objection]: that if what is meant by 'establishment' is establishment according to reality such that qiyas is what establishes the ruling and fixes it in the branch form, then we do not concede the impossibility of change without it. And if what is meant is establishment according to our knowledge, then it does not require attributing the ruling in reality to qiyas so that it becomes a complete source for it. And regarding the fifth [objection]: after conceding what was mentioned, that ijma indeed needs a proof for its verification, not for its own indication of the ruling, for the one who uses it as evidence does not need to consider the proof and turn to it, unlike qiyas, for using it as evidence is not possible without considering one of the three sources and the cause deduced from them. And sometimes it is answered that ijma establishes an additional matter beyond what the proof establishes, namely the definitiveness of the ruling, contrary to qiyas, for it does not provide an addition, but rather may cause a deficiency, such that the ruling of the original is definitive and its ruling is speculative. Translation: Objections were made to it with several reasons: First: there is no meaning of 'absolute source' except that it is a foundation for something else, whether that other is a branch or not. Second: the proximate cause is more deserving even if it is an effect from a distant cause when applying the name 'cause' to it. Third: that some categories being more deserving in the meaning of the divided [term] is necessary for every division, so it would be necessary to separate the weak category. Fourth: that the change of a ruling from specific to general is not possible except with its establishment in another case, which is the meaning of absolute sources. Fifth: that ijma also needs a proof, so it is not appropriate for it to be an absolute source. And the answer to the first objection: we do not claim that being not a branch has any role in the concept of source, but rather the term 'source' is used ambiguously, and that source which is independent in the sense of originality and being a branch upon it, as in the example of a book, is stronger than this source which is in the meaning of being based on something else like qiyas, and the weaker is not included in the absolute source in the sense of being included in originality, and this is clear. And in any case, now, except that it is [like] a son to his father in existence, not in fatherhood, nor in the sense of originality for the child. So it is not among what we mentioned in anything. And the answer to the second objection: the proximate cause is effective in its effect and leads to it, and the effect of the distant cause is only that it is effective in the intermediary which is the proximate cause, not in its effect, so it will necessarily be more deserving and stronger than the distant cause including [originality] in the sense of originality for that effect, and what we are discussing, that qiyas is not the establisher of the branch's ruling, let alone being proximate so that it would be more deserving of originality, but rather it is a manifestation of the branch's ruling being attributed to the text and consensus. And the answer to the third objection: we do not concede the necessity of some categories being more deserving in every division, and how can it be imagined in the division of real essences into their species and individuals, like the division of animal into human and other. And if its necessity in every division is conceded, then we do not concede the necessity of pointing to it and alerting upon it. The extent in this chapter is that it is permissible. And the answer to the fourth objection: if what is meant by 'establishment' is establishment according to reality such that qiyas is what establishes the ruling and fixes it in the branch form, then we do not concede the impossibility of change without it. And if what is meant is according to our knowledge, then it does not require attributing the ruling in reality to qiyas so that it becomes a complete source for it. And the answer to the fifth objection: after conceding that ijma needs a proof for its verification, not for the indication of the ruling, then the one who uses it as evidence does not need to consider the proof and turn to it, unlike qiyas, for the one who uses it as evidence cannot do so without considering one of the three sources and the cause deduced from them. And sometimes it is answered that ijma establishes an additional matter beyond what the proof establishes, namely the definitiveness of the ruling, contrary to qiyas, for it does not provide an addition, but rather sometimes causes a deficiency, such that the ruling of the original is definitive and its ruling is speculative. Objections on calling qiyas a deficient source. Explanation: 'And it was objected with reasons': this is the fifth part of the phrase; from here the commentator narrated five objections.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary presents five objections to the claim that qiyas (analogical reasoning) qualifies as an 'asl mutlaq' (absolute source) of law, followed by detailed Hanafi responses. The objections target the definition of 'asl', the role of proximate and distant causes, the necessity of prioritizing certain categories in division, the possibility of changing a ruling without qiyas, and a comparison with ijma (consensus). The Hanafi responses defend qiyas by clarifying its function: qiyas does not create the ruling but manifests it from the primary sources (text and consensus). The commentary (sharh) expands on the original matn, systematically refuting each objection. This is a classical dispute between Hanafis and opponents who deny qiyas the status of an independent source, likely referring to Zahiri or other anti-qiyas schools. The passage reinforces the Hanafi view that qiyas, while not definitive like ijma, is a valid and necessary tool for deriving rulings from revelation.

Key Terms
اصل مطلق (asl mutlaq): An absolute source that itself establishes a ruling independently without needing another source.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning to extend a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a common effective cause (illah).
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of the mujtahidun on a ruling. In this passage, it is compared to qiyas regarding its reliance on a proof.
تشکیک (tashkik): Ambiguous usage; a term that applies to multiple instances with varying degrees of strength.
قطعية (qat'iyyah): Definitiveness; a ruling that is certain and beyond doubt.
ظن (zann): Speculative; a ruling based on preponderant probability but not certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fifth objection and response in this passage, how does qiyas differ from ijma?
A) Qiyas definitively establishes a ruling, while ijma does not.
B) Ijma adds definitiveness to a ruling beyond what the proof provides, while qiyas does not.
C) Qiyas is independent of any proof, while ijma requires a proof.
D) Ijma is weaker than qiyas because it needs a proof.

Key Takeaway
The status of qiyas as an asl mutlaq is contested, but Hanafis affirm its validity and necessity by clarifying its derivative and manifestive role, distinguishing it from the definitiveness of ijma.
